File: hooks/check-aws-ttl.sh
================
#!/bin/bash
# Claude Code PreToolUse hook: AWS credential lifecycle management
#
# Checks credential TTL before every Bash tool call and handles refresh
# through the best available method for the current environment.
#
# States handled:
#   - Credentials valid (TTL > 5min)        → pass through (exit 0)
#   - Credentials expiring soon (TTL < 5min) → attempt proactive refresh
#   - Credentials expired (TTL <= 0)         → block + trigger refresh
#   - No credentials file                    → block + instruct user
#   - No awsmyid_session_expiration field    → pass through (not our credentials)
#
# Refresh strategies (tried in order):
#   tmux   → tmux display-popup (stays in same window, blocks until done)
#   macOS  → silent refresh (cookies valid?) → iTerm2 tab → Terminal.app tab
#   Linux  → silent refresh (cookies valid?) → instruct user
#
# Edge cases:
#   - Silent refresh timeout (15s) prevents hanging if password is needed
#   - tmux popup is synchronous — Claude waits, then retries automatically
#   - Terminal tabs are async — hook blocks so Claude knows to retry later
#   - Credentials file missing entirely → treated as "not managed by us"
#   - Profile missing from credentials → pass through

set -uo pipefail

# --- Configuration ----------------------------------------------------------

AWS_CREDS_FILE="${HOME}/.aws/credentials"
AWS_PROFILE_NAME="twdc-bedrock-central"
TTL_WARNING=300    # 5 minutes — proactive refresh threshold
TTL_CRITICAL=60    # 1 minute — urgent, definitely block
CA_CMD="${HOME}/.local/bin/ca"
SILENT_TIMEOUT=15  # seconds to wait for non-interactive refresh
REFRESH_FLAG="${HOME}/.claude/.aws-refresh-pending"
REFRESH_FLAG_TTL=120  # seconds before flag is considered stale

# --- Helpers ----------------------------------------------------------------

get_remaining_seconds() {
    [[ -f "$AWS_CREDS_FILE" ]] || { echo "nofile"; return; }

    # Check if our profile exists at all
    if ! grep -q "^\[${AWS_PROFILE_NAME}\]" "$AWS_CREDS_FILE" 2>/dev/null; then
        echo "noprofile"
        return
    fi

    local expiration
    expiration=$(awk -v profile="[$AWS_PROFILE_NAME]" '
        $0 == profile { found=1; next }
        /^\[/ { found=0 }
        found && /awsmyid_session_expiration/ { gsub(/[^0-9]/, "", $NF); print $NF }
    ' "$AWS_CREDS_FILE" 2>/dev/null)

    if [[ -z "$expiration" ]] || ! [[ "$expiration" =~ ^[0-9]+$ ]]; then
        echo "noexpiry"
        return
    fi

    echo $(( expiration - $(date +%s) ))
}

format_remaining() {
    local secs=$1
    if [[ "$secs" -le 0 ]]; then
        echo "EXPIRED"
    elif [[ "$secs" -lt 60 ]]; then
        echo "${secs}s"
    elif [[ "$secs" -lt 3600 ]]; then
        echo "$(( secs / 60 ))m"
    else
        local h=$(( secs / 3600 )) m=$(( (secs % 3600) / 60 ))
        [[ "$m" -gt 0 ]] && echo "${h}h${m}m" || echo "${h}h"
    fi
}

# --- Refresh flag (prevents opening multiple terminal tabs) -----------------

# Check if a refresh terminal tab was recently opened
is_refresh_pending() {
    [[ -f "$REFRESH_FLAG" ]] || return 1

    local flag_ts
    flag_ts=$(cat "$REFRESH_FLAG" 2>/dev/null) || return 1
    [[ "$flag_ts" =~ ^[0-9]+$ ]] || return 1

    local now age
    now=$(date +%s)
    age=$(( now - flag_ts ))

    # Flag is stale — treat as no pending refresh
    [[ "$age" -lt "$REFRESH_FLAG_TTL" ]]
}

set_refresh_pending() {
    mkdir -p "$(dirname "$REFRESH_FLAG")"
    date +%s > "$REFRESH_FLAG" 2>/dev/null
}

clear_refresh_pending() {
    rm -f "$REFRESH_FLAG" 2>/dev/null
}

# --- Refresh strategies -----------------------------------------------------

# tmux popup — synchronous, best UX
refresh_tmux() {
    tmux display-popup \
        -E \
        -w 80 -h 20 \
        -T " AWS Credential Refresh " \
        "$CA_CMD refresh" 2>/dev/null
}

# Silent refresh — non-interactive, works when MyID session cookies are valid
# Returns 0 if credentials are now valid, 1 otherwise
refresh_silent() {
    local pid
    "$CA_CMD" refresh </dev/null &>/dev/null &
    pid=$!

    local elapsed=0
    while kill -0 "$pid" 2>/dev/null && [[ $elapsed -lt $SILENT_TIMEOUT ]]; do
        sleep 1
        elapsed=$((elapsed + 1))
    done

    if kill -0 "$pid" 2>/dev/null; then
        # Still running — waiting for interactive input. Kill it.
        kill "$pid" 2>/dev/null
        wait "$pid" 2>/dev/null
        return 1
    fi

    wait "$pid" 2>/dev/null
    local remaining
    remaining=$(get_remaining_seconds)
    [[ "$remaining" =~ ^-?[0-9]+$ ]] && [[ "$remaining" -gt "$TTL_WARNING" ]]
}

# macOS: open a new tab in the detected terminal emulator
refresh_terminal_tab() {
    # Build a command that shows context before running refresh
    local refresh_cmd
    refresh_cmd="echo ''; echo '========================================'; echo '  AWS Credential Refresh for Claude Code'; echo '========================================'; echo ''; echo 'Claude Code needs valid AWS credentials to'; echo 'communicate with Bedrock. Please authenticate'; echo 'below, then return to your Claude session.'; echo ''; ${CA_CMD} refresh"

    case "${TERM_PROGRAM:-}" in
        iTerm.app)
            osascript -e "
                tell application \"iTerm2\"
                    tell current window
                        create tab with default profile
                        tell current session of current tab
                            write text \"${refresh_cmd}\"
                        end tell
                    end tell
                end tell
            " 2>/dev/null
            ;;
        Apple_Terminal)
            osascript -e "
                tell application \"Terminal\"
                    activate
                    do script \"${refresh_cmd}\"
                end tell
            " 2>/dev/null
            ;;
        vscode)
            # VS Code integrated terminal — can't easily open a new tab
            # via osascript, fall through to manual instructions
            return 1
            ;;
        *)
            # Unknown terminal on macOS — try Terminal.app as fallback
            if [[ "$(uname)" == "Darwin" ]]; then
                osascript -e "
                    tell application \"Terminal\"
                        activate
                        do script \"${refresh_cmd}\"
                    end tell
                " 2>/dev/null
            else
                return 1
            fi
            ;;
    esac
}

# --- Main -------------------------------------------------------------------

remaining=$(get_remaining_seconds)

# Not our credentials to manage — pass through
case "$remaining" in
    nofile|noprofile|noexpiry)
        exit 0
        ;;
esac

# Credentials are healthy — clear any pending refresh flag and pass through
if [[ "$remaining" -gt "$TTL_WARNING" ]]; then
    clear_refresh_pending
    exit 0
fi

# Build status message
if [[ "$remaining" -le 0 ]]; then
    status_msg="AWS credentials EXPIRED — refresh required"
else
    status_msg="AWS credentials expire in $(format_remaining "$remaining")"
fi

# --- tmux environment -------------------------------------------------------

if [[ -n "${TMUX:-}" ]]; then
    echo "$status_msg — opening refresh popup..." >&2
    if refresh_tmux; then
        remaining=$(get_remaining_seconds)
        if [[ "$remaining" =~ ^[0-9]+$ ]] && [[ "$remaining" -gt "$TTL_WARNING" ]]; then
            clear_refresh_pending
            echo "Credentials refreshed. Continuing." >&2
            exit 0
        fi
    fi
    echo "Refresh did not complete. Run 'ca refresh' in a tmux pane." >&2
    exit 1
fi

# --- Non-tmux: try silent first, then terminal tab --------------------------

echo "$status_msg — attempting silent refresh..." >&2
if refresh_silent; then
    clear_refresh_pending
    echo "Credentials refreshed (session cookies were valid). Continuing." >&2
    exit 0
fi

# Silent failed — try opening a terminal tab (macOS only)
if [[ "$(uname)" == "Darwin" ]]; then
    if is_refresh_pending; then
        # A refresh tab was already opened recently — don't open another
        echo "" >&2
        echo ">>> A refresh tab is already open. Authenticate there, then retry. <<<" >&2
        exit 1
    fi

    echo "Interactive login required — opening new terminal tab..." >&2
    if refresh_terminal_tab; then
        set_refresh_pending
        echo "" >&2
        echo ">>> Authenticate in the new tab, then retry this operation. <<<" >&2
        exit 1
    fi
fi

# --- Final fallback ---------------------------------------------------------

echo "" >&2
echo ">>> Open another terminal and run: ca refresh <<<" >&2
exit 1

File: hooks/ensure-mlflow.sh

#!/usr/bin/env bash
# ensure-mlflow.sh — SessionStart hook to guarantee MLflow server is running

MLFLOW_HOST="127.0.0.1"
MLFLOW_PORT="5001"
MLFLOW_URL="http://${MLFLOW_HOST}:${MLFLOW_PORT}/health"
MLFLOW_DB="sqlite:////Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db"

# Check if MLflow is already running
if curl -sf --max-time 2 "$MLFLOW_URL" > /dev/null 2>&1; then
  echo "MLflow server already running on port ${MLFLOW_PORT}"
  exit 0
fi

# Not running — start it in the background
echo "Starting MLflow server on port ${MLFLOW_PORT}..."
nohup mlflow server \
  --host "$MLFLOW_HOST" \
  --port "$MLFLOW_PORT" \
  --backend-store-uri "$MLFLOW_DB" \
  > /dev/null 2>&1 &

# Wait up to 5 seconds for it to come up
for i in 1 2 3 4 5; do
  sleep 1
  if curl -sf --max-time 1 "$MLFLOW_URL" > /dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "MLflow server started successfully on port ${MLFLOW_PORT}"
    exit 0
  fi
done

echo "WARNING: MLflow server did not respond within 5 seconds on port ${MLFLOW_PORT}"
exit 0

File: hooks/git-auto-pull.sh

#!/usr/bin/env bash
# git-auto-pull.sh — SessionStart hook to auto-pull updates from remote claude-settings repo
# Conservative pull-only approach: never modifies local uncommitted changes

CLAUDE_DIR="$HOME/.claude"
REMOTE_HOST="github.twdcgrid.net"
REPO_NAME="sameul-nasir/claude-settings"

# Change to .claude directory
cd "$CLAUDE_DIR" || {
  echo "WARNING: Could not access ~/.claude directory for auto-pull"
  exit 0
}

# Verify this is a git repository
if [ ! -d ".git" ]; then
  echo "WARNING: ~/.claude is not a git repository, skipping auto-pull"
  exit 0
fi

# Check if working tree is clean (conservative approach)
if [ -n "$(git status --porcelain)" ]; then
  echo "Working tree has uncommitted changes, skipping auto-pull"
  echo "Run 'cd ~/.claude && git status' to see changes"
  exit 0
fi

# Verify gh auth is working for the correct hostname
if ! gh auth status --hostname "$REMOTE_HOST" >/dev/null 2>&1; then
  echo "WARNING: gh auth not configured for $REMOTE_HOST, skipping auto-pull"
  echo "Run 'gh auth login --hostname $REMOTE_HOST' to configure authentication"
  exit 0
fi

# Check if current branch tracks a remote
current_branch=$(git branch --show-current)
if [ -z "$current_branch" ]; then
  echo "WARNING: Not on a branch (detached HEAD), skipping auto-pull"
  exit 0
fi

# Check if branch has upstream tracking
if ! git config --get "branch.$current_branch.remote" >/dev/null 2>&1; then
  echo "WARNING: Branch '$current_branch' does not track a remote, skipping auto-pull"
  exit 0
fi

# Attempt to pull with timeout
echo "Checking for updates from $REMOTE_HOST/$REPO_NAME..."

# Set git timeout and attempt pull
export GIT_SSH_COMMAND="ssh -o ConnectTimeout=5 -o BatchMode=yes"
if timeout 5 git pull --ff-only origin "$current_branch" 2>/dev/null; then
  # Check if anything was actually pulled
  if git diff --quiet HEAD@{1} HEAD 2>/dev/null; then
    echo "Already up to date with remote"
  else
    commit_count=$(git rev-list --count HEAD@{1}..HEAD 2>/dev/null || echo "unknown")
    echo "Pulled $commit_count commit(s) from $REMOTE_HOST/$REPO_NAME"
  fi
else
  echo "Auto-pull failed or timed out, continuing with local settings"
  echo "You can manually sync with: cd ~/.claude && git pull"
fi

# Always exit successfully to not block session startup
exit 0

File: hooks/save-compact-state.py
================
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""PreCompact hook: save working state before context compaction.

Parses the session transcript to extract recent user messages and files
being worked on, writes them to ~/.claude/.compact-state.md so the
SessionStart hook can reload context after compaction.
"""

import json
import os
import sys
from datetime import datetime

COMPACT_STATE_PATH = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/.compact-state.md")
MAX_USER_MESSAGES = 5
MAX_FILES = 15


def main():
    # Read hook input from stdin
    try:
        data = json.load(sys.stdin)
    except (json.JSONDecodeError, EOFError):
        return

    transcript_path = data.get("transcript_path", "")
    if not transcript_path or not os.path.exists(transcript_path):
        return

    user_messages = []
    files_touched = set()

    try:
        with open(transcript_path) as f:
            for line in f:
                try:
                    entry = json.loads(line)
                except json.JSONDecodeError:
                    continue

                # Collect user messages
                if entry.get("type") == "user":
                    content = entry.get("message", {}).get("content", "")
                    if isinstance(content, list):
                        content = " ".join(
                            c.get("text", "") for c in content if isinstance(c, dict)
                        )
                    text = content.strip()
                    if text:
                        user_messages.append(text[:300])

                # Collect files from assistant tool use
                if entry.get("type") == "assistant":
                    for block in entry.get("message", {}).get("content", []):
                        if not isinstance(block, dict):
                            continue
                        if block.get("type") == "tool_use":
                            fp = block.get("input", {}).get("file_path", "")
                            if fp:
                                files_touched.add(fp)
    except (OSError, IOError):
        return

    if not user_messages:
        return

    # Build the state file
    now = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M")
    recent_messages = user_messages[-MAX_USER_MESSAGES:]
    recent_files = sorted(files_touched)[-MAX_FILES:]

    lines = [
        f"# Compact State (auto-saved {now})",
        "",
        "Context was compacted. This file preserves what was being worked on.",
        "",
        "## Recent User Requests",
    ]
    for msg in recent_messages:
        # Collapse newlines for readability
        lines.append(f"- {msg.replace(chr(10), ' ')}")

    if recent_files:
        lines.append("")
        lines.append("## Files Being Worked On")
        for fp in recent_files:
            lines.append(f"- `{fp}`")

    lines.append("")

    try:
        with open(COMPACT_STATE_PATH, "w") as f:
            f.write("\n".join(lines))
    except OSError:
        pass


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

================
File: hooks/sync-traces.sh
================
#!/usr/bin/env bash
# SessionStart hook: auto-sync traces.csv if it's been modified since last sync.
# Compares CSV mtime against a marker file. Runs sync_traces.py if CSV is newer.

CSV="$HOME/.claude/traces.csv"
MARKER="$HOME/.claude/.traces-last-sync"
SYNC_SCRIPT="$HOME/sync_traces.py"

# Nothing to sync if CSV doesn't exist
[ -f "$CSV" ] || exit 0

# If marker doesn't exist, this is the first sync — create it and sync
if [ ! -f "$MARKER" ]; then
    python3 "$SYNC_SCRIPT" 2>&1
    touch "$MARKER"
    exit 0
fi

# Compare mtimes: sync only if CSV is newer than marker
if [ "$CSV" -nt "$MARKER" ]; then
    python3 "$SYNC_SCRIPT" 2>&1
    touch "$MARKER"
fi

# GitHub Multi-Account Setup

Reference for managing two GitHub accounts on the same machine.

---

## Accounts

| Component | TWDC (`github.twdcgrid.net`) | Personal (`github.com`) |
|-----------|------------------------------|------------------------|
| **SSH Key** | `~/.ssh/id_rsa` | `~/.ssh/id_ed25519` |
| **gh auth** | `sameul-nasir` (SSH, keyring) | `Sameulnsr1` (SSH, keyring) |
| **Git identity** | Global: `Sameul Nasir <sameul.nasir@disney.com>` | Conditional: `Sameulnsr1 <sameulnasir28@gmail.com>` (repos under `~/personal/`) |

---

## How SSH Routing Works

`~/.ssh/config` maps each hostname to the correct key with `IdentitiesOnly yes`. No manual switching needed for `git push`/`pull` — the remote URL determines which key is used automatically.

- `git@github.twdcgrid.net:...` → uses `~/.ssh/id_rsa`
- `git@github.com:...` → uses `~/.ssh/id_ed25519`

## How `gh` CLI Routing Works

`gh` detects the hostname from the repo's remote URL when inside a repo directory. For non-repo commands or ambiguous contexts, use `--hostname` flag or `gh auth switch`.

## Conditional Gitconfig

Repos under `~/personal/` automatically use personal identity via `includeIf` in `~/.gitconfig`:

```
[includeIf "gitdir:~/personal/"]
    path = ~/.gitconfig-personal
```

`~/.gitconfig-personal` sets `user.name = Sameulnsr1` and `user.email = sameulnasir28@gmail.com`.

For repos outside `~/personal/` that should use personal identity (e.g., `~/claude-settings-public`), set repo-local config:

```bash
cd <repo>
git config user.name "Sameulnsr1"
git config user.email "sameulnasir28@gmail.com"
```

---

## Quick Reference Commands

```bash
# See all authenticated accounts
gh auth status

# Switch active gh account
gh auth switch --hostname github.twdcgrid.net   # Switch to TWDC
gh auth switch --hostname github.com              # Switch to personal

# Test SSH connectivity
ssh -T git@github.twdcgrid.net                   # Should greet sameul-nasir
ssh -T git@github.com                            # Should greet Sameulnsr1

# Check commit identity for current repo
cd <repo> && git config user.email

# Check which GitHub a repo points to
git remote -v
```

---

## Common Pitfalls

- **2026-02-21** [claude-code]: Committing with wrong email — repos outside `~/personal/` inherit the global Disney email. Always set repo-local identity for personal repos not under `~/personal/`.
- **2026-02-21** [claude-code]: `gh repo create` targeting wrong host — always specify `--hostname` or check `gh auth status` first to confirm which account is active.
- **2026-02-21** [claude-code]: Forgetting `IdentitiesOnly yes` in SSH config — without it, the SSH agent may offer the wrong key first.

# Jira — Setup & Tools

---

## Curl Workflow

Core curl-vs-MCP rule and JQL encoding patterns auto-load from `rules/jira-workflow.md`.

### Create Issue

```bash
curl -s --max-time 15 -X POST \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $JIRA_TOKEN" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  "https://jira.disney.com/rest/api/2/issue" \
  -d '{
    "fields": {
      "project": {"key": "QMDS"},
      "issuetype": {"id": "10206"},
      "summary": "Title here",
      "description": "Jira wiki markup description",
      "customfield_10101": "EPIC-KEY"
    }
  }'
```

### Add Issue to Sprint

```bash
curl -s --max-time 10 -X POST \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $JIRA_TOKEN" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  "https://jira.disney.com/rest/agile/1.0/sprint/<SPRINT_ID>/issue" \
  -d '{"issues": ["PROJ-123"]}'
```

### Update Issue Fields

```bash
curl -s --max-time 10 -X PUT \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $JIRA_TOKEN" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  "https://jira.disney.com/rest/api/2/issue/PROJ-123" \
  -d '{"fields": {"customfield_10106": 1}}'
```

---

## Custom Field Reference

| Field | Custom Field ID | Notes |
|-------|----------------|-------|
| Epic Link | `customfield_10101` | Key of parent Epic (e.g., `DSACQ-15043`) |
| Epic Name | `customfield_10103` | Often `null` — resolve via Epic Link if empty |
| Sprint | `customfield_10105` | List of sprint strings; parse `name=` from `state=ACTIVE` entry |
| Story Points | `customfield_10106` | Numeric; may be `null` for unestimated tickets |

**Active statuses** (for finding in-progress work):
`"Open", "In Progress", "In Review", "In Development", "Code Review", "Ready for QA", "In QA", "To Do", "Blocked", "Reopened", "Ready for Development"`

**Completed statuses** (for finding done work):

## Docker / MCP Server Setup

- **Transport**: SSE on `http://localhost:3000/sse` (configured in `~/.claude.json` under `mcpServers`)
- **Source**: `/Users/sameul.nasir/audience-jira-mcp-server/`
- **Server**: `https://jira.disney.com`
- **Run**: `docker run -d -p 3000:3000 -e JIRA_TOKEN="<token>" -e JIRA_URL="https://jira.disney.com" -e MCP_TRANSPORT=sse -e MCP_PORT=3000 audience-jira-mcp-server`
- **Token refresh**: `https://jira.disney.com/secure/ViewProfile.jspa` → Personal Access Tokens
- **Startup note**: Container validates token at startup (can take 30s+ with retries)
- The MCP container is kept for token storage and health check infrastructure only

## Health Check Auto-Healing

- **SSE liveness** (`health-check.py`): If SSE endpoint unresponsive, extracts token and auto-restarts. Polls up to 30s. Checks HTTP status code (not curl exit code) since SSE streams indefinitely.
- **Leak patch** (`health-check.py`): Verifies `_read_stream_writers.pop()` exists in local and container `mcp/server/sse.py`. Verification-only — no runtime patching. Fix is baked into the Docker image.

## Token Management

- **Persistent store**: `~/.atlassian-tokens.env` (chmod 600, NOT in git). Contains `JIRA_TOKEN=...` and `CONFLUENCE_TOKEN=...`.
- **Validation script**: `~/.claude/scripts/validate-atlassian-token.py --token <TOKEN> [--service jira|confluence|auto] [--apply]`
  - `--service auto` (default): tries both endpoints, reports which works
  - `--apply`: writes to token file + restarts Jira container / updates Confluence .env
  - Checks expiry via `/rest/pat/latest/tokens` API
- **Skill**: `/update-atlassian-token` — interactive workflow for token updates
- **Fallback chain**: Docker container env var → `~/.atlassian-tokens.env` → ask user
- **Token refresh URLs**:
  - Jira: `https://jira.disney.com/secure/ViewProfile.jspa` → Personal Access Tokens
  - Confluence: `https://confluence.disney.com/plugins/personalaccesstokens/usertokens.action`

## Known Issues

See `domain/known-issues.md` for all Jira-related issues and workarounds (SSE leak, rank_issues deserialization, health check false-negatives).

# MLflow — Setup & Tools

---

## Server

- **Port**: 5001 (port 5000 blocked by macOS AirPlay Receiver)
- **Start command**: `mlflow server --host 127.0.0.1 --port 5001 --backend-store-uri sqlite:////Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db &`
- **Critical**: Use 4 slashes for absolute SQLite path (`sqlite:////path`). Three slashes = relative path, which silently creates a new DB in the working directory.
- **Critical**: Always use `--backend-store-uri`. Without it, MLflow defaults to file-based `./mlruns`, which silently loses traces.
- **Auto-start**: `~/.claude/hooks/ensure-mlflow.sh` (SessionStart hook) checks health and starts MLflow if not running. No manual start needed.
- **Status line**: `~/.claude/statusline.sh` shows `mlf OK` or `mlf DOWN` via health check on `http://127.0.0.1:5001/health`.

## MCP Server

- Config lives in `~/.claude.json` under the `mcpServers` key (NOT `~/.claude/mcp.json` — that file is not read by Claude Code).
- Global env vars (`MLFLOW_TRACKING_URI`, `MLFLOW_CLAUDE_TRACING_ENABLED`) must be in `settings.json` under the `env` key (NOT `environment` — that key is ignored by Claude Code).
- Tracking URI: `http://127.0.0.1:5001`
- Requires session restart after config changes.

## Cost Tracking

- **Stop hook**: `~/.claude/hooks/capture-cost.py` — parses transcript JSONL on session end, sums token usage (main + subagent transcripts), computes USD cost from Bedrock pricing, writes to CSV and tags MLflow trace.
- **CSV log**: `~/.claude/cost-log.csv` — columns: `date, session_id, cost_usd, input_tokens, output_tokens, cache_read, cache_write, model`
- **Pricing**: Configurable at top of `capture-cost.py` (Opus, Sonnet, Haiku rates per 1M tokens).
- **Note**: Stop hook payload does not include cost/token fields — transcript parsing is the workaround. See known issues.

## Trace Provenance (Source System Separation)

**Purpose**: Distinguish Cortex Code traces from Claude Code traces to prevent contamination in analysis workflows.

- **Auto-detection**: `capture-cost.py` detects source system via `CORTEX_SESSION_ID` environment variable
- **Source tags**: All traces automatically tagged with:
  - `system_source`: `"cortex_code"` or `"claude_code"`
  - `tool_context`: `"mcp_bash_snowflake_local"` vs `"web_claude_tools"`  
  - `session_type`: `"cli_interactive"` vs `"web_chat"`
- **CSV columns**: Source tags appear as read-only columns in `~/.claude/traces.csv`
- **Analysis filtering**: Memory refresh scripts and failure pattern analysis respect source boundaries
- **Health monitoring**: `~/.claude/scripts/health-check.py` includes trace provenance verification

**Why this matters**: Mixing traces from different systems corrupts failure pattern analysis, cost attribution, and memory systems. Each system has different tool sets, interaction models, and failure modes.

## Trace Tagging (CSV Workflow)

Primary method for tagging traces — edit a CSV, sync back to SQLite:

1. `python3 ~/export_traces.py` → writes `~/.claude/traces.csv`
2. Edit CSV (spreadsheet or ask Claude in-session)
3. `python3 ~/sync_traces.py` → writes changed tags back to SQLite, auto-refreshes memory files
4. **Auto-sync hook**: `~/.claude/hooks/sync-traces.sh` (SessionStart) detects CSV edits and syncs automatically on next session start.

## Scripts

| Script | Purpose | Key Flags |
|--------|---------|-----------|
| `~/export_traces.py` | Export traces from SQLite to CSV (denormalized) | `--days N` (30), `--all`, `--output PATH` |
| `~/sync_traces.py` | Sync edited CSV tags back to SQLite | `--dry-run`, `--input PATH` |
| `~/tag_traces.py` | Interactive CLI to tag, bookmark, and view traces | `--save`, `--known-issue`, `--view <id>`, `--full-response`, `--saved-only`, `--category <name>` |
| `~/.claude/scripts/cortex_to_mlflow_converter.py` | Convert Cortex conversations to MLflow traces (idempotent — skips already-imported sessions) | `--dry-run`, `--cortex-dir PATH`, `--mlflow-db PATH` |
| `~/refresh_failure_patterns.py` | Rebuild `domain/failure-patterns.md` (groups by category, uses prevention_rule verbatim) | `--max N` (200), `--days N` (30) |
| `~/refresh_saved_traces.py` | Rebuild `domain/saved-traces.md` from bookmarked traces | `--max N` (200), `--days N` (90) |
| `~/refresh_known_issues.py` | Rebuild `domain/known-issues.md` from traces + manual JSON | `--max N` (200), `--days N` (90) |

- Config: `~/.mlflow_failure_modes.json`
- Manual known issues: `~/.claude/known_issues_manual.json`
- Full workflow reference: `~/.claude/mlflow/README.md`

## Trace Tagging & Learning Systems

Three systems learn from past sessions via MLflow traces. Each tracks a different type of issue:

| System | What it tracks | Who's at fault | Tag command (primary) | Tag command (secondary) |
|--------|---------------|----------------|----------------------|------------------------|
| **Failure Patterns** | Mistakes Claude made (hallucination, wrong tool, didn't follow instructions) | Claude | Edit `~/.claude/traces.csv` → `python3 ~/sync_traces.py` | `python3 ~/tag_traces.py` (terminal) |
| **Saved Traces** | Good sessions worth distilling into skills | N/A | Edit `~/.claude/traces.csv` → `python3 ~/sync_traces.py` | `python3 ~/tag_traces.py --save` (terminal) |
| **Known Issues (trace)** | Environment/tool/config problems discovered in a session | Environment | `python3 ~/tag_traces.py --known-issue` | N/A |
| **Known Issues (manual)** | Environment/tool/config problems recorded directly | Environment | "add this as a known issue" | N/A |

## In-Session Trace Editing

Claude can read and edit `~/.claude/traces.csv` during any session — no external tools needed.

**Reading traces**: When the user asks to see traces ("show me my traces", "what did my last session cost"), read `~/.claude/traces.csv` and present a summary table.

**Editing traces**: When the user says things like:
- "tag that as a failure" → update the `failure_mode` column
- "add that into the description" → update the `description` column
- "mark that as high severity" → update the `severity` column
- "the prevention rule should be..." → update the `prevention_rule` column
- "save that trace for later" → set `save` to `true`

Use a Python one-liner via Bash to edit the CSV safely (proper quoting/escaping):

```python
python3 -c "
import csv, sys
rows = list(csv.reader(open('$CSV')))
header = rows[0]
col_idx = header.index('$COLUMN')
for i, row in enumerate(rows[1:], 1):
    if row[0].startswith('$TRACE_ID'):
        row[col_idx] = '$VALUE'
        break
writer = csv.writer(open('$CSV', 'w', newline=''))
writer.writerows(rows)
"
```

**Syncing**: When the user says "sync traces" or after finishing a batch of edits, run `python3 ~/sync_traces.py`.

**Prevention rule drafting**: Standards auto-load from `rules/mlflow.md`. See that file for the Specific/Actionable/Testable/Trigger criteria.

## Saved Traces & Skill Distillation

Bookmark good sessions for later distillation into skill files using `tag_traces.py --save`.

**Workflow:**
1. **Bookmark**: `python3 ~/tag_traces.py --save` — pick a trace, assign a category, mark as saved
2. **Review candidates**: Read `~/.claude/memory/domain/saved-traces.md` to see what's accumulated per domain
3. **Inspect a trace**: `python3 ~/tag_traces.py --view <trace_id>` to read the full conversation (add `--full-response` to skip truncation)
4. **Distill**: Extract patterns/templates from the trace into the relevant skill file
5. **Filter**: `--saved-only` shows only bookmarked traces; `--category <name>` filters by category

The saved traces index auto-refreshes every time a trace is bookmarked. To manually refresh: `python3 ~/refresh_saved_traces.py`

# Data Analysis Patterns

## Query Strategy

1. **Semantic views first**: Before complex business queries, always check `cortex semantic-views search "<topic>"` for curated definitions.
2. **Progressive complexity**: Start with simple exploration queries, then build complexity based on results.
3. **Result validation**: For suspicious analysis results (e.g., mid-week data for weekly analysis), always investigate and explain discrepancies.
4. **Truncated results investigation**: If grep/search shows `"... [X lines truncated] ..."`, use filters (`head_limit`, `glob`, `path`) to get complete data.

## Data Quality Checks

1. **Freshness awareness**: For time-sensitive analysis, check data freshness with `cortex search docs "data freshness"` patterns.
2. **Completeness validation**: When analysis results seem incomplete, validate data completeness before drawing conclusions.
3. **Cross-validation**: For critical metrics, cross-validate against multiple data sources or time periods.

## Result Interpretation

1. **Business context**: Always provide business-focused interpretation of technical results.
2. **Anomaly explanation**: When data shows unexpected patterns, investigate root causes before reporting.
3. **Confidence indicators**: Clearly indicate when results are preliminary, estimated, or require validation.

## Performance Optimization

1. **Query optimization**: For large datasets, suggest appropriate warehouse sizing or query patterns.
2. **Incremental approaches**: Break large analysis into manageable chunks when possible.
3. **Resource awareness**: Monitor query costs and execution time for complex analyses.

# Memory Management (Cortex Code)

## Failure Pattern Prevention

1. **Show before edit**: Always draft content and show user for review before editing memory files, failure patterns, or rules. Never edit first and explain after.
2. **Real-time capture**: When repeating known failure patterns, update failure-patterns.md immediately without waiting for user reminder.
3. **Format verification**: Read existing patterns/entries before writing new ones to match structure and format.
4. **Path verification**: Use bash commands to verify file locations before updating rules about paths. Don't assume based on logic alone.
5. **Documentation sync**: When creating new rule files or directories, immediately update memory index and relevant documentation.

## Memory System Integration

1. **Dual environment awareness**: Remember that memory system spans both Claude Code (~/.claude/) and Cortex Code (~/.snowflake/cortex/).
2. **Cross-system commits**: Changes to ~/.claude/memory/ or ~/.claude/rules/ must be committed via git even when working from Cortex Code.
3. **Source tagging**: All new memory entries must include [cortex-code] source tags when created from Cortex environment.

## Review Process

1. **Always get approval**: For memory file edits, rule changes, or failure pattern updates - show proposed content first.
2. **Structured format**: Follow existing patterns for consistency across all memory and rule files.
3. **Immediate action**: Don't defer memory updates or commits - handle immediately when identified.

# Semantic Models & Views

## Pre-Implementation Research

1. **Always check product docs**: Before working with semantic views/models, MANDATORY to use `snowflake_product_docs` to understand current concepts and API.
2. **Understand the distinction**: 
   - Semantic Model = YAML annotation layer over tables (stage files)  
   - Semantic View = Snowflake object created from semantic model
3. **Never assume knowledge**: Snowflake semantic concepts evolve rapidly. Always verify against current documentation.

## Creation & Validation

1. **YAML validation**: Always use `cortex reflect <file.yaml>` to validate semantic model YAML before deployment.
2. **Target schema specification**: Use `--target-schema DB.SCHEMA` flag when validating to ensure proper compilation.
3. **Discovery before creation**: Search for existing semantic views with `cortex semantic-views search "<topic>"` before creating new ones.

## Usage Patterns

1. **Business analytics priority**: For questions about revenue, customers, KPIs, always check semantic views FIRST before writing raw SQL.
2. **Semantic view description**: Use `cortex semantic-views describe <view>` to understand dimensions, facts, and metrics before querying.
3. **Analyst integration**: Use `cortex analyst query "<question>" --view=<view>` for natural language queries against semantic views.

## Troubleshooting

1. **Object does not exist errors**: When working with semantic views, transform YAML to SQL-ready markdown first using semantic-view-transform agent.
2. **Physical table mapping**: Always ensure physical table names are prominently displayed in documentation to prevent SQL generation errors.

# Snowflake Workflows

## Connection Management

1. **Always use active connection**: Check current connection with `cortex connections list` and use DISNEYSTREAMING unless user specifies otherwise.
2. **Connection validation**: Before complex operations, validate connection with a simple query like `SELECT CURRENT_ACCOUNT()`.
3. **Cross-connection work**: When user specifies different connection, remember and use it for entire session context.

## SQL Best Practices

1. **Always validate before executing**: Use `only_compile=true` for complex queries unless user explicitly wants execution.
2. **Check semantic views first**: Before writing business analytics SQL (revenue, customers, metrics), always search for semantic views using `cortex semantic-views search "<topic>"`.
3. **Object references**: Always use exact entity names specified by user (table names, schema names, etc.). Don't substitute similar names.
4. **Error handling**: When SQL fails, check syntax separately using `snowflake_sql_execute` with `only_compile=true`.

## Data Operations

1. **Large result awareness**: Be mindful of result set sizes. Use LIMIT for exploration queries.
2. **Performance considerations**: For complex analysis, suggest using warehouse sizing or query optimization.
3. **Security awareness**: Never expose credentials in SQL comments or query text.

## Documentation Requirements

1. **Query descriptions**: Always provide clear, business-focused descriptions for SQL queries.
2. **Semantic view grounding**: When using semantic views, start descriptions with '[Grounded: VIEW_NAME]'.

# Airtable Workflow

## Default Filters

- Always filter for **Sam Nasir** using an OR across both fields: `OR({Created By} = "Sam Nasir", FIND("Sam Nasir", ARRAYJOIN({Product Workstream Lead(s)})))`. Never filter by just one field alone.
- Exclude completed items by default: wrap in `AND(..., {Event Status} != "Complete")`. Only include Complete items when explicitly asked.
- Do NOT use named views like "Sam's View" — they include the entire fleet. Use formula filters instead.

## Hyperlinks

Always hyperlink **Event Name** and **L3 Initiative** columns in the output sheet:
- Event Name → use the `Edit Initiative Record` field URL from the L4 record
- L3 Initiative → construct from the `L3 Record ID` field: `https://airtable.com/appT2LzFjaV5SwIbk/pagp926kb6wIZWvC2?tNvEL={L3 Record ID}`
- Use `=HYPERLINK("url","display text")` formula in Google Sheets cells

## Before Any Airtable Query

Read `~/.claude/memory/tools/airtable.md` for base IDs, table IDs, field names, and formula patterns.

# Jira Workflow

## Always Use Direct curl (NOT MCP tools)

Never use `mcp__jira__*` tools for queries. They are unreliable (parameter errors, SSE flakiness). Always query the Jira REST API directly via curl.

## Token Extraction

```bash
JIRA_TOKEN=$(docker exec $(docker ps -q --filter ancestor=audience-jira-mcp-server) printenv JIRA_TOKEN)
```

Fallback chain if container token extraction fails:
1. Read from `~/.atlassian-tokens.env`
2. Ask the user

## JQL with Special Characters

For JQL containing parentheses, quotes, or special chars, use `curl -G` with `--data-urlencode`:

```bash
curl -s --max-time 15 -G \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $JIRA_TOKEN" \
  --data-urlencode 'jql=project = DSACQ AND summary ~ "\"Hulu Media360\""' \
  --data-urlencode 'fields=key,summary,status,assignee' \
  --data-urlencode 'maxResults=50' \
  "https://jira.disney.com/rest/api/2/search"
```

## Before Any Jira Operation

Always read `~/.claude/memory/tools/jira.md` (curl templates, custom field IDs, Docker setup) and `~/.claude/memory/domain/jira.md` (project keys, sprint IDs, epics) before executing.

# Testing Conventions

## Framework

- **pytest** for all Python tests in `~/.claude/tests/`
- Tests run automatically via pre-commit hook (`check-doc-sync.py`)

## Preferred Patterns

- **`monkeypatch`** over `unittest.mock.patch` — flat structure, no nested `with` blocks
- **`pytest.approx`** for all float comparisons
- **`pytest.param(id=...)`** on all `@pytest.mark.parametrize` calls for readable output
- **`capsys`** to capture and assert stdout/stderr
- **`pytest.raises`** for exception testing
- **`conftest.py`** for shared fixtures (module loading, test data, report objects)

## Test Data

- Use **relative dates** (`datetime.now() - timedelta(days=N)`) for time-sensitive fixtures, never hardcoded dates
- Shared fixtures in `tests/conftest.py` — hyphenated script modules loaded via `importlib`

## Coverage

- Every new script or hook should have corresponding tests
- Test both happy path and error cases (missing files, bad input, timeouts)

File: scripts/lib/skill_parser.py
================
"""Parse SKILL.md files: YAML front-matter, file references, MCP tool lists."""

import os
import re
import yaml


def parse_front_matter(path: str) -> dict | None:
    """Parse YAML front-matter between --- delimiters. Returns dict or None if missing/invalid."""
    try:
        with open(path) as f:
            content = f.read()
    except (OSError, IOError):
        return None

    match = re.match(r'^---\s*\n(.*?)\n---', content, re.DOTALL)
    if not match:
        return None

    try:
        return yaml.safe_load(match.group(1)) or {}
    except yaml.YAMLError:
        return None


def extract_file_references(path: str) -> list[dict]:
    """Scan SKILL.md for relative markdown links [text](path).

    Returns list of dicts: {"text": str, "ref": str, "abs_path": str, "exists": bool}
    """
    try:
        with open(path) as f:
            content = f.read()
    except (OSError, IOError):
        return []

    # Strip fenced code blocks and inline code before scanning for links
    stripped = re.sub(r'```.*?```', '', content, flags=re.DOTALL)
    stripped = re.sub(r'`[^`]+`', '', stripped)

    skill_dir = os.path.dirname(path)
    refs = []
    # Match markdown links but exclude http/https URLs and anchors
    for match in re.finditer(r'\[([^\]]+)\]\(([^)]+)\)', stripped):
        text, ref = match.group(1), match.group(2)
        if ref.startswith(('http://', 'https://', '#', 'mailto:')):
            continue
        abs_path = os.path.normpath(os.path.join(skill_dir, ref))
        refs.append({
            "text": text,
            "ref": ref,
            "abs_path": abs_path,
            "exists": os.path.exists(abs_path),
        })
    return refs


def extract_mcp_tools(front_matter: dict) -> list[str]:
    """Pull allowed-tools list from parsed front-matter. Returns empty list if missing."""
    if not front_matter:
        return []
    tools = front_matter.get("allowed-tools", [])
    return tools if isinstance(tools, list) else []


def get_all_skills(skills_dir: str) -> list[dict]:
    """Discover all skills under the given directory.

    Returns list of dicts: {"name": str, "path": str, "skill_md": str}
    """
    skills = []
    if not os.path.isdir(skills_dir):
        return skills

    for entry in sorted(os.listdir(skills_dir)):
        skill_dir = os.path.join(skills_dir, entry)
        skill_md = os.path.join(skill_dir, "SKILL.md")
        if os.path.isdir(skill_dir) and os.path.isfile(skill_md):
            skills.append({
                "name": entry,
                "path": skill_dir,
                "skill_md": skill_md,
            })
    return skills

File: scripts/cortex_to_mlflow_converter.py
================
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Convert Cortex Code conversation JSON files to MLflow traces.
Preserves full provenance with enhanced tagging system.
"""

import csv
import json
import os
import sqlite3
import uuid
from datetime import datetime, timezone
from pathlib import Path
import argparse

COST_LOG_PATH = Path("~/.claude/cost-log.csv").expanduser()


def get_imported_session_ids(mlflow_db_path):
    """Return set of cortex_session_id values already in MLflow."""
    conn = sqlite3.connect(mlflow_db_path)
    try:
        rows = conn.execute(
            "SELECT value FROM trace_request_metadata WHERE key = 'cortex_session_id'"
        ).fetchall()
        return {row[0] for row in rows}
    finally:
        conn.close()


# Enhanced provenance tagging for Cortex traces
def get_cortex_provenance_tags(cortex_session_id, conversation_file):
    """Generate enhanced provenance tags for Cortex traces."""
    return {
        # Existing system (from capture-cost.py)
        "system_source": "cortex_code",
        "tool_context": "mcp_bash_snowflake_local", 
        "session_type": "cli_interactive",
        
        # Enhanced provenance
        "data_source": "cortex_conversations",
        "import_method": "json_converter", 
        "original_session_id": cortex_session_id,
        "source_file": str(conversation_file.name),
        "converted_at": datetime.now(timezone.utc).isoformat(),
        "converter_version": "1.0"
    }


def append_to_cost_log(session_id, input_tokens, output_tokens, timestamp_ms):
    """Append a Cortex Code session row to cost-log.csv."""
    date_str = datetime.fromtimestamp(timestamp_ms / 1000).strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
    # Cortex Code uses Snowflake-hosted models — cost is not directly measurable,
    # so we record 0.0 and rely on token counts for relative comparison.
    row = [date_str, session_id, "0.0", str(input_tokens), str(output_tokens), "0", "0", "cortex-code"]
    with open(COST_LOG_PATH, "a", newline="") as f:
        csv.writer(f).writerow(row)


def convert_cortex_conversation_to_mlflow(conversation_file, mlflow_db_path, already_imported=None):
    """Convert a single Cortex conversation JSON to MLflow trace format.

    Args:
        already_imported: Optional set of cortex_session_id strings to skip.
            If None, queries MLflow directly to check.
    """
    # Read Cortex conversation
    with open(conversation_file, 'r') as f:
        conversation = json.load(f)

    session_id = conversation.get('session_id', str(uuid.uuid4()))

    # Dedup: skip if already imported
    if already_imported is not None:
        if session_id in already_imported:
            print(f"⏭️  Skipping {session_id} (already imported)")
            return None
    else:
        if session_id in get_imported_session_ids(mlflow_db_path):
            print(f"⏭️  Skipping {session_id} (already imported)")
            return None

    print(f"Converting {conversation_file}...")
    title = conversation.get('title', 'Untitled Cortex Session')
    
    # Generate MLflow trace data
    trace_id = str(uuid.uuid4())
    request_id = str(uuid.uuid4())
    
    # Build conversation text and collect message IDs for cross-reference
    messages = []
    message_ids = []
    total_input_tokens = 0
    total_output_tokens = 0

    for entry in conversation.get('history', []):
        role = entry.get('role', 'unknown')
        msg_id = entry.get('id', '')
        if msg_id:
            message_ids.append(msg_id)
        content_items = entry.get('content', [])

        for item in content_items:
            if item.get('type') == 'text':
                text = item.get('text', '')
                if text and not item.get('internalOnly', False):
                    messages.append(f"{role.upper()}: {text}")

                    # Rough token estimation (will be overridden by actual usage if available)
                    if role == 'user':
                        total_input_tokens += len(text.split()) * 1.3  # rough estimate
                    else:
                        total_output_tokens += len(text.split()) * 1.3

            # Extract actual token usage if available
            if 'usage' in item:
                usage = item['usage']
                total_input_tokens += usage.get('input_tokens', 0)
                total_output_tokens += usage.get('output_tokens', 0)

    conversation_text = "\n\n".join(messages)
    
    # Get enhanced provenance tags
    provenance_tags = get_cortex_provenance_tags(session_id, conversation_file)
    
    # Connect to MLflow SQLite database
    conn = sqlite3.connect(mlflow_db_path)
    cursor = conn.cursor()
    
    try:
        # Insert trace_info
        timestamp_ms = int(datetime.now(timezone.utc).timestamp() * 1000)
        
        cursor.execute("""
            INSERT INTO trace_info (
                request_id, experiment_id, timestamp_ms, execution_time_ms, status
            ) VALUES (?, ?, ?, ?, ?)
        """, (request_id, "0", timestamp_ms, 0, "OK"))
        
        # Insert trace_request_metadata (provenance tags)
        for key, value in provenance_tags.items():
            cursor.execute("""
                INSERT INTO trace_request_metadata (request_id, key, value)
                VALUES (?, ?, ?)
            """, (request_id, key, str(value)))
        
        # Add conversation metadata
        metadata = {
            "cortex_title": title,
            "cortex_session_id": session_id,
            "cortex_message_ids": json.dumps(message_ids),
            "message_count": len(conversation.get('history', [])),
            "estimated_input_tokens": int(total_input_tokens),
            "estimated_output_tokens": int(total_output_tokens),
            "conversation_text": conversation_text[:5000] + "..." if len(conversation_text) > 5000 else conversation_text
        }
        
        for key, value in metadata.items():
            cursor.execute("""
                INSERT INTO trace_request_metadata (request_id, key, value)
                VALUES (?, ?, ?)
            """, (request_id, key, str(value)))
        
        conn.commit()

        # Append to cost-log.csv
        append_to_cost_log(
            session_id=session_id,
            input_tokens=int(total_input_tokens),
            output_tokens=int(total_output_tokens),
            timestamp_ms=timestamp_ms,
        )

        print(f"✅ Converted session {session_id} -> MLflow trace {request_id}")
        return request_id
        
    except Exception as e:
        conn.rollback()
        print(f"❌ Error converting {conversation_file}: {e}")
        return None
    finally:
        conn.close()


def main():
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description='Convert Cortex conversations to MLflow traces')
    parser.add_argument('--cortex-dir', default='~/.snowflake/cortex/conversations',
                        help='Directory containing Cortex conversation JSON files')
    parser.add_argument('--mlflow-db', default='~/mlflow.db',
                        help='Path to MLflow SQLite database')
    parser.add_argument('--dry-run', action='store_true',
                        help='Show what would be converted without making changes')
    
    args = parser.parse_args()
    
    cortex_dir = Path(args.cortex_dir).expanduser()
    mlflow_db = Path(args.mlflow_db).expanduser()
    
    if not cortex_dir.exists():
        print(f"❌ Cortex directory not found: {cortex_dir}")
        return 1
    
    if not mlflow_db.exists():
        print(f"❌ MLflow database not found: {mlflow_db}")
        return 1
    
    # Find all Cortex conversation files
    conversation_files = list(cortex_dir.glob("*.json"))
    if not conversation_files:
        print(f"No conversation JSON files found in {cortex_dir}")
        return 0
    
    print(f"Found {len(conversation_files)} Cortex conversation files")

    # Fetch already-imported sessions once for dedup
    already_imported = get_imported_session_ids(mlflow_db)

    if args.dry_run:
        new_files = []
        for f in conversation_files:
            with open(f, 'r') as fh:
                sid = json.load(fh).get('session_id', '')
            if sid in already_imported:
                print(f"  ⏭️  {f.name} (already imported)")
            else:
                print(f"  🆕 {f.name}")
                new_files.append(f)
        print(f"\nDRY RUN: {len(new_files)} new, {len(conversation_files) - len(new_files)} already imported")
        return 0

    # Convert each conversation (dedup handled inside)
    converted_count = 0
    for conv_file in conversation_files:
        result = convert_cortex_conversation_to_mlflow(conv_file, mlflow_db, already_imported)
        if result:
            converted_count += 1

    print(f"\n✅ Converted {converted_count} new conversations ({len(conversation_files) - converted_count} skipped as duplicates)")
    print(f"MLflow traces now include Cortex provenance tags:")
    print(f"  - system_source: cortex_code")
    print(f"  - data_source: cortex_conversations") 
    print(f"  - import_method: json_converter")
    
    return 0


if __name__ == "__main__":
    exit(main())

#!/bin/bash
# Emergency rollback for CLAUDE.md — use when Claude itself is too broken to function.
# Restores CLAUDE.md from the last auto-checkpoint (written by health-check.py on clean sessions).
set -e
CLAUDE_DIR="$HOME/.claude"
CHECKPOINT="$CLAUDE_DIR/.claude-md-checkpoint"
[ -f "$CHECKPOINT" ] || { echo "No checkpoint found at $CHECKPOINT"; exit 1; }
SHA=$(cat "$CHECKPOINT" | tr -d '[:space:]')
[ -n "$SHA" ] || { echo "Checkpoint file is empty"; exit 1; }
echo "Restoring CLAUDE.md from checkpoint ${SHA:0:7}..."
git -C "$CLAUDE_DIR" diff "$SHA" HEAD -- CLAUDE.md
git -C "$CLAUDE_DIR" checkout "$SHA" -- CLAUDE.md
git -C "$CLAUDE_DIR" add CLAUDE.md
git -C "$CLAUDE_DIR" commit -m "Emergency rollback CLAUDE.md to checkpoint ${SHA:0:7}"
echo "Restored CLAUDE.md from checkpoint ${SHA:0:7}"

================
File: scripts/tag-failure-patterns.py
================
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Tag MLflow traces with failure pattern associations and update failure-patterns.md
"""

import sqlite3
import re
from pathlib import Path

MLFLOW_DB = Path.home() / "mlflow.db"
FAILURE_PATTERNS_FILE = Path.home() / ".claude/memory/domain/failure-patterns.md"

# Failure pattern triggers to search for
FAILURE_TRIGGERS = {
    "pattern_1": "you shoudlve shown me what you added",
    "pattern_2": "Why do I need to ask you", 
    "pattern_3": "are you writing it in the same structure",
    "pattern_4": "Where are snowflake transcripts actually",
    "pattern_5": "You also did not update memory",
    "pattern_6": "claude said it sees two cortex traces"
}

SESSION_ID = "8c12b335-7831-4e8b-886a-d4e992133d43"

def find_session_traces():
    """Find all traces associated with our session"""
    conn = sqlite3.connect(MLFLOW_DB)
    
    # First try direct session lookup
    traces = conn.execute("""
        SELECT DISTINCT request_id 
        FROM trace_request_metadata 
        WHERE value = ?
    """, (SESSION_ID,)).fetchall()
    
    if traces:
        print(f"Found {len(traces)} traces by session ID")
        return [t[0] for t in traces]
    
    # Fallback: content-based search for today's traces with our keywords
    traces = conn.execute("""
        SELECT DISTINCT trm.request_id 
        FROM trace_request_metadata trm
        JOIN trace_info ti ON trm.request_id = ti.request_id
        WHERE ti.timestamp_ms >= ? 
        AND (trm.value LIKE '%commit%' OR trm.value LIKE '%memory%' OR trm.value LIKE '%failure pattern%')
    """, (1773298800000,)).fetchall()  # Today's timestamp
    
    conn.close()
    print(f"Found {len(traces)} traces by content matching")
    return [t[0] for t in traces]

def match_traces_to_patterns(trace_ids):
    """Match traces to specific failure patterns by content"""
    conn = sqlite3.connect(MLFLOW_DB)
    matched_patterns = {}
    
    for trace_id in trace_ids:
        # Get all content for this trace
        content = conn.execute("""
            SELECT key, value 
            FROM trace_request_metadata 
            WHERE request_id = ?
        """, (trace_id,)).fetchall()
        
        # Combine all content into searchable text
        full_content = " ".join([v for k, v in content])
        
        # Check each failure pattern trigger
        for pattern_id, trigger in FAILURE_TRIGGERS.items():
            if trigger.lower() in full_content.lower():
                if pattern_id not in matched_patterns:
                    matched_patterns[pattern_id] = []
                matched_patterns[pattern_id].append(trace_id)
                print(f"Matched {trace_id} to {pattern_id}: '{trigger}'")
    
    conn.close()
    return matched_patterns

def tag_traces_in_mlflow(matched_patterns):
    """Add failure pattern tags to traces in MLflow"""
    conn = sqlite3.connect(MLFLOW_DB)
    
    for pattern_id, trace_ids in matched_patterns.items():
        for trace_id in trace_ids:
            # Add failure pattern tag
            conn.execute("""
                INSERT OR REPLACE INTO trace_tags (request_id, key, value)
                VALUES (?, 'failure_pattern', ?)
            """, (trace_id, pattern_id))
            
            # Add session association tag
            conn.execute("""
                INSERT OR REPLACE INTO trace_tags (request_id, key, value) 
                VALUES (?, 'session_id', ?)
            """, (trace_id, SESSION_ID))
    
    conn.commit()
    conn.close()
    print(f"Tagged {sum(len(ids) for ids in matched_patterns.values())} traces in MLflow")

def update_failure_patterns_file(matched_patterns):
    """Update failure-patterns.md with correct trace IDs"""
    
    # Read current file
    content = FAILURE_PATTERNS_FILE.read_text()
    
    # Create mapping for replacements
    replacements = {}
    for pattern_id, trace_ids in matched_patterns.items():
        trace_list = ", ".join(trace_ids)
        replacements[f"(session-{SESSION_ID}, no-mlflow-trace)"] = f"(session-{SESSION_ID}, {trace_list})"
    
    # Apply replacements
    updated_content = content
    for old, new in replacements.items():
        updated_content = updated_content.replace(old, new)
    
    # Write back
    FAILURE_PATTERNS_FILE.write_text(updated_content)
    print("Updated failure-patterns.md with trace IDs")

def main():
    print(f"Searching for traces from session {SESSION_ID}...")
    
    # Find traces
    trace_ids = find_session_traces()
    if not trace_ids:
        print("No traces found!")
        return
    
    print(f"Found traces: {trace_ids}")
    
    # Match to failure patterns
    matched_patterns = match_traces_to_patterns(trace_ids)
    if not matched_patterns:
        print("No failure patterns matched!")
        return
    
    print(f"Matched patterns: {matched_patterns}")
    
    # Tag in MLflow
    tag_traces_in_mlflow(matched_patterns)
    
    # Update file
    update_failure_patterns_file(matched_patterns)
    
    print("Done!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

File: scripts/validate-atlassian-token.py
================
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Validate and apply Atlassian (Jira/Confluence) Personal Access Tokens.

Usage:
    python3 validate-atlassian-token.py --token <TOKEN> [--service jira|confluence|auto] [--apply]

Validates a token against Jira and/or Confluence APIs, checks expiry,
and optionally writes to ~/.atlassian-tokens.env and propagates to services.
"""

import argparse
import json
import os
import socket
import subprocess
import sys
from datetime import datetime, timezone

TOKEN_FILE = os.path.expanduser("~/.atlassian-tokens.env")
CONFLUENCE_ENV = os.path.expanduser("~/confluence-mcp-server/.env")

ENDPOINTS = {
    "jira": {
        "host": "jira.disney.com",
        "myself": "https://jira.disney.com/rest/api/2/myself",
        "tokens": "https://jira.disney.com/rest/pat/latest/tokens",
    },
    "confluence": {
        "host": "confluence.disney.com",
        "myself": "https://confluence.disney.com/rest/api/user/current",
        "tokens": "https://confluence.disney.com/rest/pat/latest/tokens",
    },
}


def check_vpn(host: str) -> bool:
    """Check if the host is reachable (VPN connected)."""
    try:
        socket.getaddrinfo(host, 443, socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)
        return True
    except socket.gaierror:
        return False


def validate_token(token: str, service: str) -> dict | None:
    """Validate a token against a service. Returns user info or None."""
    ep = ENDPOINTS[service]
    try:
        r = subprocess.run(
            ["curl", "-sf", "--max-time", "10",
             "-H", f"Authorization: Bearer {token}",
             ep["myself"]],
            capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=15,
        )
        if r.returncode != 0 or not r.stdout.strip():
            return None
        data = json.loads(r.stdout)
        # Jira returns displayName, Confluence returns displayName too
        return {
            "service": service,
            "valid": True,
            "user": data.get("displayName", "unknown"),
        }
    except (subprocess.TimeoutExpired, json.JSONDecodeError, FileNotFoundError):
        return None


def check_token_expiry(token: str, service: str) -> dict | None:
    """Check token expiry via PAT API. Returns expiry info or None."""
    ep = ENDPOINTS[service]
    try:
        r = subprocess.run(
            ["curl", "-sf", "--max-time", "10",
             "-H", f"Authorization: Bearer {token}",
             ep["tokens"]],
            capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=15,
        )
        if r.returncode != 0 or not r.stdout.strip():
            return None
        tokens = json.loads(r.stdout)
        if not tokens:
            return None

        # Find the most recently accessed token
        best = max(tokens, key=lambda t: t.get("lastAuthenticatedAt", t.get("lastAccessedAt", "")))
        expiring_at = best.get("expiringAt")
        if not expiring_at:
            return {"name": best.get("name", "unknown"), "expires": None, "days_remaining": None}

        exp_dt = datetime.fromisoformat(expiring_at.replace("Z", "+00:00"))
        now = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
        days = (exp_dt - now).days

        return {
            "name": best.get("name", "unknown"),
            "expires": exp_dt.strftime("%Y-%m-%d"),
            "days_remaining": days,
        }
    except (subprocess.TimeoutExpired, json.JSONDecodeError, FileNotFoundError, ValueError):
        return None


def read_token_file() -> dict[str, str]:
    """Read existing tokens from the token file."""
    tokens = {}
    if not os.path.isfile(TOKEN_FILE):
        return tokens
    with open(TOKEN_FILE) as f:
        for line in f:
            line = line.strip()
            if "=" in line and not line.startswith("#"):
                key, val = line.split("=", 1)
                tokens[key.strip()] = val.strip()
    return tokens


def write_token_file(tokens: dict[str, str]):
    """Write tokens to the token file (chmod 600)."""
    with open(TOKEN_FILE, "w") as f:
        for key, val in sorted(tokens.items()):
            f.write(f"{key}={val}\n")
    os.chmod(TOKEN_FILE, 0o600)


def apply_jira_token(token: str) -> bool:
    """Restart the Jira Docker container with the new token."""
    # Find running container
    try:
        r = subprocess.run(
            ["docker", "ps", "-q", "--filter", "ancestor=audience-jira-mcp-server"],
            capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=5,
        )
        container_id = r.stdout.strip()
    except (subprocess.TimeoutExpired, FileNotFoundError):
        container_id = ""

    # Stop and remove existing container
    if container_id:
        subprocess.run(["docker", "stop", container_id], capture_output=True, timeout=15)
        subprocess.run(["docker", "rm", container_id], capture_output=True, timeout=5)

    # Start new container
    try:
        r = subprocess.run(
            ["docker", "run", "-d", "-p", "3000:3000",
             "-e", f"JIRA_TOKEN={token}",
             "-e", "JIRA_URL=https://jira.disney.com",
             "-e", "MCP_TRANSPORT=sse",
             "-e", "MCP_PORT=3000",
             "audience-jira-mcp-server"],
            capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=15,
        )
        return r.returncode == 0
    except (subprocess.TimeoutExpired, FileNotFoundError):
        return False


def apply_confluence_token(token: str) -> bool:
    """Update the Confluence MCP server .env file."""
    if not os.path.isfile(CONFLUENCE_ENV):
        return False
    try:
        with open(CONFLUENCE_ENV) as f:
            lines = f.readlines()
        new_lines = []
        found = False
        for line in lines:
            if line.strip().startswith("CONFLUENCE_TOKEN="):
                new_lines.append(f"CONFLUENCE_TOKEN={token}\n")
                found = True
            else:
                new_lines.append(line)
        if not found:
            new_lines.append(f"CONFLUENCE_TOKEN={token}\n")
        with open(CONFLUENCE_ENV, "w") as f:
            f.writelines(new_lines)
        return True
    except OSError:
        return False


def main():
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Validate and apply Atlassian PAT tokens")
    parser.add_argument("--token", required=True, help="The PAT token to validate")
    parser.add_argument("--service", choices=["jira", "confluence", "auto"], default="auto",
                        help="Service to validate against (default: auto-detect)")
    parser.add_argument("--apply", action="store_true",
                        help="Write to token file and propagate to services")
    args = parser.parse_args()

    # VPN check first
    for svc in (["jira", "confluence"] if args.service == "auto" else [args.service]):
        host = ENDPOINTS[svc]["host"]
        if not check_vpn(host):
            result = {"error": f"Cannot resolve {host} — VPN likely disconnected", "valid": False}
            print(json.dumps(result, indent=2))
            sys.exit(1)

    # Validate token
    services_to_try = ["jira", "confluence"] if args.service == "auto" else [args.service]
    validated = None

    for svc in services_to_try:
        info = validate_token(args.token, svc)
        if info:
            validated = info
            break

    if not validated:
        result = {"valid": False, "error": "Token not valid for any service", "tried": services_to_try}
        print(json.dumps(result, indent=2))
        sys.exit(1)

    service = validated["service"]
    result = {
        "service": service,
        "valid": True,
        "user": validated["user"],
    }

    # Check expiry
    expiry = check_token_expiry(args.token, service)
    if expiry:
        result["token_name"] = expiry["name"]
        result["expires"] = expiry["expires"]
        result["days_remaining"] = expiry["days_remaining"]
        if expiry["days_remaining"] is not None and expiry["days_remaining"] < 7:
            result["warning"] = f"Token expires in {expiry['days_remaining']} days!"

    # Apply if requested
    if args.apply:
        # Update token file
        tokens = read_token_file()
        key = "JIRA_TOKEN" if service == "jira" else "CONFLUENCE_TOKEN"
        tokens[key] = args.token
        write_token_file(tokens)
        result["token_file_updated"] = True

        # Propagate to service
        if service == "jira":
            result["container_restarted"] = apply_jira_token(args.token)
        elif service == "confluence":
            result["env_file_updated"] = apply_confluence_token(args.token)

        result["applied"] = True
    else:
        result["applied"] = False

    print(json.dumps(result, indent=2))
    sys.exit(0)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

================
File: skills/ab-test-claude-md/README.md
================
# A/B Testing CLAUDE.md

How to compare two versions of CLAUDE.md to decide which performs better.

## Quick Start

1. Run `/ab-test-claude-md` to set up the test
2. Run the 8 test prompts in the current session
3. Swap to the other version (command provided by the skill)
4. Start a new session and run the same 8 prompts
5. Re-invoke `/ab-test-claude-md` to compare results and pick a winner

## Test Prompts

| # | Prompt | What It Tests |
|---|--------|---------------|
| 1 | `skill find-active-tickets` | Direct skill routing |
| 2 | `what should I work on` | Alias routing (find-my-to-dos) |
| 3 | `show me my recent traces` | Trace reading |
| 4 | `tag that as a failure` | Trace editing |
| 5 | `add this as a known issue` | Known issue workflow |
| 6 | `save my CLAUDE.md as test-label` | CLAUDE.md versioning (inline) |
| 7 | `is jira working` | Alias routing (connect-jira) |
| 8 | `reorganize memory` | Memory maintenance (inline) |

## How to Swap Versions

```bash
# Switch to version A
git -C ~/.claude checkout claude-md/<label_a> -- CLAUDE.md

# Switch to version B
git -C ~/.claude checkout claude-md/<label_b> -- CLAUDE.md
```

Always start a **new session** after swapping.

## How to Record Results

Open `~/.claude/claude-md-ab-test.md` and fill in the Results table:

- **Pass/Fail** for each prompt
- **Session cost** (from cost-log.csv or `/health-check`)
- **Notes** on response quality, correctness, or behavior differences

## How to Compare and Decide

Re-invoke `/ab-test-claude-md` — it reads the tracking doc, computes a cost comparison, and asks which version you want to keep. The chosen version is checked out and committed.

## Listing All Versions

```bash
git -C ~/.claude tag -l "claude-md/*"
```

---
name: ab-test-claude-md
description: Set up and track A/B tests comparing CLAUDE.md versions
allowed-tools:
  - Bash
---

# A/B Test CLAUDE.md

Set up, track, and compare two CLAUDE.md versions to determine which performs better.

## Behavior

This skill has two modes depending on whether a tracking doc already exists:

### Mode 1: Setup (no tracking doc or user wants fresh start)

**Step 1 — Identify versions**

1. List existing tags:
   ```bash
   git -C ~/.claude tag -l "claude-md/*"
   ```
2. Read the auto-checkpoint:
   ```bash
   cat ~/.claude/.claude-md-checkpoint
   ```
3. Check current CLAUDE.md size:
   ```bash
   wc -l ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md
   ```
4. Ask the user to name or confirm the two versions:
   - **Version A** = control (the baseline)
   - **Version B** = treatment (the change being tested)
5. Create git tags if they don't exist:
   ```bash
   git -C ~/.claude tag claude-md/<label> <sha>
   ```

**Step 2 — Compute baseline metrics**

1. Parse `~/.claude/cost-log.csv`:
   - Filter to Opus sessions only
   - Compute average cost per session and average tokens per session
   - Count total sessions
2. Parse `~/.claude/traces.csv` (if it exists):
   - Count sessions tagged with a failure mode
3. Present a summary table of baseline metrics.

**Step 3 — Generate tracking doc**

Create `~/.claude/claude-md-ab-test.md` with these sections:

#### Version Table

| Version | Label | Lines | Commit SHA | Git Tag |
|---------|-------|-------|------------|---------|
| A (control) | ... | ... | ... | claude-md/... |
| B (treatment) | ... | ... | ... | claude-md/... |

#### Baseline Metrics

| Metric | Value |
|--------|-------|
| Avg cost/session (Opus) | $X.XX |
| Avg tokens/session | X,XXX |
| Total sessions measured | N |
| Failure count | N |

#### Test Prompts

Run each prompt exactly as written. Record pass/fail and notes.

| # | Prompt | Tests |
|---|--------|-------|
| 1 | `skill find-active-tickets` | Direct skill routing |
| 2 | `what should I work on` | Alias routing (find-my-to-dos) |
| 3 | `show me my recent traces` | Trace reading |
| 4 | `tag that as a failure` | Trace editing |
| 5 | `add this as a known issue` | Known issue workflow |
| 6 | `save my CLAUDE.md as test-label` | CLAUDE.md versioning (inline) |
| 7 | `is jira working` | Alias routing (connect-jira) |
| 8 | `reorganize memory` | Memory maintenance (inline) |

#### Results Table

| # | Version | Date | Pass/Fail | Session Cost | Notes |
|---|---------|------|-----------|-------------|-------|
| 1 | A | | | | |
| 2 | A | | | | |
| ... | | | | | |
| 1 | B | | | | |
| ... | | | | | |

#### Switch Commands

```bash
# Switch to version A
git -C ~/.claude checkout claude-md/<label_a> -- CLAUDE.md

# Switch to version B
git -C ~/.claude checkout claude-md/<label_b> -- CLAUDE.md
```

Always start a new session after swapping.

#### Decision

_Left blank until results are recorded and the skill is re-invoked._

**Step 4 — Report**

Summarize what was done:
- Versions tagged (with labels and SHAs)
- Baseline metrics computed
- Tracking doc created at `~/.claude/claude-md-ab-test.md`

Remind the user of the protocol:
1. Run the 8 test prompts in the current session (version A)
2. Swap to version B using the switch command
3. Start a **new** session and run the same 8 prompts
4. Fill in the Results table in the tracking doc
5. Re-invoke `/ab-test-claude-md` to compare and choose a winner

### Mode 2: Compare (tracking doc exists with results)

1. Read `~/.claude/claude-md-ab-test.md`
2. Parse the Results table — count pass/fail per version
3. Compute cost comparison:
   - Parse `~/.claude/cost-log.csv` for sessions during each test period
   - Compare average cost between version A and version B periods
4. Present a comparison summary:
   - Pass rate: A vs B
   - Cost: A vs B
   - Any notable quality differences from notes
5. Ask the user via AskUserQuestion: "Which version do you want to keep?"
   - Options: Version A (label), Version B (label)
6. On selection:
   ```bash
   git -C ~/.claude checkout claude-md/<chosen_label> -- CLAUDE.md
   cd ~/.claude && git add CLAUDE.md && git commit -m "A/B test winner: <chosen_label>"
   ```
7. Confirm the swap was made.

## Guidelines

- **Always use git tags for versions**, not loose SHA references. Tags are human-readable and survive branch resets.
- **Minimum 8 test prompts per version** before comparing. Fewer than 8 gives unreliable signal — small sample sizes amplify noise.
- **Always start a new session after swapping versions.** CLAUDE.md is loaded at session start. Swapping mid-session won't take effect for most behavior.
- **Cost comparison must use Opus sessions only.** Mixed-model sessions skew cost data. Filter by model before computing averages.
- **Don't declare a winner on pass rate alone.** A version that passes 8/8 at 2x the cost may not be better. Present both metrics and let the user decide.
- **If results are inconclusive** (similar pass rate, similar cost), recommend running 8 more prompts per version or testing with different prompt categories before choosing.
- **Never delete the tracking doc** after a test completes. It's the audit trail for why a version was chosen.

---

## Examples

### Example 1: Setting Up a New Test

**User**: `/ab-test-claude-md`

**Claude does**:
1. Lists existing tags: `claude-md/slim`, `claude-md/v2-verbose`
2. Reads auto-checkpoint SHA
3. Asks: "Which two versions do you want to test? I see tags `slim` and `v2-verbose`."
4. User confirms → Claude computes baseline metrics from cost-log.csv
5. Creates tracking doc at `~/.claude/claude-md-ab-test.md`
6. Reports: "Test set up. Version A = slim (82 lines), Version B = v2-verbose (145 lines). Baseline: $0.38/session avg across 47 Opus sessions. Run the 8 test prompts, then swap versions."

### Example 2: Comparing Results

**User**: `/ab-test-claude-md` (tracking doc exists with filled results table)

**Claude does**:
1. Reads tracking doc, parses results: A passed 7/8 at $0.35/session, B passed 8/8 at $0.52/session
2. Presents comparison:
   > **Version A (slim)**: 87.5% pass rate, $0.35 avg cost
   > **Version B (v2-verbose)**: 100% pass rate, $0.52 avg cost (+49%)
   > Version B passes all tests but costs significantly more. The one A failure was alias routing for "what should I work on."
3. Asks: "Which version do you want to keep?"
4. User picks A → Claude restores and commits

File: skills/jira-ticket-finder/query_hulu_m360.py
