# Data Product Context Layer Framework

## Making Data AI-Ready

A structured approach to building the contextual intelligence that AI systems need to correctly query, interpret, and reason over data products.

---

## The Problem

AI systems (LLMs, agents, Cortex Analyst, copilots) fail on data not because the data is bad, but because the **context is missing**. When an AI agent encounters a table called `fact_revenue`, it doesn't know:

- What "revenue" means in this business context (gross? net? recognized? billed?)
- Where the data came from and how it was transformed
- What the known quality issues are
- What rules govern how it should be queried
- What past mistakes look like so it can avoid them

Without context, AI systems hallucinate column meanings, write incorrect joins, misinterpret business logic, and produce confidently wrong answers. **The context layer is the difference between an AI that queries data and an AI that understands data.**

---

## The Five Layers

Each layer answers a specific question an AI system needs answered before it can work with data reliably.

### 1. Definitions — "What does this data mean?"

The semantic and structural truth about the data. This is what AI systems need most and have least.

| Component | What It Provides to AI | Example |
|-----------|----------------------|---------|
| **Business Glossary** | Disambiguates terms so the AI uses the right business meaning | "Active Subscriber: A user with a paid, non-paused subscription as of the measurement date. Excludes free trials." |
| **Data Dictionary** | Maps natural language concepts to physical columns/tables | "`dim_subscriber.is_active` (BOOLEAN): Derived from subscription_status != 'paused' AND payment_status = 'current'" |
| **Lineage** | Tells the AI where data originates and how it transforms, preventing incorrect source attribution | "Raw events (S3) -> Bronze (Snowflake raw) -> Silver (dbt deduplicated) -> Gold (aggregate)" |
| **Contracts** | Tells the AI what guarantees hold (freshness, completeness, schema stability) | "Table refreshes daily by 6 AM ET. Partition key: event_date. Schema changes require 2-sprint notice." |
| **Relationships** | Tells the AI how to join tables correctly | "`fact_revenue.subscriber_id` joins to `dim_subscriber.subscriber_id` (many-to-one). Never join on `user_id` — it's deprecated." |

**Why this is the critical layer:** Every AI failure on data traces back to a missing or wrong definition. An LLM that doesn't know "revenue" means net recognized revenue will write a query that returns gross billed revenue and present it with full confidence.

---

### 2. Rules — "What must always be true?"

Constraints and policies that an AI system must respect when generating queries, interpreting results, or making recommendations.

| Component | What It Provides to AI | Example |
|-----------|----------------------|---------|
| **Data Quality Rules** | Guardrails for query generation and result validation | "Revenue must never be negative. If a query returns negative revenue, flag it — don't report it." |
| **Access & Compliance Policies** | Boundaries the AI must not cross | "PII columns (email, name, device_id) require masking. Never include raw PII in generated outputs." |
| **Query Patterns** | Preferred/required ways to query specific domains | "Always filter by `is_test = FALSE` on subscriber tables. Always use `event_date` partition key for performance." |
| **Business Rules** | Logic the AI must apply that isn't in the data itself | "International revenue must be converted to USD using the `dim_fx_rate` table, not a hardcoded rate." |

**Why AI needs this:** Without rules, an AI agent will write a perfectly valid SQL query that violates a business constraint. The query runs, returns results, and the results are wrong — but syntactically correct. Rules are the AI's guardrails.

---

### 3. Lessons — "What non-obvious things should I know?"

Insights that require judgment and context to apply. These are the things a senior analyst knows but a new hire (or an AI) doesn't.

| Component | What It Provides to AI | Example |
|-----------|----------------------|---------|
| **Domain Insights** | Non-obvious business logic that affects interpretation | "Q4 subscriber counts spike due to gift subscriptions. These churn in January. Don't use Q4 as a baseline for growth projections." |
| **Architecture Decisions** | Why the data is structured a certain way | "We denormalized the subscriber dimension because the normalized version had 12-way joins that timed out. The trade-off is update lag." |
| **Interpretation Guidance** | How to read results correctly | "A 'churn rate' of 0% in a given week usually means the pipeline hasn't run, not that nobody churned." |
| **Known Gotchas** | Traps that look correct but aren't | "The `created_date` field on the events table is when the record was ingested, not when the event occurred. Use `event_timestamp` instead." |

**Why AI needs this:** These are the mistakes an AI will make on its first, second, and third attempt — because the data *looks* correct. Lessons are the accumulated wisdom that prevents plausible-but-wrong analysis.

---

### 4. Memory — "What's the current state of this product?"

Operational context that changes over time. This layer keeps AI systems current on what's happening *now*.

| Component | What It Provides to AI | Example |
|-----------|----------------------|---------|
| **Stakeholder Map** | Who to reference, who cares about what | "Finance team owns revenue reporting. Marketing owns attribution. Don't mix their metric definitions." |
| **Active Migrations** | What's in flux and shouldn't be trusted yet | "Table `fact_revenue_v2` is in migration. Use `fact_revenue` until April 15 cutover." |
| **Tool & Config State** | Connection details, warehouse assignments | "Use warehouse ANALYTICS_WH for reads. Writes go to ETL_WH. Don't query raw zone directly." |
| **Artifact Index** | Where to find authoritative docs | "PRD: [link]. Architecture diagram: [link]. DQ dashboard: [link]." |

**Why AI needs this:** Data products are not static. Tables get migrated, schemas change, pipelines break and get fixed. An AI using stale memory will query deprecated tables or reference sunset metrics.

---

### 5. Failure Patterns — "What's gone wrong before?"

Documented incidents that teach AI systems what *not* to do. This is the negative space of knowledge — equally important as knowing what's correct.

| Component | What It Provides to AI | Example |
|-----------|----------------------|---------|
| **Incident Record** | What went wrong and when | "2026-02-15: Revenue report showed $0 for LATAM. Root cause: timezone mismatch in partition filter." |
| **Prevention Rule** | Specific action to avoid recurrence | "All date filters on the revenue table must use `convert_tz(event_timestamp, 'UTC', region_tz)`. Never filter on raw UTC." |
| **Anti-Patterns** | Query patterns that look correct but produce wrong results | "Don't use `COUNT(DISTINCT user_id)` on the events table for subscriber counts — it includes anonymous sessions." |
| **Recurrence Tracking** | Whether this is a one-off or a systemic issue | "Timezone-related errors have occurred 4 times across 3 tables. Systemic — always check timezone handling." |

**Why AI needs this:** Without failure patterns, an AI system will repeat every mistake the team has already made. Failure patterns are the fastest way to make an AI system as smart as a veteran team member — not by teaching it what's right, but by teaching it what's *already gone wrong*.

---

## The Graduation Chain

Context moves between layers as it matures:

```
Failure Pattern  →  Lesson  →  Rule  →  Definition
   (incident)       (insight)   (imperative)  (truth)
```

- **Failure Pattern → Lesson:** When the insight generalizes beyond one incident. *"This timezone issue affects all regional data, not just LATAM."*
- **Lesson → Rule:** When the insight can be stated as an enforceable imperative. *"All date filters must use convert_tz()."*
- **Rule → Definition:** When the rule becomes so fundamental it's part of the data model itself. *"The `event_date_local` column exists because of this rule — it pre-computes the timezone conversion."*

Not everything graduates. Some lessons stay lessons forever. The chain shows how knowledge hardens over time from incident to infrastructure.

---

## The Maturity Grid

Each layer progresses through three maturity levels. The AI-readiness of a data product is determined by how much context is machine-consumable at each level.

| Layer | Level 1: Human-Readable | Level 2: Structured | Level 3: Machine-Consumable |
|-------|----------------------|-------------------|--------------------------|
| **Definitions** | Terms listed in a doc. Key tables known. | Full glossary + dictionary in structured format. Lineage documented. | Published as a versioned, machine-readable definitions file. AI resolves terms to columns programmatically. Contracts enforced via automation. |
| **Rules** | Written informally ("we always do X"). | Codified as DQ checks and policy docs. | Enforced in CI/CD. AI query generation respects rules automatically. Violations detected in real-time. |
| **Lessons** | In people's heads. | Written in wiki/docs with structure. | Indexed for retrieval. AI loads relevant lessons before generating queries. New lessons captured from AI interactions. |
| **Memory** | Scattered across Slack and email. | Consolidated per product. Updated regularly. | Version-controlled. AI reads current state before acting. Staleness alerts when memory is outdated. |
| **Failure Patterns** | Verbal "we got burned" stories. | Logged with root cause + prevention rule. | Prevention rules injected into AI context. AI validates its own output against known anti-patterns before returning results. |

### What "AI-Ready" Means

**Level 1** = AI can't use this layer (human-only knowledge)
**Level 2** = AI can reference this layer if pointed to it (structured but manual retrieval)
**Level 3** = AI consumes this layer automatically (programmatic access, real-time)

A data product is "AI-ready" when all five layers are at Level 2 or above, with Definitions and Rules at Level 3. This means an AI system can:
- Resolve business terms to physical columns and their semantic meaning (Definitions at Level 3)
- Respect constraints automatically (Rules at Level 3)
- Access lessons and memory when relevant (Level 2+)
- Avoid known mistakes (Failure Patterns at Level 2+)

================
File: references/context-layer-implementation.md
================
# Data Product Context Layer — Implementation Guide

## How to Build Each Layer

Practical guidance for populating each context layer, from file structure to tooling.

---

### Definitions

A structured, versioned file per data product that maps every business term to its physical column, data type, derivation logic, and valid join paths. The format doesn't matter as long as an AI system can read and resolve it programmatically. Pair it with descriptions, lineage graphs, and contract guarantees (freshness SLAs, schema stability) in the same machine-parseable format.

### Rules

Rules written as structured entries — not prose in a wiki. Each rule specifies: the table/column it applies to, the constraint (e.g., `revenue >= 0`), the action on violation (flag, block, or warn), and the business justification. These live alongside the definitions file so AI loads them together. Compliance policies follow the same structure — which columns are PII, what masking applies, what's off-limits.

### Lessons

Structured files with consistent metadata — domain, status, discovery date, related tables. Each lesson has a context section (what happened), the insight (what's non-obvious), and boundaries (when this does and doesn't apply). Stored in a searchable repository so that when an AI is asked about Q4 subscriber trends, the lesson about gift subscription spikes gets loaded into context before the query is written.

### Memory

A version-controlled state file per data product — lists active migrations, deprecated tables, warehouse assignments, stakeholder ownership, and links to authoritative docs. Updated as part of the development workflow (not as an afterthought). Includes a `last_updated` timestamp per entry so stale context is detectable — if a migration note is 90 days old, something's wrong.

### Failure Patterns

A structured log where each entry has: date, what went wrong, root cause, the specific prevention rule, and an anti-pattern example (the query that looks right but isn't). Prevention rules are written as concrete imperatives — "use `convert_tz()`, not raw UTC" — not vague advice like "be careful with timezones." Track recurrence counts so systemic issues get escalated, not just patched.

---

## The Graduation Chain

Context moves between layers as it matures:

```
Failure Pattern  →  Lesson  →  Rule  →  Definition
   (incident)       (insight)   (imperative)  (truth)
```

- **Failure Pattern → Lesson:** When the insight generalizes beyond one incident. *"This timezone issue affects all regional data, not just LATAM."*
- **Lesson → Rule:** When the insight can be stated as an enforceable imperative. *"All date filters must use convert_tz()."*
- **Rule → Definition:** When the rule becomes so fundamental it's part of the data model itself. *"The `event_date_local` column exists because of this rule — it pre-computes the timezone conversion."*

Not everything graduates. Some lessons stay lessons forever. The chain shows how knowledge hardens over time from incident to infrastructure.

---

## Connecting to AI Infrastructure

How each layer maps to the tools we already have — and the workflow that ties them together.

| Layer | Where It Lives | How AI Consumes It |
|-------|---------------|-------------------|
| **Definitions** | **Alation** (business glossary, data dictionary, column descriptions) + **OMS** (lineage, metadata, contracts) + **Snowflake** (queryable view layer) | Cortex Analyst reads the Snowflake view to resolve "revenue" → `fact_revenue.net_recognized_revenue_usd`. Alation provides the business definition. OMS provides lineage so the AI knows the column traces back through the silver layer, not raw ingestion. |
| **Rules** | **GitHub repo** (structured rule files versioned alongside the definitions) + **Snowflake** (DQ monitors, row access policies, masking policies) | Rules are loaded into the AI's system prompt at query time. Snowflake enforces access and masking natively — the AI never sees unmasked PII. DQ rules validate AI-generated output before it reaches the user. GitHub Actions runs validation on rule changes via CI. |
| **Lessons** | **GitHub repo** (structured lesson files per data product) | AI retrieves relevant lessons based on the tables and domain involved in the query. When a user asks about Q4 subscriber trends, the lesson about gift subscription churn is pulled from the repo and injected into context before the SQL is generated. |
| **Memory** | **GitHub repo** (version-controlled state files) + **Composable Workspaces** (access, permissioning, stakeholder visibility) | AI reads the state file to check for active migrations or deprecated tables before querying. Composable Workspaces connects the data product context to executive dashboards — stakeholders see what's in production, what's in migration, and who owns what, without needing to read a YAML file. |
| **Failure Patterns** | **GitHub repo** (structured incident log with prevention rules) | Prevention rules are injected into the AI's context automatically. Before returning results, the AI checks its own SQL against known anti-patterns (e.g., "don't use `COUNT(DISTINCT user_id)` for subscriber counts"). GitHub Actions can flag new queries that match historical anti-patterns in CI. |

### The Workflow

```
1. Data team authors/updates context files in GitHub
   (definitions, rules, lessons, memory, failure patterns)
                          │
2. GitHub Actions validates on PR    ──→  CI checks: schema valid?
   (rule conflicts? lesson format?)        Rules consistent with
                                           definitions file?
                          │
3. On merge, context is published:
   ├── Definitions     → Snowflake semantic view (CREATE OR ALTER)
   ├── Rules           → Snowflake DQ monitors + masking policies
   ├── Glossary/Dict   → Alation catalog (API sync)
   └── Lineage         → OMS metadata (API sync)
                          │
4. AI query time (Cortex Analyst, copilot, agent):
   ├── Reads semantic view    → resolves terms to columns
   ├── Loads rules            → applies constraints to SQL generation
   ├── Retrieves lessons      → loads domain context
   ├── Checks memory          → avoids deprecated tables
   └── Validates against      → flags anti-pattern matches
       failure patterns
                          │
5. Composable Workspaces surfaces product state to stakeholders
   (what's live, what's migrating, who owns it, current quality scores)
```

**GitHub is the single source of truth.** Everything flows from versioned files in a repo. Snowflake, Alation, and OMS are downstream consumers — they reflect the context, they don't define it. This means context changes go through code review, have audit trails, and can be rolled back.

# Data Product Context Layer Scorecard

## Product Information

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Data Product Name** | |
| **Team / Domain** | |
| **Data Product Manager** | |
| **Data Lead** | |
| **Assessment Date** | |
| **Assessed By** | |

---

## Maturity Assessment

Rate each layer at its current maturity level. Check the boxes that apply, then assign the overall level for that layer.

### 1. Definitions — "What does this data mean?"

| Checkpoint | Level 1: Human-Readable | Level 2: Structured | Level 3: Machine-Consumable |
|------------|----------------------|-------------------|--------------------------|
| **Business Glossary** | [ ] Key terms listed in a doc or wiki | [ ] Full glossary in a structured, searchable format | [ ] Published as versioned definitions file; AI resolves terms to columns programmatically |
| **Data Dictionary** | [ ] Key tables/columns known informally | [ ] All columns documented with types, descriptions, derivation logic | [ ] Dictionary is the queryable view layer — AI maps natural language to physical schema automatically |
| **Lineage** | [ ] Team knows where data comes from | [ ] Lineage documented (source → bronze → silver → gold) | [ ] Lineage queryable via API; AI traces any column to its origin |
| **Contracts** | [ ] Informal expectations ("it refreshes daily") | [ ] Contracts documented (freshness, completeness, schema stability) | [ ] Contracts enforced via automation; AI reads guarantees before querying |
| **Relationships** | [ ] Join logic lives in people's heads | [ ] Join paths documented (keys, one-to-many vs. many-to-many, deprecated fields) | [ ] Relationship graph consumable by AI; correct joins generated automatically |

**Current Level:** [ ] Level 1 &emsp; [ ] Level 2 &emsp; [ ] Level 3

**Key Gaps:**


---

### 2. Rules — "What must always be true?"

| Checkpoint | Level 1: Human-Readable | Level 2: Structured | Level 3: Machine-Consumable |
|------------|----------------------|-------------------|--------------------------|
| **Data Quality Rules** | [ ] Written informally ("we always check for X") | [ ] Codified as automated data quality checks | [ ] AI-generated queries validated against rules before execution |
| **Access & Compliance** | [ ] Team knows what's sensitive | [ ] Policies documented; sensitive columns (personal data, financial data) tagged | [ ] Policies enforced automatically; AI cannot surface masked data |
| **Query Patterns** | [ ] Senior analysts know the right filters | [ ] Required filters/patterns documented per table | [ ] AI applies required filters (partition keys, test flags) automatically |
| **Business Rules** | [ ] Logic lives in tribal knowledge | [ ] Rules codified in docs or config | [ ] Rules injected into AI context; violations detected in real-time |

**Current Level:** [ ] Level 1 &emsp; [ ] Level 2 &emsp; [ ] Level 3

**Key Gaps:**


---

### 3. Lessons — "What non-obvious things should I know?"

| Checkpoint | Level 1: Human-Readable | Level 2: Structured | Level 3: Machine-Consumable |
|------------|----------------------|-------------------|--------------------------|
| **Domain Insights** | [ ] In people's heads | [ ] Written in wiki/docs with structure | [ ] Indexed for retrieval; AI loads relevant insights before generating queries |
| **Architecture Decisions** | [ ] Verbal "we did it this way because..." | [ ] Design decisions documented with rationale | [ ] AI references architecture context when generating complex queries |
| **Interpretation Guidance** | [ ] Analysts learn through experience | [ ] Documented ("0% churn means pipeline didn't run") | [ ] AI applies interpretation rules to flag suspicious results automatically |
| **Known Gotchas** | [ ] Passed along in onboarding | [ ] Cataloged with examples | [ ] AI checks output against known gotchas before returning results |

**Current Level:** [ ] Level 1 &emsp; [ ] Level 2 &emsp; [ ] Level 3

**Key Gaps:**


---

### 4. Memory — "What's the current state of this product?"

| Checkpoint | Level 1: Human-Readable | Level 2: Structured | Level 3: Machine-Consumable |
|------------|----------------------|-------------------|--------------------------|
| **Stakeholder Map** | [ ] Scattered across Slack and email | [ ] Consolidated per product | [ ] AI knows who owns what and routes questions appropriately |
| **Active Migrations** | [ ] Word of mouth | [ ] Tracked in project management tool | [ ] AI reads current state before querying; avoids deprecated tables |
| **Tool & Config State** | [ ] Tribal knowledge | [ ] Documented (warehouses, connections, environments) | [ ] AI reads config before acting; uses correct warehouses/connections |
| **Artifact Index** | [ ] Links scattered across channels | [ ] Consolidated doc index per product | [ ] AI can locate authoritative docs, dashboards, and requirements on demand |

**Current Level:** [ ] Level 1 &emsp; [ ] Level 2 &emsp; [ ] Level 3

**Key Gaps:**


---

### 5. Failure Patterns — "What's gone wrong before?"

| Checkpoint | Level 1: Human-Readable | Level 2: Structured | Level 3: Machine-Consumable |
|------------|----------------------|-------------------|--------------------------|
| **Incident Records** | [ ] Verbal "we got burned" stories | [ ] Logged with date, root cause, impact | [ ] Incidents queryable; AI references them when working in affected areas |
| **Prevention Rules** | [ ] Not documented | [ ] Written per incident ("always use convert_tz()") | [ ] Prevention rules injected into AI context automatically |
| **Anti-Patterns** | [ ] Discovered by trial and error | [ ] Cataloged with examples of wrong vs. right | [ ] AI validates its own output against anti-patterns before returning results |
| **Recurrence Tracking** | [ ] No tracking | [ ] Occurrence counts maintained | [ ] Systemic patterns trigger automated alerts and priority escalation |

**Current Level:** [ ] Level 1 &emsp; [ ] Level 2 &emsp; [ ] Level 3

**Key Gaps:**

# LLM Eval Workflow

## Core Concepts

**Golden dataset** — a file of saved test cases. Each row has an input, an expected output, axial codes (your eval dimensions), pass/fail labels, failure notes, and promoted traces (real production failures added manually).

**Prompt changes** — anything that mutates model behavior: system prompt, CLAUDE.md, few-shot examples, tool definitions, output format instructions. All treated like code changes — version controlled, eval run before deployment.

**Offline evals** — run before deployment, triggered manually by a change (prompt, model, code). You control when it runs. Input is your golden dataset. Purpose: catch regressions before they ship.

**Online evals** — run automatically in production against live traffic. Input is real requests. Purpose: catch drift after they ship.

> The tests themselves are identical — same axial codes, same judge skill, same scoring rubric. The only difference is when and how they're triggered, and what data they run against.

| | Offline | Online |
|---|---|---|
| **Triggered by** | You, manually | Production traffic, automatically |
| **Input** | Golden dataset | Real requests |
| **Purpose** | Did my change break something? | Is something breaking in the real world? |

---

## Types of Evals

| Type | Question it answers | When you run it |
|---|---|---|
| Unit tests | Does this specific behavior work correctly? | Every prompt change |
| Regression | Did I break something that used to work? | Every prompt/model change |
| Behavioral | Does the model follow instructions consistently? | When adding new capabilities |
| Adversarial | Can edge cases break it? | Before major releases |
| A/B | Is version B actually better than version A? | When comparing two candidates |
| Online monitoring | Is quality drifting in production right now? | Continuously |

---

## Toolstack

| Tool | Owns |
|---|---|
| **Judge Skill** | LLM-as-a-judge — rubric, scoring prompt, output schema |
| **MLflow** | All traces, scores, versioning, regression comparison |
| **Golden dataset** | Ground truth inputs + expected outputs, versioned separately |

---

## What "Running Your Golden Dataset" Actually Means

A loop over your test cases. For each one: re-run the input through your current pipeline, score the output per axial code using programmatic checks or the judge skill (see Online Monitoring), log everything to MLflow with version tags.

```python
for trace in golden_dataset:
    # 1. Re-run the input through your current prompt
    actual_output = your_pipeline(trace["input"])

    # 2. Evaluate per axial code
    format_score = check_format(actual_output)         # programmatic
    accuracy_score = judge_skill(                       # LLM-as-a-judge
        input=trace["input"],
        expected=trace["expected_output"],
        actual=actual_output
    )

    # 3. Log to MLflow with version tags
    with mlflow.start_run():
        mlflow.log_params({
            "prompt_version": "v1.2",
            "dataset_version": "golden_v3",
            "judge_version": "v1.0"
        })
        mlflow.log_metrics({
            "format_score": format_score,
            "accuracy_score": accuracy_score
        })
```

---

## Regression Workflow Step by Step

1. Change something (prompt, model, tool definition)
2. Loop golden dataset through updated pipeline
3. Score each output per axial code
4. Log scores to MLflow with version tags
5. Compare run to baseline in MLflow experiment view
6. Promoted traces fail → high priority, reintroduced known bug
7. Any axial code drops → fix and re-run before shipping

### Versioning in MLflow

Three things to version independently on every run:

```python
mlflow.log_params({
    "app_prompt_version": "v2.1",
    "judge_skill_version": "v1.3",
    "dataset_version": "golden_v4"
})
```

This lets you answer: did the application prompt regress, or did the judge get stricter?

---

## Online Monitoring

Online evals use the same tests as offline — programmatic checks and LLM-as-a-judge. The difference is they run against your real production traces, not your golden dataset.

Since your traces are already logged in MLflow, you've done the hard part. What you need is:

**1. A judge skill** — takes a batch of production traces, runs your evaluators, logs scores back to MLflow.

**2. A dashboard** — MLflow's experiment view plotting your scores over time.

You call the skill whenever you want to check in on quality — after heavy usage, or after a prompt change, to see how it's performing on real inputs vs your golden dataset.

**The flow:**

```
You use your workflow (traces auto-log to MLflow)
        ↓
When you want to evaluate — call your judge skill
        ↓
Skill pulls recent unscored traces from MLflow
        ↓
Runs programmatic checks + LLM-as-a-judge per axial code
        ↓
Logs scores back to the same MLflow experiment
        ↓
View score trends in MLflow dashboard
        ↓
Drift detected? → promote trace to golden dataset, investigate offline
```

**Keep online and offline scores in the same MLflow experiment.** This lets you compare them directly:

- Offline scores high, online scores drifting down → golden dataset isn't representative enough, promote production traces into it
- Both drifting down → something in your pipeline changed, trigger a full offline regression run

**Not every check needs LLM-as-a-judge.** Only use it when the quality being measured is subjective or semantic. For structural checks use programmatic evaluators — cheaper, faster, and more reliable.

| Checking... | Evaluator |
|---|---|
| Valid JSON returned? | Programmatic |
| Right tool called? | Programmatic |
| Token usage / cost | Programmatic (MLflow logs automatically) |
| Factual accuracy? | LLM-as-a-judge |
| Tone drift? | LLM-as-a-judge |

**The judge skill** is a separate Claude call whose only job is scoring:

```python
import anthropic
import json

def judge_skill(input, actual, criteria="accuracy", expected=None):
    client = anthropic.Anthropic()
    response = client.messages.create(
        model="claude-sonnet-4-20250514",
        max_tokens=1000,
        system="""You are an evaluation judge.
Score the response 1-5 on the given criteria and return JSON only:
{"score": int, "reasoning": str}""",
        messages=[{
            "role": "user",
            "content": f"Criteria: {criteria}\nInput: {input}\nExpected: {expected or 'N/A'}\nActual: {actual}"
        }]
    )
    return json.loads(response.content[0].text)
```

Note: online traces won't always have an expected output (unlike golden dataset rows) — the judge scores quality on criteria alone.



---

## The Feedback Loop

Online evals surface failure patterns your golden dataset doesn't cover. Those new cases get **promoted into the golden dataset**. Your golden dataset grows more robust over time and your offline evals get harder to pass — which is exactly what you want.

```
Production failure detected (online)
        ↓
Add to golden dataset as promoted trace
        ↓
Offline evals now test for this case on every future change
        ↓
Golden dataset compounds in quality over time
```

# Confluence Workflow

## Always Read Before Updating

Before updating any Confluence page, always read it first via `mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_get_page` to get:
1. The current version number (required for update — must increment by 1)
2. The existing HTML body (to merge changes, not overwrite)

Never blindly overwrite a page. Read, merge, then update.

## Use Storage Format HTML

All page content must be valid Confluence storage format XHTML. Use the templates in `references/confluence-page-templates.md` for structure. Key rules:
- Use `ac:structured-macro` for TOC, details, expand, status, note, code blocks
- Use blue-highlighted headers (`highlight-#0065ff`) with white text for table header rows
- Use `<h2>` for main sections, `<h3>` for subsections, `<h4>` for table headings
- Use `class="wrapped relative-table"` with `<colgroup>` for all tables
- Include `<p class="auto-cursor-target"><br /></p>` for paragraph spacing

## Table Construction

- Always define column widths via `<colgroup>` with percentage-based `<col style="width: X%;">`
- For auto-numbered tables, add `data-snooker-col-series="numbers"` and `data-snooker-locked-cols="0"` to the `<table>` tag
- Numbering column cells need: `class="numberingColumn" contenteditable="false" data-mce-resize="false"`

## CSV-to-Table Workflow

When building a design doc mappings table from a CSV or TSV file:
1. Read the file with pandas (check encoding — UTF-16 tab-separated is common for exports)
2. Map columns to the standard 5-column format: #, Field Name, Data Type, Sample Values, Definition
3. Generate storage format HTML using the auto-numbered table template
4. Each row gets a `numberingColumn` cell with the row number

## Page Templates

Before creating a new page, read `references/confluence-page-templates.md` and `memory/tools/confluence.md` for:
- HTML templates (requirements page, design doc, mappings table)
- MCP tool names and parameters
- Space keys and parent page IDs

## Space Default

Default space is **DSSDSA** unless the user specifies otherwise.

# Evals Workflow

## Reference Guide

Before any eval-related work (designing evals, building golden datasets, writing rubrics, validating judges, measuring system performance, or discussing eval strategy), always read `~/.claude/references/ai-evals-reference.md` first. Apply its frameworks, terminology, and phased approach.

This includes work on the user's personal operating system (OS) — measuring and evaluating its performance over time.

## Golden Dataset Updates

When tagging a new failure pattern or identifying a strong passing trace, also add an eval record to `evals/golden-dataset.json`:

1. Run: `python3 ~/.claude/scripts/add-eval-record.py --session-id <id> --pass-fail <Pass|Fail> --summary "..." --axial-code <code> --feature-category "..." --feature-use-case "..." [fail/pass-specific flags]`
2. All 19 fields must be populated — the script validates required fields based on pass/fail status
3. For Fail records: `--severity`, `--prevention-rule`, `--failure-mode`, and `--failure-note` are required
4. For Pass records: `--passing-note` is required
5. Valid axial codes: commit_discipline, knowledge_consultation, proactive_compliance, output_fidelity, intent_comprehension, diagnostic_reasoning, error_recovery
6. After adding, commit and push per the auto-commit rule

# Marp Workflow

## Always Use Rose Pine Dawn Theme

Before running any Marp build command, read `memory/tools/marp.md` for the correct build command and flags.

Every Marp build must use the patched Rose Pine Dawn theme:

```bash
marp ~/.claude/SLIDES.md --no-stdin --theme-set ~/rose-pine-dawn-fixed.css -o <output> 2>&1
```

Required flags:
- `--no-stdin` — prevents Marp from hanging
- `--theme-set ~/rose-pine-dawn-fixed.css` — loads the patched Rose Pine Dawn theme

Never omit `--theme-set`. Never guess theme paths. The theme file is at `~/rose-pine-dawn-fixed.css`.

For PPTX output, add `--pptx`. For HTML, the default output is HTML.

# MLflow Workflow

## Trace Search

When searching MLflow traces for specific content (prompts, URLs, keywords), always query SQLite directly (`sqlite3 ~/mlflow.db "SELECT ... FROM trace_request_metadata WHERE value LIKE ..."`) instead of the MLflow Python SDK. Reserve the SDK only for programmatic operations (tagging, exporting).

## Prevention Rule Drafting

When tagging a failure, draft the prevention rule using conversation context. Present the draft for user confirmation before writing. Rules must be:

- **Specific** — references the exact mistake and context, not generic advice
- **Actionable** — describes what to do differently, not just "be careful"
- **Testable** — another person could verify compliance
- **Includes trigger** — mentions what situation activates the rule

BAD: "Double-check your response before submitting."
GOOD: "When querying spreadsheets for team-specific data, always filter on the explicit column name (e.g., 'Team Name') rather than matching keywords across all columns."

## CSV Safety

Never run `export_traces.py` with `--days` or narrow filters to find a single trace — it overwrites the full CSV. Instead: (1) edit the CSV in place with a Python one-liner, or (2) use `--all` to preserve history. Warn the user before any re-export that it will overwrite.

## Before Any MLflow Operation

Read `~/.claude/memory/tools/mlflow.md` for server config, scripts, CSV workflow, and trace tagging reference data.

File: scripts/lib/mcp_config.py
================
"""Load MCP server config and validate tool prefixes."""

import json
import os

# Built-in Claude Code tools (always available, no MCP config needed)
BUILTIN_TOOLS = {
    "Bash", "Write", "Read", "Glob", "Grep", "WebFetch", "WebSearch",
    "Skill", "Edit", "Task", "NotebookEdit", "AskUserQuestion",
    "EnterPlanMode", "ExitPlanMode", "TodoWrite", "TodoRead",
    "TaskCreate", "TaskUpdate", "TaskGet", "TaskList", "Agent",
}

# User-level MCP servers not in mcp.json (configured via `claude mcp add`)
USER_LEVEL_SERVERS = {"notion"}

# Tools that reference user-level servers — warn instead of fail
USER_LEVEL_PREFIXES = {"mcp__notion__"}

# Known MCP tools that may not be installed — warn instead of fail
OPTIONAL_PREFIXES = {"mcp__figma-desktop__", "mcp__figma__"}


def load_mcp_servers(mcp_json_path: str | None = None) -> dict:
    """Parse ~/.claude/mcp.json and return the mcpServers dict."""
    if mcp_json_path is None:
        mcp_json_path = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/mcp.json")

    try:
        with open(mcp_json_path) as f:
            data = json.load(f)
    except (OSError, IOError, json.JSONDecodeError):
        return {}

    return data.get("mcpServers", {})


def get_configured_tool_prefixes(mcp_json_path: str | None = None) -> set[str]:
    """Return set of MCP tool prefixes like {'mcp__jira__', 'mcp__universal-doc__', ...}.

    Includes both mcp.json servers and user-level servers (Notion).
    """
    servers = load_mcp_servers(mcp_json_path)
    prefixes = set()
    for name in servers:
        # MCP tool names use the pattern mcp__{server-name}__
        prefixes.add(f"mcp__{name}__")

    # Add user-level servers
    for name in USER_LEVEL_SERVERS:
        prefixes.add(f"mcp__{name}__")

    return prefixes


def classify_tool(tool_name: str, configured_prefixes: set[str] | None = None) -> str:
    """Classify a tool reference.

    Returns one of: "builtin", "configured", "user_level", "optional", "unknown"
    """
    if tool_name in BUILTIN_TOOLS:
        return "builtin"

    if configured_prefixes is None:
        configured_prefixes = get_configured_tool_prefixes()

    # Check if tool matches a configured MCP server prefix
    for prefix in configured_prefixes:
        if tool_name.startswith(prefix):
            return "configured"

    # Check user-level prefixes (warn, not fail)
    for prefix in USER_LEVEL_PREFIXES:
        if tool_name.startswith(prefix):
            return "user_level"

    # Check optional/known-missing prefixes
    for prefix in OPTIONAL_PREFIXES:
        if tool_name.startswith(prefix):
            return "optional"

    # Skill tool references (e.g., "Notion:notion-search")
    if ":" in tool_name and not tool_name.startswith("mcp__"):
        return "builtin"

    return "unknown"

================
File: scripts/add-eval-record.py
================
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Add a new eval record to the golden dataset JSON.

Usage:
    python3 add-eval-record.py --session-id <id> --pass-fail <Pass|Fail> --summary "..." [options]

Required fields are validated based on pass/fail status. Auto-derivable fields
(cost_usd, turn_count) default to empty if not supplied.
"""

import argparse
import json
import os
import sys
from datetime import datetime

DATASET_PATH = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/evals/golden-dataset.json")

VALID_AXIAL_CODES = [
    "commit_discipline",
    "knowledge_consultation",
    "proactive_compliance",
    "output_fidelity",
    "intent_comprehension",
    "diagnostic_reasoning",
    "error_recovery",
]

VALID_FEATURE_CATEGORIES = [
    "Jira",
    "Teams",
    "Airtable",
    "Google Workspace",
    "MLflow",
    "Memory",
    "System Maintenance",
    "Databricks",
    "Outlook",
    "Confluence",
    "Evals",
    "General",
]


def build_parser():
    p = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Add an eval record to golden-dataset.json")

    # Always required
    p.add_argument("--session-id", required=True, help="Session UUID")
    p.add_argument("--pass-fail", required=True, choices=["Pass", "Fail"], help="Pass or Fail")
    p.add_argument("--summary", required=True, help="One-line session summary")
    p.add_argument("--axial-code", required=True, choices=VALID_AXIAL_CODES, help="Axial code")
    p.add_argument("--feature-category", required=True, help="Feature category")
    p.add_argument("--feature-use-case", required=True, help="Feature use case description")

    # Conditionally required (validated after parsing)
    p.add_argument("--severity", choices=["high", "medium", "low"], help="Failure severity (required for Fail)")
    p.add_argument("--prevention-rule", help="Prevention rule text (required for Fail)")
    p.add_argument("--failure-mode", help="Failure mode tag (required for Fail)")
    p.add_argument("--failure-note", help="Evaluative paragraph for failures (required for Fail)")
    p.add_argument("--passing-note", help="Evaluative paragraph for passes (required for Pass)")

    # Auto-derivable / optional
    p.add_argument("--date", default=datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d"), help="Session date (default: today)")
    p.add_argument("--cost-usd", default="", help="Session cost in USD")
    p.add_argument("--model", default="claude-opus-4-6", help="Model used (default: claude-opus-4-6)")
    p.add_argument("--source-system", default="claude_code", help="Source system (default: claude_code)")
    p.add_argument("--turn-count", default="", help="Number of turns")
    p.add_argument("--selection-reason", default="", help="Why this session was selected")
    p.add_argument("--golden-candidate", default="No", choices=["Yes", "No"], help="Golden candidate (default: No)")
    p.add_argument("--borderline", default="No", choices=["Yes", "No"], help="Borderline (default: No)")

    return p


def validate_conditional_fields(args):
    """Validate fields required based on pass/fail status."""
    errors = []

    if args.pass_fail == "Fail":
        if not args.severity:
            errors.append("--severity is required for Fail records")
        if not args.prevention_rule:
            errors.append("--prevention-rule is required for Fail records")
        if not args.failure_mode:
            errors.append("--failure-mode is required for Fail records")
        if not args.failure_note:
            errors.append("--failure-note is required for Fail records")

    if args.pass_fail == "Pass":
        if not args.passing_note:
            errors.append("--passing-note is required for Pass records")

    return errors


def main():
    parser = build_parser()
    args = parser.parse_args()

    errors = validate_conditional_fields(args)
    if errors:
        for e in errors:
            print(f"Error: {e}", file=sys.stderr)
        sys.exit(1)

    # Load existing dataset
    try:
        with open(DATASET_PATH) as f:
            dataset = json.load(f)
    except (OSError, json.JSONDecodeError) as e:
        print(f"Error reading {DATASET_PATH}: {e}", file=sys.stderr)
        sys.exit(1)

    # Check for duplicate session_id
    existing_ids = {r["session_id"] for r in dataset["records"]}
    if args.session_id in existing_ids:
        print(f"Error: session_id {args.session_id} already exists in dataset", file=sys.stderr)
        sys.exit(1)

    # Build record
    record = {
        "session_id": args.session_id,
        "date": args.date,
        "cost_usd": args.cost_usd,
        "model": args.model,
        "summary": args.summary,
        "source_system": args.source_system,
        "turn_count": args.turn_count,
        "severity": args.severity or "",
        "prevention_rule": args.prevention_rule or "",
        "failure_mode": args.failure_mode or "",
        "selection_reason": args.selection_reason,
        "pass_fail": args.pass_fail,
        "failure_note": args.failure_note or "",
        "passing_note": args.passing_note or "",
        "axial_code": args.axial_code,
        "golden_candidate": args.golden_candidate,
        "borderline": args.borderline,
        "feature_category": args.feature_category,
        "feature_use_case": args.feature_use_case,
    }

    dataset["records"].append(record)

    # Write back
    with open(DATASET_PATH, "w") as f:
        json.dump(dataset, f, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False)
        f.write("\n")

    count = len(dataset["records"])
    print(f"Added {args.pass_fail} record for {args.session_id} ({count} total records)")
    return 0


if __name__ == "__main__":
    sys.exit(main())

================
File: scripts/build-lessons-index.sh
================
#!/bin/bash
# Build a compact lessons index for SessionStart injection.
# Extracts title + "The Lesson" one-liner from each lessons/*.md file.
# Only includes lessons with status: active.

LESSONS_DIR="$HOME/.claude/lessons"

if [ ! -d "$LESSONS_DIR" ] || [ -z "$(ls -A "$LESSONS_DIR"/*.md 2>/dev/null)" ]; then
  echo "(no lessons recorded)"
  exit 0
fi

total=0
output=""

for file in "$LESSONS_DIR"/*.md; do
  domain=$(basename "$file" .md)
  file_lessons=""
  current_title=""
  in_lesson_section=false
  skip=false

  while IFS= read -r line; do
    # Detect lesson title (# Title, not ## subsection, not file header like "# Claude Code Lessons")
    # Must capture BASH_REMATCH before other regex tests overwrite it
    if [[ "$line" =~ ^#\ (.+)$ ]]; then
      captured="${BASH_REMATCH[1]}"
      if [[ ! "$line" =~ ^##\  ]] && [[ ! "$captured" =~ Lessons$ ]]; then
        current_title="$captured"
        in_lesson_section=false
        skip=false
      fi
    fi

    # Check for deprecated status — skip this lesson
    if [[ "$line" =~ ^"**status:**".*deprecated ]]; then
      skip=true
      current_title=""
    fi

    # Detect "## The Lesson" section
    if [[ "$line" == "## The Lesson" ]]; then
      in_lesson_section=true
      continue
    fi

    # If we're in The Lesson section, grab the first non-empty line
    if $in_lesson_section && [ -n "$line" ] && [[ ! "$line" =~ ^## ]] && ! $skip; then
      # Truncate to first sentence if very long
      lesson_text="$line"
      if [ ${#lesson_text} -gt 200 ]; then
        lesson_text="${lesson_text:0:197}..."
      fi
      file_lessons="${file_lessons}- **${current_title}**: ${lesson_text}\n"
      total=$((total + 1))
      in_lesson_section=false
    fi

    # Stop reading The Lesson on next section header
    if $in_lesson_section && [[ "$line" =~ ^## ]] && [[ "$line" != "## The Lesson" ]]; then
      in_lesson_section=false
    fi
  done < "$file"

  if [ -n "$file_lessons" ]; then
    output="${output}\n## ${domain}.md\n${file_lessons}"
  fi
done

file_count=$(ls -1 "$LESSONS_DIR"/*.md 2>/dev/null | wc -l | tr -d ' ')
echo "${total} lessons across ${file_count} file(s)"
echo -e "$output"

Agent-friendly Confluence CLI with structured JSON output. Pages, spaces, CQL search, comments, attachments, labels, templates.

## Quick Reference

```bash
# Pages
confluence --agent page get 12345678

confluence --agent page versions 12345678

confluence --agent page compare-versions --id 12345678 --v1 2 --v2 3

# Spaces
confluence --agent space list --limit 10
confluence --agent space get DEV

# Search (CQL)
confluence --agent search query --cql "text ~ 'deployment guide'" --limit 5
confluence --agent search query --cql "space = DEV AND type = page AND title ~ 'release'" --limit 10

# Comments
confluence --agent comment list 12345678
confluence --agent comment add --page-id 12345678 --body "Comment text"

confluence --agent label remove --page-id 12345678 --label outdated

# Users
confluence --agent user me
```

## CQL Query Syntax

```
text ~ "search term"                              # full-text search
space = DEV AND type = page                       # filter by space and type
title ~ "release notes" AND lastModified > now("-7d")  # recent pages
label = "important" AND space = DEV               # by label
creator = currentUser() ORDER BY lastModified DESC     # my pages
```

## Tips

- Always use `--agent` for structured JSON output
- Use `--limit N` to control response size
- CQL is Confluence Query Language (similar to JQL)
- Run `confluence agent schema` for full command/flag reference

---
name: teams-cli
version: 0.3.1
description: >
  Microsoft Teams CLI for chats, channels, messages, meetings, people search,
  activity, favorites, and transcripts. Hybrid Graph + internal APIs via browser
  token capture. Use when user asks about Teams chats, channels, messages,
  meetings, or people.
metadata:
  requires:
    bins: ["teams"]
---

# Microsoft Teams CLI

Agent-friendly Teams CLI with structured JSON output. Hybrid Graph API + internal Teams APIs.

## Authentication

```bash
teams auth login       # Microsoft browser token capture (Graph + Skype + Substrate + CSA)
teams auth status      # Check current tokens
teams auth logout      # Clear stored tokens
```

## Quick Reference

```bash
# Chats
teams --agent chat list --limit 10
teams --agent chat get <chat-id>
teams --agent chat members <chat-id>
teams --agent chat get-chat --user-id "8:orgid:<guid>"    # 1:1 chat by user
teams --agent chat create-group --members "user1@,user2@" --topic "Project"
teams --agent chat favorites
teams --agent chat activity
teams --agent chat saved

# Channels (Teams & Channels)
teams --agent channel teams                                # list all teams + channels
teams --agent channel list --team-id <team-id>
teams --agent channel get --team-id <id> --channel-id <id>
teams --agent channel messages --team-id <id> --channel-id <id>
teams --agent channel send --team-id <id> --channel-id <id> --content "Hello"
teams --agent channel members --team-id <id> --channel-id <id>
teams --agent channel tags --team-id <id>
teams --agent channel files --team-id <id> --channel-id <id>

# Messages
teams --agent message list --chat-id <chat-id>
teams --agent message send --chat-id <id> --content "Hello"
teams --agent message edit --chat-id <id> --message-id <id> --content "Updated"
teams --agent message delete --chat-id <id> --message-id <id>
teams --agent message react --chat-id <id> --message-id <id> --emoji like
teams --agent message mark-read --chat-id <id> --message-id <id>

# Meetings
teams --agent meeting list --days 7
teams --agent meeting get <meeting-id>
teams --agent meeting transcript --thread-id "19:meeting_xxx@thread.v2"

# People
teams --agent people search --query "John"
teams --agent people frequent

# Search (via Substrate)
teams --agent search messages --query "project update"
teams --agent search emails --query "quarterly report"
teams --agent search channels --query "general"

# User
teams --agent user me
teams --agent user get <user-id>
teams --agent user presence
```

## Hybrid Usage

This CLI is used alongside MCP Teams tools in a **hybrid** setup:

- **CLI handles**: writes (send, reply, delete, edit), lookups (people, channels, meetings, favorites, user)
- **MCP handles**: search (`mcp__teams__teams_search` — has messageLink, conversationId, content) and activity feed (`mcp__teams__teams_get_activity` — has mention type filtering)

The CLI search (`teams --agent search messages`) does not return `messageLink`, `conversationId`, or message `content` — so MCP is still required for search-dependent workflows (mentions catch-up, topic conversations).

### MRI Construction for @Mentions

People search returns a GUID `id` field. Construct the MRI for @mentions as: `8:orgid:{id}`

Example: `teams --agent people search --query "Stephen Massa"` returns `id: "89137a4f-..."` → MRI is `8:orgid:89137a4f-...`

Use in messages: `@[Massa, Stephen](8:orgid:89137a4f-...)`

## Tips

- Always use `--agent` for structured JSON output
- Add `--full` to preserve all API fields (including nulls)
- Auth auto-triggers on first use — browser captures multiple token types
- Uses internal APIs (chatsvc, CSA, Substrate) for features not in Graph API
- Use `--limit N` to control response size
- Run `teams agent schema` for full command/flag reference

================
File: skills/teams-thread/SKILL.md
================
---
name: teams-thread
description: Create a Teams channel thread with a reply and tagged people, with self-notes preview before posting
allowed-tools:
  - Bash
  - mcp__teams__teams_search
  - AskUserQuestion
---

# Teams Thread Creator

Create a new thread in a Teams channel with a reply body and tagged people, previewing in self-notes before posting.

Uses **hybrid CLI + MCP**: CLI (`teams --agent`) for writes/lookups, MCP for search only.

## Workflow

### Step 1: Gather inputs

Ask the user (via AskUserQuestion or from their message) for:

1. **Channel** — which Teams channel to post in (e.g. "acq-fivetran-migration-public")
2. **Thread title** — the root post text (e.g. "[Hulu Media360 - SSNT, SS, Devices, SFTP vs. Email]")
3. **Reply body** — the message to post as a reply in the thread
4. **People to tag** — names of people to cc in the reply

If the user provides all of these upfront, skip asking.

### Step 2: Resolve channel

Use CLI to list all teams and channels, then match by name:

```bash
teams --agent channel teams
```

Extract the `teamId` and `channelId` for the matching channel.

### Step 3: Resolve people

Use CLI to look up each person:

```bash
teams --agent people search --query "Seth Newman"
```

Construct MRI from the `id` field: `8:orgid:{id}`

Present the resolved names and emails to the user for confirmation:

> Confirming these are the right people:
> 1. Newman, Seth (Seth.Newman@disney.com)
> 2. Chan, Christine (Christine.Chan@disney.com)
>
> Correct?

Wait for user confirmation before proceeding.

### Step 4: Preview in self-notes

Send the **reply message** (body + cc: @mentions) to self-notes so the user can verify formatting:

```bash
teams --agent message send --chat-id "48:notes" --content "<content>" --content-type html
```

Tell the user:

> Test message sent to your self-notes. Check it in Teams (search "Notes" in your chat list). Do the @mentions render correctly?

Wait for user confirmation before proceeding.

### Step 5: Post to channel

Once the user approves:

1. **Send thread title** as a plain-text root message to the channel:
   ```bash
   teams --agent channel send --team-id <team-id> --channel-id <channel-id> --content "<title>"
   ```

2. **Reply with body + tags** using the root message's ID:
   ```bash
   teams --agent channel reply --team-id <team-id> --channel-id <channel-id> --message-id <root-msg-id> --content "<body + cc>"
   ```

The reply format:
```
{reply body}

cc: @[Name1](mri) @[Name2](mri) ...
```

Where `mri` is `8:orgid:{id}` from the people search result.

### Step 6: Share link

Build and share the thread link:
```
https://teams.microsoft.com/l/message/{channelId}/{serverMessageId}?tenantId=56b731a8-a2ac-4c32-bf6b-616810e913c6
```

## Rules

- **Never bold the thread title** — send as plain text, no markdown formatting
- **Never use `message edit` for @mentions** — it renders them as raw text. If a message needs fixing, delete and re-send
- **Always prefix tags with "cc: "** — e.g. `cc: @[Newman, Seth](8:orgid:abc-123)`
- **Always confirm people before posting** — show resolved names/emails and wait for approval
- **Always preview in self-notes first** — never post directly to the channel without user verifying the test message
- **Always @mention people by name** — look up via `teams --agent people search`, construct MRI as `8:orgid:{id}`, use `@[Name](mri)` syntax

## Examples

### Example 1: Full Thread with Tags

**User**: "Create a thread in acq-fivetran-migration-public titled [Hulu Media360 - SSNT] with body 'Meeting set for tomorrow' and tag Seth and Christine"

**Claude does**:
1. Runs `teams --agent channel teams` → finds channelId for acq-fivetran-migration-public
2. Runs `teams --agent people search --query "Seth Newman"` and `--query "Christine Chan"` → shows names/emails → waits for confirmation
3. Sends to 48:notes via `teams --agent message send`: `Meeting set for tomorrow\n\ncc: @[Newman, Seth](8:orgid:...) @[Chan, Christine](8:orgid:...)`
4. Waits for user to verify in Teams
5. Posts thread title via `teams --agent channel send` → replies via `teams --agent channel reply`
6. Shares thread link

### Example 2: Thread Without Tags

**User**: "Post a thread in data-engineering-public titled 'Airflow DAG Maintenance Window' with body 'DAGs paused Friday 6-8pm PT for infra upgrade. No action needed.'"

**Claude does**:
1. Runs `teams --agent channel teams` → finds channelId
2. No people to tag → skips people resolution
3. Sends to 48:notes via `teams --agent message send`
4. Waits for user to verify in Teams
5. Posts thread title via `teams --agent channel send` → replies with body via `teams --agent channel reply`
6. Shares thread link

# Universal Document CLI

Agent-friendly document CLI with structured JSON output. Multi-provider: `--provider google|microsoft|local`.

## Quick Reference

```bash
# Documents
udoc --agent doc read <doc-id>
udoc --agent doc create --title "New Doc" --content "Hello"
udoc --agent doc update --id <id> --content "Updated content"
udoc --agent doc delete <id>
udoc --agent doc metadata <id>
udoc --agent doc copy --id <id> --title "Copy of Doc"
udoc --agent doc download --id <id> --output ./local.pdf
udoc --agent doc upload --path ./report.pdf

# Spreadsheets
udoc --agent sheet read-range --id <sheet-id> --range "A1:D10"
udoc --agent sheet write-range --id <sheet-id> --range "A1:C3" --data '[[1,2,3],[4,5,6]]'
udoc --agent sheet append --id <sheet-id> --range "A1" --data '[[7,8,9]]'
udoc --agent sheet clear --id <sheet-id> --range "A1:D10"
udoc --agent sheet list-sheets --id <sheet-id>

# Slides
udoc --agent slide list --id <presentation-id>
udoc --agent slide get --id <presentation-id> --slide-index 0

# Search
udoc --agent search documents --query "report" --limit 10
udoc --agent search recent --limit 10

# Folders
udoc --agent folder list <folder-id>
udoc --agent folder create --name "New Folder"

# Sharing
udoc --agent share share --id <id> --email user@example.com --role reader
udoc --agent share permissions --id <id>

# Comments & Revisions
udoc --agent comment list <id>
udoc --agent comment add --id <id> --content "Review"
udoc --agent revision list <id>

# Batch Operations
udoc --agent batch read --ids "id1,id2,id3"
udoc --agent batch metadata --ids "id1,id2"

# Health
udoc --agent health check
```

## Tips

- Always use `--agent` for structured JSON output
- Use `--provider google|microsoft|local` to select backend (default: google)
- Use `--limit N` to control response size
- Run `udoc agent schema` for full command/flag reference

# Databricks Troubleshooting Patterns

## Authentication Issues

### Token expired
**Symptom**: CLI commands return `Error: token expired` or HTTP 401
**Fix**: `databricks auth login --host https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com`
**Note**: Cannot be automated — requires browser SSO

### Wrong workspace
**Symptom**: Tables/pipelines not found, permission denied
**Check**: Verify `DATABRICKS_HOST` matches the intended workspace
**Fix**: Set correct host or use `--profile` flag

### Token cache corrupted
**Symptom**: Auth login succeeds but subsequent commands fail
**Fix**: Clear cache: `rm -rf ~/.databricks/token-cache.json` then re-auth

## Pipeline Issues

### Pipeline shows FAILED
**Debug steps**:
1. Get pipeline: `databricks pipelines get <id> --output json`
2. List updates: `databricks pipelines list-updates <id> --output json`
3. Get latest update: `databricks pipelines get-update <id> --update-id <latest_update_id> --output json`
4. Check `cause` field in the update's events for error details

### Pipeline stuck in STARTING
**Possible causes**: Cluster provisioning delays, resource constraints
**Check**: Look at update events for provisioning status

## Unity Catalog Issues

### Table not found
**Debug steps**:
1. Verify catalog exists: `databricks unity-catalog catalogs list --output json`
2. Verify schema: `databricks unity-catalog schemas list --catalog-name <catalog> --output json`
3. Check permissions: user may not have access to the catalog/schema

### Permission denied on catalog
**Check**: Verify user groups in workspace-config.md match the catalog's grants
**Common fix**: Request access through the appropriate Databricks admin

## SQL Query Issues

### Warehouse is STOPPED
**Symptom**: Query hangs or returns warehouse unavailable error
**Fix**: Use the Default Unity SQL Endpoint (`b682b4d44313d3a4`) which is typically RUNNING
**Note**: Stopped warehouses require manual start by workspace admins

### Query timeout
**Symptom**: run-query.sh exits after 120s with "still running"
**Fix**: Check the statement status manually:
```bash
curl -s -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
  "$HOST/api/2.0/sql/statements/<statement_id>"
```
Consider adding LIMIT to reduce result set size.

# Universal CLI Dispatcher

Routes commands to native CLI tools and external plugins with automatic auth injection.

## Quick Reference

```bash
unvrs install gh

unvrs databricks clusters list --output json

```

## Available Plugins

| Plugin | Binary | Install |
|--------|--------|---------|
| databricks | `databricks` | `brew install databricks/tap/databricks` |
| gh | `gh` | `brew install gh` |
| ldcli | `ldcli` | `brew tap launchdarkly/homebrew-tap && brew install ldcli` |
| terraform | `terraform` | `brew install hashicorp/tap/terraform` |

## Tips

- Plugins defined as TOML manifests in `plugins/` directory
- Auth auto-injected from pat-manager if configured
- Use `unvrs --list` to see what's installed

File: hooks/capture-cost.py

#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Stop hook: parse transcript JSONL to capture per-session cost and tag MLflow trace."""

import csv
import glob
import json
import os
import subprocess
import sys
import time
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

MLFLOW_TRACKING_URI = "http://127.0.0.1:5001"
COST_LOG_PATH = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/cost-log.csv")
LAST_SESSION_PATH = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/.last-session.md")

# Bedrock pricing per 1M tokens (USD)
# Update these if pricing changes
PRICING = {
    "claude-opus-4-6": {
        "input": 15.00,
        "output": 75.00,
        "cache_write": 18.75,
        "cache_read": 1.50,
    },
    "claude-sonnet-4-6": {
        "input": 3.00,
        "output": 15.00,
        "cache_write": 3.75,
        "cache_read": 0.30,
    },
    "claude-haiku-4-5": {
        "input": 0.80,
        "output": 4.00,
        "cache_write": 1.00,
        "cache_read": 0.08,
    },
}

# Fallback: use opus pricing if model unknown
DEFAULT_PRICING = PRICING["claude-opus-4-6"]

# Validation thresholds
LOW_TOKEN_THRESHOLD = 10
COST_ANOMALY_MULTIPLIER = 3
COST_ROLLING_DAYS = 7
COST_MIN_ROWS_FOR_ANOMALY = 5


def notify(title, body=""):
    """Send a macOS notification."""
    short = body[:200].replace('"', '\\"').replace("\n", " ") if body else ""
    try:
        subprocess.run(
            ["osascript", "-e",
             f'display notification "{short}" with title "Claude Code" subtitle "{title}"'],
            capture_output=True, timeout=5,
        )
    except (FileNotFoundError, subprocess.TimeoutExpired):
        pass


def parse_transcript(transcript_path):
    """Parse a single JSONL transcript file and return aggregated token counts and model."""
    totals = {
        "input_tokens": 0,
        "output_tokens": 0,
        "cache_read": 0,
        "cache_write": 0,
    }
    models = set()

    try:
        with open(transcript_path) as f:
            for line in f:
                try:
                    entry = json.loads(line)
                except json.JSONDecodeError:
                    continue
                if entry.get("type") != "assistant":
                    continue
                msg = entry.get("message") or {}
                usage = msg.get("usage") or {}
                totals["input_tokens"] += usage.get("input_tokens", 0)
                totals["output_tokens"] += usage.get("output_tokens", 0)
                totals["cache_write"] += usage.get("cache_creation_input_tokens", 0)
                totals["cache_read"] += usage.get("cache_read_input_tokens", 0)
                model = msg.get("model")
                if model:
                    models.add(model)
    except (OSError, IOError) as e:
        print(f"capture-cost: error reading {transcript_path}: {e}", file=sys.stderr)

    return totals, models


def compute_cost(totals, model_name):
    """Compute USD cost from token counts and model pricing."""
    # Match model name to pricing (prefix match for versioned names)
    prices = DEFAULT_PRICING
    for key, p in PRICING.items():
        if key in model_name:
            prices = p
            break

    cost = (
        totals["input_tokens"] * prices["input"] / 1_000_000
        + totals["output_tokens"] * prices["output"] / 1_000_000
        + totals["cache_write"] * prices["cache_write"] / 1_000_000
        + totals["cache_read"] * prices["cache_read"] / 1_000_000
    )
    return round(cost, 4)


def detect_source_system():
    """Detect whether this is a Cortex Code or Claude Code session."""
    # Check for Cortex Code environment variable
    if os.environ.get("CORTEX_SESSION_ID"):
        return {
            "system_source": "cortex_code",
            "tool_context": "mcp_bash_snowflake_local", 
            "session_type": "cli_interactive"
        }
    else:
        return {
            "system_source": "claude_code",
            "tool_context": "web_claude_tools",
            "session_type": "web_chat"
        }


def sweep_untagged_traces(mlflow, fallback_source_tags):
    """Tag orphaned last-traces from prior sessions.

    The stop hook races with MLflow's final trace write, so the last trace in
    each session is often missed.  For each untagged trace, look up a tagged
    sibling in the same session and copy its tags.  If no sibling exists (single-
    trace session), apply fallback_source_tags so at least source_system is set.
    """
    import sqlite3

    db_path = os.path.expanduser("~/mlflow.db")
    if not os.path.isfile(db_path):
        return

    try:
        conn = sqlite3.connect(db_path, timeout=5)
        # Find traces that have no system_source tag
        untagged = conn.execute("""
            SELECT ti.request_id, tm.value AS session_id
            FROM trace_info ti
            JOIN trace_request_metadata tm
              ON ti.request_id = tm.request_id AND tm.key = 'mlflow.trace.session'
            WHERE ti.request_id NOT IN (
                SELECT request_id FROM trace_tags WHERE key = 'system_source'
            )
        """).fetchall()

        if not untagged:
            conn.close()
            return

        tagged_count = 0
        for request_id, session_id in untagged:
            # Find a tagged sibling in the same session to copy tags from
            sibling_tags = conn.execute("""
                SELECT tt.key, tt.value
                FROM trace_tags tt
                JOIN trace_request_metadata tm
                  ON tt.request_id = tm.request_id AND tm.key = 'mlflow.trace.session'
                WHERE tm.value = ?
                  AND tt.request_id != ?
                  AND tt.key NOT IN ('mlflow.artifactLocation', 'mlflow.trace.spansLocation', 'mlflow.traceName')
                LIMIT 20
            """, (session_id, request_id)).fetchall()

            if sibling_tags:
                tags_to_apply = dict(sibling_tags)
            else:
                # Single-trace session with no tagged sibling — apply minimal tags
                tags_to_apply = fallback_source_tags

            for key, value in tags_to_apply.items():
                try:
                    mlflow.set_trace_tag(request_id, key, value)
                except Exception:
                    pass
            tagged_count += 1

        conn.close()

        if tagged_count > 0:
            print(f"capture-cost: sweep tagged {tagged_count} orphaned trace(s)", file=sys.stderr)

    except Exception as e:
        print(f"capture-cost: sweep error: {e}", file=sys.stderr)


def main():
    try:
        data = json.load(sys.stdin)
    except (json.JSONDecodeError, EOFError):
        print("capture-cost: no valid JSON on stdin", file=sys.stderr)
        return

    session_id = data.get("session_id", "")
    transcript_path = data.get("transcript_path", "")

    if not session_id or not transcript_path:
        return

    # --- Parse main transcript + subagent transcripts ---
    totals = {"input_tokens": 0, "output_tokens": 0, "cache_read": 0, "cache_write": 0}
    all_models = set()

    # Main transcript
    t, m = parse_transcript(transcript_path)
    for k in totals:
        totals[k] += t[k]
    all_models.update(m)

    # Subagent transcripts: {session_dir}/subagents/*.jsonl
    session_dir = transcript_path.replace(".jsonl", "")
    subagent_dir = os.path.join(session_dir, "subagents")
    for sub_path in glob.glob(os.path.join(subagent_dir, "*.jsonl")):
        t, m = parse_transcript(sub_path)
        for k in totals:
            totals[k] += t[k]
        all_models.update(m)

    # Filter out synthetic/non-real model names
    real_models = {m for m in all_models if not m.startswith("<") and m != "unknown"}
    model_name = sorted(real_models)[0] if real_models else "unknown"
    cost_usd = compute_cost(totals, model_name)

    # --- Tag the MLflow trace ---
    try:
        import mlflow

        mlflow.set_tracking_uri(MLFLOW_TRACKING_URI)

        # Wait for the final trace to flush — the last conversation turn's trace
        # is written to MLflow after the stop hook fires, causing a race condition
        # where the last trace in every session is missed.
        time.sleep(2)

        df = mlflow.search_traces(
            filter_string=f"metadata.`mlflow.trace.session` = '{session_id}'",
            max_results=100,
        )

        # Detect source system and build tags once (reused for sweep too)
        source_tags = detect_source_system()
        tags = {
            "cost_usd": str(cost_usd),
            "input_tokens": str(totals["input_tokens"]),
            "output_tokens": str(totals["output_tokens"]),
            "cache_read_tokens": str(totals["cache_read"]),
            "cache_write_tokens": str(totals["cache_write"]),
            "model": model_name,
            **source_tags,
        }

        if df is not None and not df.empty:
            # Tag ALL traces in this session
            for _, row in df.iterrows():
                trace_id = str(row.get("trace_id", row.get("request_id", "")))
                if trace_id:
                    for key, value in tags.items():
                        mlflow.set_trace_tag(trace_id, key, value)
        else:
            print(f"capture-cost: no trace found for session {session_id}", file=sys.stderr)

        # --- Retroactive sweep: tag untagged last-traces from prior sessions ---
        # Each session's last trace is written after the stop hook searches,
        # so it gets missed. Find these orphans and tag them with their session's tags.
        sweep_untagged_traces(mlflow, source_tags)

    except Exception as e:
        print(f"capture-cost: MLflow error: {e}", file=sys.stderr)

    # --- Upsert to CSV log (overwrite existing row for same session_id) ---
    try:
        new_row = [
            datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S"),
            session_id,
            cost_usd,
            totals["input_tokens"],
            totals["output_tokens"],
            totals["cache_read"],
            totals["cache_write"],
            model_name,
        ]
        header = ["date", "session_id", "cost_usd", "input_tokens", "output_tokens",
                  "cache_read", "cache_write", "model"]

        # Read existing rows, replace if session_id exists
        existing = []
        replaced = False
        if os.path.exists(COST_LOG_PATH):
            with open(COST_LOG_PATH, newline="") as f:
                reader = csv.reader(f)
                file_header = next(reader, None)
                for row in reader:
                    if len(row) >= 2 and row[1] == session_id:
                        existing.append(new_row)
                        replaced = True
                    else:
                        existing.append(row)

        if not replaced:
            existing.append(new_row)

        with open(COST_LOG_PATH, "w", newline="") as f:
            writer = csv.writer(f)
            writer.writerow(header)
            writer.writerows(existing)
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"capture-cost: CSV error: {e}", file=sys.stderr)
        notify("Cost Tracking Issue", f"Failed to write cost CSV: {e}")
        return

    # --- Write session summary for next-session continuity ---
    write_last_session(transcript_path, session_id, cost_usd, model_name)

    # --- Self-validate the row we just wrote ---
    validate_and_alert(session_id, totals, cost_usd)


def write_last_session(transcript_path, session_id, cost_usd, model_name):
    """Write a session summary to .last-session.md for next-session continuity."""
    user_messages = []
    files_modified = set()

    try:
        with open(transcript_path) as f:
            for line in f:
                try:
                    entry = json.loads(line)
                except json.JSONDecodeError:
                    continue

                if entry.get("type") == "user":
                    content = entry.get("message", {}).get("content", "")
                    if isinstance(content, list):
                        content = " ".join(
                            c.get("text", "") for c in content if isinstance(c, dict)
                        )
                    text = content.strip()
                    if text:
                        user_messages.append(text[:300])

                if entry.get("type") == "assistant":
                    for block in entry.get("message", {}).get("content", []):
                        if not isinstance(block, dict):
                            continue
                        if block.get("type") == "tool_use":
                            inp = block.get("input", {})
                            fp = inp.get("file_path", "")
                            tool_name = block.get("name", "")
                            if fp and tool_name in ("Edit", "Write"):
                                files_modified.add(fp)
    except (OSError, IOError):
        return

    if not user_messages:
        return

    now = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M")
    lines = [
        f"# Last Session Summary ({now})",
        f"Session: {session_id} | Cost: ${cost_usd} | Model: {model_name}",
        "",
        "## What Was Being Worked On",
    ]
    # Use last 5 user messages as task context
    for msg in user_messages[-5:]:
        lines.append(f"- {msg.replace(chr(10), ' ')}")

    if files_modified:
        lines.append("")
        lines.append("## Files Modified")
        for fp in sorted(files_modified)[-15:]:
            lines.append(f"- `{fp}`")

    lines.append("")

    try:
        with open(LAST_SESSION_PATH, "w") as f:
            f.write("\n".join(lines))
    except OSError:
        pass


def validate_and_alert(session_id, totals, cost_usd):
    """Validate the row we just wrote and alert on anomalies."""
    warnings = []

    # Check for near-zero tokens (transcript parsing may have failed)
    if totals["input_tokens"] < LOW_TOKEN_THRESHOLD and totals["output_tokens"] < LOW_TOKEN_THRESHOLD:
        warnings.append(
            f"Cost row looks empty (input={totals['input_tokens']}, output={totals['output_tokens']}) "
            "— transcript parsing may have failed"
        )

    # Check for zero cost with non-zero tokens
    if cost_usd <= 0 and (totals["input_tokens"] > 100 or totals["output_tokens"] > 100):
        warnings.append(
            f"Cost is $0 but tokens are non-zero (in={totals['input_tokens']}, out={totals['output_tokens']}) "
            "— pricing calculation may be broken"
        )

    # Check for cost anomaly against rolling average
    try:
        if os.path.isfile(COST_LOG_PATH):
            with open(COST_LOG_PATH, newline="") as f:
                reader = csv.DictReader(f)
                rows = list(reader)
            cutoff = datetime.now() - timedelta(days=COST_ROLLING_DAYS)
            recent_costs = []
            for r in rows:
                try:
                    dt = datetime.strptime(r.get("date", ""), "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
                    c = float(r.get("cost_usd", 0))
                    if dt >= cutoff and c > 0 and r.get("session_id") != session_id:
                        recent_costs.append(c)
                except (ValueError, TypeError):
                    continue
            if len(recent_costs) >= COST_MIN_ROWS_FOR_ANOMALY and cost_usd > 0:
                avg = sum(recent_costs) / len(recent_costs)
                if cost_usd > avg * COST_ANOMALY_MULTIPLIER:
                    warnings.append(
                        f"Session cost ${cost_usd:.2f} is {cost_usd/avg:.1f}x your "
                        f"{COST_ROLLING_DAYS}-day average (${avg:.2f})"
                    )
    except Exception:
        pass

    for w in warnings:
        print(f"capture-cost: {w}", file=sys.stderr)
        notify("Cost Tracking Issue", w)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

File: memory/domain/portability-plan.md

# Plan: Make ~/.claude/ Portable Across Machines

## Context

The `~/.claude/` repo has 86 hardcoded references to `/Users/sameul.nasir` across 35 files, plus 5 loose scripts and a config file sitting at `~/` outside the repo. None of this survives a machine swap. The goal: `git clone` + `bootstrap.sh` = working setup on any machine.

## Lessons Applied (Failure Patterns & Known Issues)

| Source | Lesson | How it's applied |
|--------|--------|------------------|
| Failure: "wrong_code — SQLite DB was wrong after modifying ensure-mlflow hook" | Same kind of change here. Add `$HOME` guard to prevent 3-slash URI bug. | Step 3 |
| Known issue: "SQLite URI with 3 slashes is relative" | `sqlite:///${HOME}/mlflow.db` must expand to 4 slashes. Guard against unset HOME. | Step 3 |
| Failure: "Did not update READMEs after modifying hooks/settings/mcp" | Pre-commit hook (`check-doc-sync.py`) blocks without README updates. | Step 10 |
| Failure: "Did not commit and push after modifying config files" | CLAUDE.md rule 7 requires immediate git sync. | Step 11 |

| Known issue: "MCP servers in mcp.json not loaded by Claude Code" | May be outdated, but verify MCP servers load after changes. | Verification |
