# Obsidian CLI

## Setup

- **Binary**: `/usr/local/bin/obsidian` (CLI Universe tool)
- **Vault**: `~/Desktop/Sam Nasir` (93 files as of 2026-03-26)
- **Auth**: No auth required — local vault access

## Key Commands

| Command | Purpose |
|---------|---------|
| `obsidian read file=<name>` | Read note contents |
| `obsidian search query=<text>` | Full-text vault search |
| `obsidian search:context query=<text>` | Search with matching line context |
| `obsidian create name=<name> content=<text>` | Create a new note |
| `obsidian append file=<name> content=<text>` | Append to existing note |
| `obsidian files` | List all vault files |
| `obsidian files total` | File count |
| `obsidian tasks` | List tasks across vault |
| `obsidian tags` | List tags in vault |
| `obsidian recents` | Recently opened files |
| `obsidian daily` | Open daily note |
| `obsidian daily:append content=<text>` | Append to daily note |
| `obsidian properties file=<name>` | Show file properties/frontmatter |
| `obsidian bookmarks` | List bookmarks |
| `obsidian outline file=<name>` | Show headings tree |
| `obsidian links file=<name>` | Outgoing links from a file |
| `obsidian backlinks file=<name>` | Incoming links to a file |
| `obsidian vaults verbose` | List known vaults with paths |

## Claude Code Symlinks in Obsidian

Symlinked `~/.claude/` files live at `~/Desktop/Sam Nasir/Claude Code/` with this structure:

```
Claude Code/
├── Overview/          ← CLAUDE.md, README.md, SLIDES.md, Memory Index.md
├── Domain/            ← Failure Patterns, Known Issues, Skills Catalog, Artifacts
├── Lessons/           ← Claude Code.md
├── References/        ← AI Evals, Context Layer (3), AI-Ready Data Framework, LLM Eval Workflow
└── Rules/             ← 13 rule files + Cortex/ subfolder (4 files)
```

All are absolute-path symlinks — edits in Obsidian update the repo, and vice versa.

**Gotcha**: Pasting images in Obsidian into symlinked files embeds base64 inline (not as attachments). Extract to a standalone PNG if this happens.

## Notes

- Part of CLI Universe (`~/.cliuniverse/`) — see `tools/cli-universe.md` for shared infra
- No browser auth needed (unlike Teams/Outlook CLIs)
- Supports `format=json|tsv|csv` on most list commands
- Has developer/debugging commands (`dev:dom`, `dev:css`, `eval`)
- Can manage plugins, themes, snippets, and sync

# AI-Ready Data Framework

## Overview

Below is a diagram using a system-based approach on how I define AI-Ready Data.

- **Layer 0 and Layer 1** are the core dependencies required to support Layer 2 & 3.
- For the **bold purple boxes** in each layer, I'm using the heuristic of a backend (data store) and frontend as the MVP data products necessary to drive our business goals and strategy.
- The other boxes across each layer are the frontend/backend stack to achieve our business goals and strategy at Disney scale.

## Pain Point

Our current state is point solutions in Layer 1 that are data product/analytics team specific. They aren't extensible or composable to Layer 2 and Layer 3 yet.

This is primarily because the business goal and strategy has historically been to support Reporting/Activation for each specific team.

There is limited shared context between the different Data Product 360s:
- Data Definitions
- Business Logic
- Data Contracts

## Strategy & Principles

Our future state requires us to align on Layer 1 so that it is ready to support Layer 2 and Layer 3.

1. Focus on defining the backend and frontend (**purple boxes**) of each layer as MVP
2. Ensure the MVP backend/frontend across layers are natively connected bi-directionally (e.g., CWS) — data created by each system can be shared with each system
3. Use the principle of a **Mono-Repo** so our team and organization are aligned on shared resources (memory, context, semantics, skills, services)
4. Tooling and service decisions are based on what exists, and what we need to improve our AI systems based on our **Evaluation Criteria** — start with the least amount of tools, layer when needed based on evaluation data and success criteria
5. Tooling (the frontend/backend stack) should be **composable services** so they are easy to integrate across all Data Product teams

## Roadmap

1. Define a Use Case and the Goal we want to drive/measure
2. Understand the Data Sources we need to support the Use Case and measure its success
3. Understand the MVP Backend/Frontend Tooling that exists to support the use cases across each Layer 1, 2, 3
4. Define Context, Semantics, Memory for AI based on the MVP backend/frontend stack needed across each layer
5. Ensure Alation Pages and Definitions are up to date across the data sets
6. Create a Shared Memory (Tools, References, Rules, Contracts) Repository for teams and organizations
   - https://github.twdcgrid.net/AIAdvance/engram
7. Work with Analytics Partners to create the **Semantic Layer** — markdown files that create the connection between our shared memory (Context, Business Logic/Rules, Tools) and Data Definitions
   - These are version-controlled markdown files and shareable across the business
8. Define Observability tooling so we can measure our MVP system for AI-Ready Data and create the necessary Eval Criteria
9. Use this Eval Criteria to systematically improve the Semantic Layer
10. Use the success criteria of our goal and our Eval criteria to improve our backend/frontend stack (a combination of existing tooling from Layer 1, 2, 3 or net new) that follows our strategy/principles

# Skills Workflow

## Validation Checklist

When creating or modifying a skill, validate against this checklist before committing:

1. Frontmatter has `name` + `description` that says when to use it
2. `allowed-tools` lists every tool the skill needs
3. An **Examples** section with at least one realistic usage scenario
4. A **Guidelines** section with constraints and edge cases
5. No hardcoded paths use `~` or `$HOME`
6. Skill is self-contained with no undeclared runtime dependencies
7. `disable-model-invocation` is NOT set unless there's a specific, documented reason (e.g., skill requires interactive user input mid-flow)

## Skill Invocation Failures

When a skill matches the user's request (via alias or keyword) but the Skill tool rejects it, investigate the cause immediately. If `disable-model-invocation: true` is set, evaluate whether it's still justified. If the skill's workflow is sequential steps with no interactive input, remove the flag and invoke. Never silently fall back to manual execution — fix the invocation path first.

## Doc Sync

When adding or modifying skills under `skills/*/SKILL.md`, always update and stage three files in the same commit:
1. `memory/domain/skills-catalog.md`
2. `README.md`
3. `CLAUDE.md` (update skill count references if count changed)

## Before Committing

After modifying any skill file, before running `git commit`:
1. Stage `CLAUDE.md`, `README.md`, and `memory/domain/skills-catalog.md` alongside the skill change
2. The pre-commit hook (`check-doc-sync.py`) will reject the commit if these are missing
3. Make at least a trivial relevant edit to each doc file if no substantive update is needed (e.g., update a date or description)
4. Commit and push immediately — do not wait for the user to ask

File: scripts/lib/memory_validator.py

"""Validate memory index, detect changelog issues, check staleness."""

import json
import os
import re
import time
from datetime import datetime


def load_memory_index(path: str) -> list[dict]:
    """Parse the markdown table from memory.md.

    Returns list of dicts: {"file": str, "description": str}
    """
    try:
        with open(path) as f:
            content = f.read()
    except (OSError, IOError):
        return []

    entries = []
    # Match table rows: | `file` | description |
    for match in re.finditer(r'\|\s*`([^`]+)`\s*\|\s*(.+?)\s*\|', content):
        filename = match.group(1)
        desc = match.group(2).strip()
        # Skip header row
        if filename == "File" or desc.startswith("---"):
            continue
        entries.append({"file": filename, "description": desc})
    return entries


def get_actual_memory_files(memory_dir: str) -> list[str]:
    """Walk ~/.claude/memory/ for all .md files. Returns relative paths."""
    files = []
    if not os.path.isdir(memory_dir):
        return files

    for root, _dirs, filenames in os.walk(memory_dir):
        for fname in filenames:
            if fname.endswith(".md"):
                rel = os.path.relpath(os.path.join(root, fname), memory_dir)
                # Skip the index file itself
                if rel == "memory.md":
                    continue
                files.append(rel)
    return sorted(files)


def find_index_mismatches(memory_dir: str) -> tuple[list[str], list[str]]:
    """Compare index entries to actual files on disk.

    Returns (in_index_not_on_disk, on_disk_not_in_index).
    """
    index_path = os.path.join(memory_dir, "memory.md")
    entries = load_memory_index(index_path)
    indexed_files = {e["file"] for e in entries}
    actual_files = set(get_actual_memory_files(memory_dir))

    in_index_not_on_disk = sorted(indexed_files - actual_files)
    on_disk_not_in_index = sorted(actual_files - indexed_files)

    return in_index_not_on_disk, on_disk_not_in_index


def detect_duplicate_changelog_entries(path: str) -> list[tuple[str, list[int]]]:
    """Find same-date duplicate entries in changelog sections.

    Returns list of (date_str, [line_numbers]) for dates with duplicates.
    """
    try:
        with open(path) as f:
            lines = f.readlines()
    except (OSError, IOError):
        return []

    # Track dates and their line numbers within changelog sections
    in_changelog = False
    date_lines: dict[str, list[int]] = {}

    for i, line in enumerate(lines, 1):
        stripped = line.strip()
        # Detect changelog section start
        if stripped.lower().startswith("## changelog"):
            in_changelog = True
            continue
        # Exit changelog on next section header
        if in_changelog and stripped.startswith("## ") and "changelog" not in stripped.lower():
            in_changelog = False
            continue

        if in_changelog:
            match = re.match(r'-\s*\*\*(\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2})\*\*', stripped)
            if match:
                date_str = match.group(1)
                date_lines.setdefault(date_str, []).append(i)

    return [(date, lns) for date, lns in date_lines.items() if len(lns) > 1]


def check_readme_accuracy(claude_dir: str) -> list[str]:
    """Compare README.md directory tree against actual files on disk.

    Parses the fenced code block in README.md that shows the directory tree,
    extracts listed files/dirs, and compares against what actually exists.

    Returns list of warning strings (empty if everything matches).
    """
    readme_path = os.path.join(claude_dir, "README.md")
    try:
        with open(readme_path) as f:
            content = f.read()
    except (OSError, IOError):
        return []

    # Extract the directory tree code block
    tree_match = re.search(r'```\n~/.claude/\n(.+?)```', content, re.DOTALL)
    if not tree_match:
        return []

    tree_text = tree_match.group(1)

    # Directories to audit: map dir name -> set of filenames listed in README
    # Parse lines like: │   ├── filename.ext    # description
    # Track which directory we're in by indentation depth
    dir_checks = {
        "rules": {"path": os.path.join(claude_dir, "rules"), "listed": set()},
        "hooks": {"path": os.path.join(claude_dir, "hooks"), "listed": set()},
        "scripts": {"path": os.path.join(claude_dir, "scripts"), "listed": set()},
        "scripts/lib": {"path": os.path.join(claude_dir, "scripts", "lib"), "listed": set()},
        "memory/domain": {"path": os.path.join(claude_dir, "memory", "domain"), "listed": set()},
        "memory/tools": {"path": os.path.join(claude_dir, "memory", "tools"), "listed": set()},
        "references": {"path": os.path.join(claude_dir, "references"), "listed": set()},
    }

    # Parse the tree to find files under each tracked directory
    current_dir = None
    for line in tree_text.splitlines():
        stripped = line.strip()
        # Detect directory headers like: ├── rules/
        dir_match = re.search(r'[├└]── ([\w/.-]+)/\s', stripped + " ")
        if dir_match:
            dirname = dir_match.group(1)
            # Handle nested: if we see "lib/" while in scripts, it's scripts/lib
            if current_dir == "scripts" and dirname == "lib":
                current_dir = "scripts/lib"
            elif dirname in dir_checks:
                current_dir = dirname
            elif current_dir and f"{current_dir}/{dirname}" in dir_checks:
                current_dir = f"{current_dir}/{dirname}"
            else:
                # Check two-level dirs like memory/domain
                for key in dir_checks:
                    if key.endswith(f"/{dirname}"):
                        current_dir = key
                        break
                    elif dirname == key:
                        current_dir = key
                        break
                else:
                    current_dir = None
            continue

        # Detect file entries: ├── filename.ext  or └── filename.ext
        file_match = re.search(r'[├└]── ([\w.-]+\.\w+)', stripped)
        if file_match and current_dir and current_dir in dir_checks:
            dir_checks[current_dir]["listed"].add(file_match.group(1))

    warnings = []
    for dir_name, info in dir_checks.items():
        dir_path = info["path"]
        listed = info["listed"]

        if not os.path.isdir(dir_path):
            continue
        if not listed:
            continue

        # Get actual files (non-dirs, skip hidden)
        actual = {
            f for f in os.listdir(dir_path)
            if os.path.isfile(os.path.join(dir_path, f))
            and not f.startswith(".")
            and f != "__pycache__"
        }

        missing_from_readme = actual - listed
        in_readme_not_on_disk = listed - actual

        for f in sorted(missing_from_readme):
            warnings.append(f"README missing {dir_name}/{f} (exists on disk)")
        for f in sorted(in_readme_not_on_disk):
            warnings.append(f"README lists {dir_name}/{f} (not found on disk)")

    return warnings


def check_failure_pattern_trace_ids(memory_dir: str) -> list[dict]:
    """Check that all Trigger/Recent-trigger lines have trace or session IDs.

    Returns list of dicts: {"line": int, "text": str} for lines missing IDs.
    """
    fp_path = os.path.join(memory_dir, "domain", "failure-patterns.md")
    try:
        with open(fp_path) as f:
            lines = f.readlines()
    except (OSError, IOError):
        return []

    missing = []
    trace_id_pattern = re.compile(r'\(tr-[a-f0-9]+\)|\(session-[a-f0-9]+|trace input truncated')

    for i, line in enumerate(lines, 1):
        stripped = line.strip()
        # Match "Trigger: ..." lines
        is_trigger = stripped.startswith("Trigger:")
        # Match "- " recent trigger lines that contain a date like (2026-03-17)
        is_recent = stripped.startswith("- ") and re.search(r'\(\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2}\)', stripped)

        if is_trigger or is_recent:
            if not trace_id_pattern.search(stripped):
                missing.append({"line": i, "text": stripped[:120]})

    return missing


def check_golden_dataset_fields(dataset_path: str) -> list[str]:
    """Validate golden dataset records have required fields populated.

    Required for all: session_id, pass_fail, axial_code, feature_category, feature_use_case
    Required for Fail: severity, prevention_rule, failure_mode, failure_note
    Required for Pass: passing_note

    Returns list of problem strings (empty = clean).
    """
    try:
        with open(dataset_path) as f:
            data = json.load(f)
    except (OSError, IOError, json.JSONDecodeError):
        return [f"Cannot read or parse {dataset_path}"]

    records = data.get("records", [])
    if not records:
        return []

    always_required = ["session_id", "pass_fail", "axial_code", "feature_category", "feature_use_case"]
    fail_required = ["severity", "prevention_rule", "failure_mode", "failure_note"]
    pass_required = ["passing_note"]

    problems = []
    for i, rec in enumerate(records):
        sid = rec.get("session_id", f"record #{i}")
        pf = rec.get("pass_fail", "")

        for field in always_required:
            if not rec.get(field, "").strip():
                problems.append(f"{sid}: missing {field}")

        if pf == "Fail":
            for field in fail_required:
                if not rec.get(field, "").strip():
                    problems.append(f"{sid}: Fail record missing {field}")

        if pf == "Pass":
            for field in pass_required:
                if not rec.get(field, "").strip():
                    problems.append(f"{sid}: Pass record missing {field}")

    return problems


def check_auto_generated_staleness(memory_dir: str, max_age_days: int = 7) -> list[dict]:
    """Check mtime of auto-generated memory files.

    Returns list of dicts: {"file": str, "age_days": int, "stale": bool}
    """
    auto_generated = [
        "domain/failure-patterns.md",
        "domain/saved-traces.md",
        "domain/known-issues.md",
    ]

    results = []
    now = time.time()

    for rel_path in auto_generated:
        full_path = os.path.join(memory_dir, rel_path)
        if not os.path.isfile(full_path):
            results.append({"file": rel_path, "age_days": -1, "stale": True})
            continue

        mtime = os.path.getmtime(full_path)
        age_days = int((now - mtime) / 86400)
        results.append({
            "file": rel_path,
            "age_days": age_days,
            "stale": age_days > max_age_days,
        })

    return results

================
File: scripts/maintain-check.py
================
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Stop hook: quick maintenance checks. Read-only, <2 seconds, always exits 0.

Outputs warnings to stderr with [maintain] prefix. Silent when clean.
Reads stdin (Stop hook JSON) but only needs filesystem access.
"""

import json
import os
import sys

sys.path.insert(0, os.path.dirname(__file__))
from lib.memory_validator import (
    find_index_mismatches,
    detect_duplicate_changelog_entries,
    check_auto_generated_staleness,
    check_readme_accuracy,
    check_failure_pattern_trace_ids,
    check_golden_dataset_fields,
)

MEMORY_DIR = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/memory")
PREFIX = "[maintain]"

# Files to check for duplicate changelog entries
CHANGELOG_FILES = [
    os.path.join(MEMORY_DIR, "memory.md"),
    os.path.join(MEMORY_DIR, "tools", "mlflow.md"),
]


def warn(msg: str):
    print(f"{PREFIX} {msg}", file=sys.stderr)


def main():
    # Consume stdin (Stop hook sends JSON) but we don't need it
    try:
        sys.stdin.read()
    except Exception:
        pass

    warnings = 0

    # 1. Memory index vs actual files on disk
    missing, extra = find_index_mismatches(MEMORY_DIR)
    if missing:
        warn(f"Memory index references missing files: {', '.join(missing)}")
        warnings += 1
    if extra:
        warn(f"Memory files not in index: {', '.join(extra)}")
        warnings += 1

    # 2. Auto-generated file staleness (>7 days)
    stale = check_auto_generated_staleness(MEMORY_DIR)
    stale_files = [s["file"] for s in stale if s["stale"]]
    if stale_files:
        warn(f"Auto-generated files stale (>7 days): {', '.join(stale_files)}")
        warnings += 1

    # 3. Same-day duplicate changelog entries
    for filepath in CHANGELOG_FILES:
        if not os.path.isfile(filepath):
            continue
        dupes = detect_duplicate_changelog_entries(filepath)
        if dupes:
            fname = os.path.relpath(filepath, os.path.expanduser("~/.claude"))
            for date, lines in dupes:
                warn(f"Duplicate changelog entries in {fname}: {date} (lines {', '.join(str(l) for l in lines)})")
                warnings += 1

    # 4. README directory tree vs actual files on disk
    claude_dir = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude")
    readme_drifts = check_readme_accuracy(claude_dir)
    if readme_drifts:
        warn(f"README.md directory tree out of date ({len(readme_drifts)} discrepancies):")
        for drift in readme_drifts:
            warn(f"  - {drift}")
        warnings += 1

    # 5. Failure pattern trigger lines missing trace IDs
    missing_ids = check_failure_pattern_trace_ids(MEMORY_DIR)
    if missing_ids:
        warn(f"{len(missing_ids)} failure pattern trigger(s) missing trace IDs:")
        for m in missing_ids:
            warn(f"  - line {m['line']}: {m['text']}")
        warnings += 1

    # 6. Golden dataset field validation
    dataset_path = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/evals/golden-dataset.json")
    if os.path.isfile(dataset_path):
        field_problems = check_golden_dataset_fields(dataset_path)
        if field_problems:
            warn(f"{len(field_problems)} golden dataset record(s) with missing fields:")
            for p in field_problems[:5]:
                warn(f"  - {p}")
            if len(field_problems) > 5:
                warn(f"  ... and {len(field_problems) - 5} more")
            warnings += 1

    # Always exit 0 — this is a best-effort check, never block the session
    return 0


if __name__ == "__main__":
    sys.exit(main())

================
File: skills/health-check/SKILL.md

---
name: health-check
description: Full system diagnostics — infra, MCP servers, AWS creds, cost tracking, skill validation
allowed-tools:
  - Bash
---

# Health Check

Run a full diagnostic of all Claude Code infrastructure and skills.

## Execution

```bash
python3 ~/.claude/scripts/health-check.py --mode full
```

## What Each Check Does

### Infrastructure

| Check | How It Works | Healthy | Unhealthy |
|-------|-------------|---------|-----------|
| **MLflow** | `curl -sf http://127.0.0.1:5001/` | HTTP 200 | Connection refused or timeout |
| **Docker** | `docker info > /dev/null 2>&1` | Exit 0 | Docker Desktop not running |
| **Jira container** | `docker ps --filter ancestor=audience-jira-mcp-server` | Container running | No container or stopped |
| **Jira SSE** | `curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}" --max-time 3 http://localhost:3000/sse` | HTTP 200 | Non-200 status (check exit code known issue) |
| **Jira API** | `curl -sf -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" https://jira.disney.com/rest/api/2/myself` | Returns user JSON | 401 (expired token) or timeout (VPN) |
| **AWS credentials** | Checks `~/.aws/credentials` TTL via `ca` helper | TTL > 5 minutes | Expired or missing profile |
| **Cortex import** | Runs `cortex_to_mlflow_converter.py` to import new Cortex conversations | All imported or N new imported | Converter failed or timed out |

### MCP Servers

Reads `~/.claude.json` (mcpServers key) and verifies each server's dependencies:
- **stdio servers**: checks that the `command` binary exists on PATH
- **SSE/HTTP servers**: checks that the URL endpoint responds

### Cost Tracking

| Check | What It Validates |
|-------|-------------------|
| **CSV integrity** | `~/.claude/cost-log.csv` exists, has expected columns, no empty rows |
| **Anomaly detection** | Flags sessions with cost > 3x the rolling average |
| **Spend trends** | Computes avg cost/session for current vs. previous week |

### Git Status

| Check | What It Validates |
|-------|-------------------|
| **Working tree** | No uncommitted changes in `~/.claude/` repository |
| **Remote sync** | Local branch is in sync with `github.twdcgrid.net/sameul-nasir/claude-settings` |
| **Branch tracking** | Current branch tracks a remote branch properly |
| **Network connectivity** | Can fetch from remote repository (auth and network) |

### Skills

Runs `test-skills.py` checks: YAML frontmatter, required fields (`name`, `description`), file references resolve, `allowed-tools` match available MCP tools, Examples and Guidelines sections present, skills-catalog.md sync.

## Jira Auto-Repair

When the health check detects Jira issues, follow these steps to auto-repair instead of just reporting the problem.

### Docker Not Running
Tell the user to start Docker Desktop. Stop — nothing else can be done.

### Container Stopped
```bash
# Find stopped container
docker ps -a --filter ancestor=audience-jira-mcp-server --format '{{.ID}}' | head -1
# Restart it (preserves env vars)
docker start <CONTAINER_ID>
```

### No Container Exists
```bash
# Get token from persistent store
JIRA_TOKEN=$(grep '^JIRA_TOKEN=' ~/.atlassian-tokens.env 2>/dev/null | cut -d= -f2)
# Create container
docker run -d -p 3000:3000 -e JIRA_TOKEN="$JIRA_TOKEN" -e MCP_TRANSPORT=sse audience-jira-mcp-server
```
If `JIRA_TOKEN` is empty, ask the user to provide it.

### Token Expired (401)
Tell the user to regenerate their Jira PAT or run `/update-atlassian-token`.

### VPN Not Connected
Tell the user to connect to the corporate VPN. Don't suggest other fixes.

### After Repair
Verify SSE endpoint (`curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}" --max-time 3 http://localhost:3000/sse`) and Jira API connectivity before reporting success.

## Manual Checks (When Script Fails)

If the health-check script itself errors, run these individually:

```bash
# MLflow
curl -sf http://127.0.0.1:5001/ && echo "OK" || echo "DOWN"

# Docker + Jira
docker ps --filter ancestor=audience-jira-mcp-server --format '{{.ID}} {{.Status}}'

# Jira SSE (use HTTP status, not exit code — SSE streams never end)
curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}" --max-time 3 http://localhost:3000/sse

# AWS credentials
aws sts get-caller-identity --profile twdc-bedrock-central

# Cost CSV
wc -l ~/.claude/cost-log.csv && tail -1 ~/.claude/cost-log.csv

# Skills validation
python3 ~/.claude/scripts/test-skills.py --static-only

# Git status and sync
cd ~/.claude && git status --porcelain  # Should be empty for clean tree
cd ~/.claude && git fetch && git status  # Check sync status
cd ~/.claude && git rev-list --left-right --count HEAD...@{upstream}  # Compare with remote
```

## Guidelines

- **Never print raw script output verbatim.** Summarize results conversationally — the user doesn't need to see JSON or stack traces.
- **Lead with the overall status**, then details. "All healthy" or "2 issues found" should be the first thing the user reads.
- **For each issue, include the fix.** Don't just say "MLflow is down" — say how to start it. Don't just say "Docker container stopped" — follow the Jira Auto-Repair steps above.
- **Cost trends are informational, not alarming.** Report them factually (e.g., "avg $0.38/session this week, up from $0.31 last week") without editorializing.
- **If the health-check script itself fails** (Python error, missing dependency), report the error and fall back to the Manual Checks section above rather than silently failing.

## Examples

### Example 1: All Systems Healthy

**User**: `/health-check` or "system status"

**Claude runs** `python3 ~/.claude/scripts/health-check.py --mode full`, then reports:

> All systems healthy — MLflow on port 5001, Jira container running (SSE 200), AWS creds valid (expires in 11h), cost tracking current (318 traces, $47.22 total). All 13 skills passing validation.

### Example 2: Issues Found

**Claude runs** the health check and finds problems, then reports:

> Two issues found:
> - **MLflow**: Server not running on port 5001. Fix: `mlflow server --host 127.0.0.1 --port 5001 --backend-store-uri sqlite:////Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db &`
> - **Jira**: Docker container stopped. Restarting... ✓ Container back up, SSE healthy.
>
> Everything else healthy — AWS creds valid, cost tracking current, all 13 skills passing.

## Reporting

After running, present the results conversationally:

1. **All healthy** — confirm briefly: "All systems healthy — infra, MCP servers, cost tracking, and all skills passing."
2. **Issues found** — list each with what's wrong and how to fix it. Be specific and actionable.
3. Mention cost trends if included.

Do not reprint the raw output verbatim — summarize it naturally.

File: skills/jira-ticket-finder/query_report.py
================
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Jira sprint report — overview + risk analysis for all boards.

Usage:
    python3 query_report.py
"""
import json, csv, os, re, subprocess, sys
from datetime import date, datetime
from urllib.parse import quote

# --- Config ---
JIRA_BASE = "https://jira.disney.com"
BOARDS = {
    "DSACQ": 12209,
    "MEOW": 14236,
    "QMDS": 12489,
}

# Epics to break out into their own section
BREAKOUT_EPICS = {
    "DSACQ-15049": "FiveTran Migration",
}

# Token extraction: Docker container -> token file -> fail
TOKEN = os.popen(
    'docker exec $(docker ps -q --filter ancestor=audience-jira-mcp-server) printenv JIRA_TOKEN 2>/dev/null'
).read().strip()
if not TOKEN:
    token_file = os.path.expanduser("~/.atlassian-tokens.env")
    if os.path.exists(token_file):
        with open(token_file) as f:
            for line in f:
                if line.startswith("JIRA_TOKEN="):
                    TOKEN = line.strip().split("=", 1)[1]
                    break
if not TOKEN:
    print("ERROR: Could not extract JIRA_TOKEN. Run /connect-jira or /update-atlassian-token first.")
    sys.exit(1)


def curl_get(url):
    result = subprocess.run(
        ["curl", "-sf", "--max-time", "30",
         "-H", f"Authorization: Bearer {TOKEN}",
         "-H", "Content-Type: application/json",
         url],
        capture_output=True, text=True
    )
    if result.returncode != 0:
        raise RuntimeError(f"curl failed (exit {result.returncode}): {result.stderr}")
    return json.loads(result.stdout)


def get_active_sprint(board_id):
    url = f"{JIRA_BASE}/rest/agile/1.0/board/{board_id}/sprint?state=active"
    data = curl_get(url)
    sprints = data.get("values", [])
    if not sprints:
        return None
    s = sprints[0]
    return {
        "id": s["id"],
        "name": s["name"],
        "startDate": s.get("startDate", ""),
        "endDate": s.get("endDate", ""),
    }


def get_sprint_issues(sprint_id):
    all_issues = []
    start_at = 0
    while True:
        url = (
            f"{JIRA_BASE}/rest/agile/1.0/sprint/{sprint_id}/issue"
            f"?maxResults=100&startAt={start_at}"
            f"&fields=key,summary,status,priority,assignee,issuetype,customfield_10106,customfield_10101,updated"
        )
        data = curl_get(url)
        issues = data.get("issues", [])
        all_issues.extend(issues)
        if start_at + len(issues) >= data.get("total", 0):
            break
        start_at += 100
    return all_issues


def parse_issue(issue):
    f = issue.get("fields", {})
    key = issue.get("key", "")
    project = key.split("-")[0] if "-" in key else ""
    assignee_obj = f.get("assignee")
    pts = f.get("customfield_10106")
    updated_raw = f.get("updated", "")
    updated_date = None
    if updated_raw:
        try:
            updated_date = datetime.fromisoformat(updated_raw.replace("+0000", "+00:00")[:19])
        except (ValueError, TypeError):
            pass

    return {
        "project": project,
        "key": key,
        "summary": f.get("summary", ""),
        "status": (f.get("status") or {}).get("name", ""),
        "status_category": (f.get("status") or {}).get("statusCategory", {}).get("name", ""),
        "priority": (f.get("priority") or {}).get("name", ""),
        "assignee": assignee_obj.get("displayName", "") if assignee_obj else "Unassigned",
        "issue_type": (f.get("issuetype") or {}).get("name", ""),
        "story_points": float(pts) if pts is not None else 0,
        "updated": updated_date,
        "epic_link": f.get("customfield_10101", ""),
    }


def compute_risk(ticket, days_remaining):
    score = 0
    status = ticket["status"]
    pts = ticket["story_points"]

    # Status risk
    if status in ("Open", "To Do", "Backlog"):
        score += 3
    elif status in ("In Progress", "In Development", "Discovery"):
        score += 1

    if status == "Blocked":
        score += 4

    # Size risk
    if pts >= 5:
        score += 2
    elif pts >= 3:
        score += 1

    # Time pressure
    if days_remaining <= 3 and status not in ("In Review", "Done", "Closed", "Resolved"):
        score += 2
    elif days_remaining <= 5 and status in ("Open", "To Do", "Backlog"):
        score += 1

    # Staleness
    if ticket["updated"]:
        days_since_update = (datetime.now() - ticket["updated"]).days
        if days_since_update >= 5:
            score += 2
        elif days_since_update >= 3:
            score += 1

    # Unassigned
    if ticket["assignee"] == "Unassigned":
        score += 2

    return score


def risk_label(score):
    if score >= 5:
        return "HIGH"
    elif score >= 3:
        return "MEDIUM"
    else:
        return "LOW"


def risk_reasons(ticket, days_remaining):
    reasons = []
    status = ticket["status"]
    pts = ticket["story_points"]

    if status == "Blocked":
        reasons.append("Blocked")
    if status in ("Open", "To Do", "Backlog"):
        reasons.append(f"Still {status}")
    if pts >= 5:
        reasons.append(f"{pts:.0f} pts")
    if days_remaining <= 3 and status not in ("In Review", "Done", "Closed", "Resolved"):
        reasons.append(f"Only {days_remaining}d left")
    if ticket["updated"]:
        days_stale = (datetime.now() - ticket["updated"]).days
        if days_stale >= 5:
            reasons.append(f"No update in {days_stale}d")
    if ticket["assignee"] == "Unassigned":
        reasons.append("Unassigned")
    return ", ".join(reasons) if reasons else "Minor risk factors"


# --- Main ---
today = date.today()
all_board_data = {}

for project, board_id in BOARDS.items():
    sprint = get_active_sprint(board_id)
    if not sprint:
        print(f"  {project}: No active sprint found")
        continue

    issues = get_sprint_issues(sprint["id"])
    tickets = [parse_issue(i) for i in issues]

    # Calculate days remaining
    end_str = sprint.get("endDate", "")
    days_remaining = 7  # default if can't parse
    if end_str:
        try:
            end_date = datetime.fromisoformat(end_str.replace("+0000", "+00:00")[:19]).date()
            days_remaining = max(0, (end_date - today).days)
        except (ValueError, TypeError):
            pass

    all_board_data[project] = {
        "sprint": sprint,
        "tickets": tickets,
        "days_remaining": days_remaining,
    }

# --- Helper functions for output ---

def print_assignee_table(tickets):
    """Print an assignee overview table for a set of tickets."""
    assignee_stats = {}
    for t in tickets:
        a = t["assignee"]
        if a not in assignee_stats:
            assignee_stats[a] = {"In Progress": 0, "In Review": 0, "Open": 0, "Done": 0, "Blocked": 0, "Other": 0, "pts": 0}
        s = t["status"]
        if s in ("In Progress", "In Development"):
            assignee_stats[a]["In Progress"] += 1
        elif s in ("In Review", "Code Review", "Ready for QA", "In QA"):
            assignee_stats[a]["In Review"] += 1
        elif s in ("Open", "To Do", "Backlog", "Reopened", "Ready for Development", "Discovery"):
            assignee_stats[a]["Open"] += 1
        elif s in ("Done", "Closed", "Resolved"):
            assignee_stats[a]["Done"] += 1
        elif s == "Blocked":
            assignee_stats[a]["Blocked"] += 1
        else:
            assignee_stats[a]["Other"] += 1
        assignee_stats[a]["pts"] += t["story_points"]

    print(f"{'Assignee':<28} {'In Prog':>8} {'Review':>8} {'Open':>8} {'Done':>8} {'Blocked':>8} {'Pts':>6}")
    print("-" * 86)
    for a in sorted(assignee_stats):
        s = assignee_stats[a]
        print(f"{a:<28} {s['In Progress']:>8} {s['In Review']:>8} {s['Open']:>8} {s['Done']:>8} {s['Blocked']:>8} {s['pts']:>6.0f}")


def print_risk_analysis(tickets, header):
    """Print risk analysis for a set of tickets. Returns (high_risk, medium_risk) lists."""
    high_risk = [t for t in tickets if t.get("risk_label") == "HIGH"]
    medium_risk = [t for t in tickets if t.get("risk_label") == "MEDIUM"]
    high_risk.sort(key=lambda t: -t["risk_score"])
    medium_risk.sort(key=lambda t: -t["risk_score"])

    print(f"\n{'='*86}")
    print(header)
    print(f"{'='*86}")

    if high_risk:
        print(f"\nHIGH RISK ({len(high_risk)} tickets)\n")
        print(f"{'Key':<16} {'Summary':<60} {'Status':<16} {'Assignee':<24} {'Pts':>4}  {'Why':<40}")
        print("-" * 164)
        for t in high_risk:
            summary = t['summary'][:57] + '...' if len(t['summary']) > 60 else t['summary']
            print(f"{t['key']:<16} {summary:<60} {t['status']:<16} {t['assignee']:<24} {t['story_points']:>4.0f}  {t['risk_reasons']:<40}")
    else:
        print("\nNo HIGH risk tickets.")

    if medium_risk:
        print(f"\nMEDIUM RISK ({len(medium_risk)} tickets)\n")
        print(f"{'Key':<16} {'Summary':<60} {'Status':<16} {'Assignee':<24} {'Pts':>4}  {'Why':<40}")
        print("-" * 164)
        for t in medium_risk:
            summary = t['summary'][:57] + '...' if len(t['summary']) > 60 else t['summary']
            print(f"{t['key']:<16} {summary:<60} {t['status']:<16} {t['assignee']:<24} {t['story_points']:>4.0f}  {t['risk_reasons']:<40}")
    else:
        print("\nNo MEDIUM risk tickets.")

    return high_risk, medium_risk


# --- Output: Sprint Overview ---
all_tickets = []
breakout_tickets = []  # tickets belonging to breakout epics
board_regular_tickets = {}  # per-board non-breakout risk tickets

for project in ["DSACQ", "MEOW", "QMDS"]:
    if project not in all_board_data:
        continue
    bd = all_board_data[project]
    sprint = bd["sprint"]
    tickets = bd["tickets"]
    days_left = bd["days_remaining"]

    # Separate breakout epic tickets from the rest
    board_breakout = [t for t in tickets if t.get("epic_link") in BREAKOUT_EPICS]
    board_regular = [t for t in tickets if t.get("epic_link") not in BREAKOUT_EPICS]

    breakout_note = ""
    if board_breakout:
        epic_key = board_breakout[0]["epic_link"]
        breakout_note = f" (+{len(board_breakout)} {BREAKOUT_EPICS[epic_key]})"
    print(f"\n### {sprint['name']} ({days_left} days remaining) -- {len(board_regular)} tickets{breakout_note}\n")

    print_assignee_table(board_regular)

    # Compute risk for all non-done tickets
    board_regular_tickets[project] = []
    for t in tickets:
        if t["status_category"] == "Done":
            continue
        score = compute_risk(t, days_left)
        t["risk_score"] = score
        t["risk_label"] = risk_label(score)
        t["risk_reasons"] = risk_reasons(t, days_left)
        t["sprint_name"] = sprint["name"]
        t["days_remaining"] = days_left
        if t.get("epic_link") in BREAKOUT_EPICS:
            breakout_tickets.append(t)
        else:
            board_regular_tickets[project].append(t)
            all_tickets.append(t)

# --- Output: Breakout Epic Sections ---
for epic_key, epic_name in BREAKOUT_EPICS.items():
    epic_all = [t for t in breakout_tickets if t.get("epic_link") == epic_key]
    if not epic_all:
        continue

    # Include done tickets for the overview table
    epic_all_with_done = []
    for bd in all_board_data.values():
        epic_all_with_done.extend([t for t in bd["tickets"] if t.get("epic_link") == epic_key])

    print(f"\n### {epic_name} (Epic {epic_key}) -- {len(epic_all_with_done)} tickets\n")
    print_assignee_table(epic_all_with_done)

    bo_high, bo_med = print_risk_analysis(epic_all, f"{epic_name.upper()} — RISK ANALYSIS")

    done_count = len([t for t in epic_all_with_done if t["status_category"] == "Done"])
    print(f"\n--- {epic_name} Summary ---")
    print(f"Total: {len(epic_all_with_done)} | Done: {done_count} | Remaining: {len(epic_all_with_done) - done_count}")
    print(f"High risk: {len(bo_high)} | Medium risk: {len(bo_med)}")

# --- Output: Per-Board Risk Analysis (excluding breakout epics) ---
total_high = sum(1 for t in breakout_tickets if t.get("risk_label") == "HIGH")
total_med = sum(1 for t in breakout_tickets if t.get("risk_label") == "MEDIUM")

for project in ["DSACQ", "MEOW", "QMDS"]:
    if project not in board_regular_tickets or not board_regular_tickets[project]:
        continue
    bd = all_board_data[project]
    sprint_name = bd["sprint"]["name"]
    board_tix = board_regular_tickets[project]
    b_high, b_med = print_risk_analysis(board_tix, f"{sprint_name} — RISK ANALYSIS")

    board_all = [t for t in bd["tickets"] if t.get("epic_link") not in BREAKOUT_EPICS]
    done_count = len([t for t in board_all if t["status_category"] == "Done"])
    print(f"\n--- {project} Summary ---")
    print(f"Total: {len(board_all)} | Done: {done_count} | Remaining: {len(board_all) - done_count}")
    print(f"High risk: {len(b_high)} | Medium risk: {len(b_med)}")
    total_high += len(b_high)
    total_med += len(b_med)

# Overall summary
total_tickets = sum(len(bd["tickets"]) for bd in all_board_data.values())
done_tickets = sum(1 for bd in all_board_data.values() for t in bd["tickets"] if t["status_category"] == "Done")
print(f"\n{'='*86}")
print(f"--- Overall Summary ---")
print(f"Total: {total_tickets} tickets | Done: {done_tickets} | Remaining: {total_tickets - done_tickets}")
print(f"High risk: {total_high} | Medium risk: {total_med}")

# --- CSV Export ---
csv_path = os.path.expanduser(f"~/Desktop/sprint_report_{today.isoformat()}.csv")
combined_tickets = all_tickets + breakout_tickets
with open(csv_path, "w", newline="") as fout:
    writer = csv.DictWriter(fout, fieldnames=[
        "Project", "Key", "Summary", "Status", "Assignee", "Priority",
        "Issue Type", "Story Points", "Sprint", "Epic", "Risk", "Risk Score", "Risk Reasons",
    ])
    writer.writeheader()
    for t in sorted(combined_tickets, key=lambda x: (-x["risk_score"], x["project"], x["key"])):
        epic_label = BREAKOUT_EPICS.get(t.get("epic_link", ""), "")
        writer.writerow({
            "Project": t["project"],
            "Key": t["key"],
            "Summary": t["summary"],
            "Status": t["status"],
            "Assignee": t["assignee"],
            "Priority": t["priority"],
            "Issue Type": t["issue_type"],
            "Story Points": t["story_points"],
            "Sprint": t.get("sprint_name", ""),
            "Epic": epic_label,
            "Risk": t["risk_label"],
            "Risk Score": t["risk_score"],
            "Risk Reasons": t["risk_reasons"],
        })

print(f"\nCSV exported to: {csv_path}")

File: skills/unity-databricks/scripts/run-query.sh
================
#!/bin/bash
# Run a SQL query against Databricks via the SQL Statements API
# Usage: ./run-query.sh "<SQL>" [warehouse_id]
#
# Default warehouse: b682b4d44313d3a4 (Default Unity SQL Endpoint)
# Polls for completion with exponential backoff (max 120s)

set -euo pipefail

QUERY="${1:?Usage: run-query.sh \"<SQL>\" [warehouse_id]}"
WAREHOUSE_ID="${2:-b682b4d44313d3a4}"
HOST="https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com"
MAX_WAIT=120

# Get token (use profile to avoid duplicate-host ambiguity)
TOKEN=$(databricks auth token --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD 2>&1 | grep -o 'eyJ[^"]*' || true)
if [ -z "$TOKEN" ]; then
    echo "ERROR: Auth token not available. Run: databricks auth login --host $HOST" >&2
    exit 1
fi

# Submit query
RESPONSE=$(curl -s -X POST "$HOST/api/2.0/sql/statements/" \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d "$(python3 -c "import json; print(json.dumps({'warehouse_id': '$WAREHOUSE_ID', 'statement': $(python3 -c "import json; print(json.dumps('$QUERY'))"), 'wait_timeout': '30s'}))")" 2>&1)

# Parse response
python3 -c "
import json, sys, time

try:
    r = json.loads('''$RESPONSE''')
except:
    r = json.load(open('/dev/stdin'))

status = r.get('status', {}).get('state', 'UNKNOWN')
statement_id = r.get('statement_id', '')

# Poll if still pending
elapsed = 0
interval = 2
while status in ('PENDING', 'RUNNING') and elapsed < $MAX_WAIT:
    import subprocess
    time.sleep(interval)
    elapsed += interval
    interval = min(interval * 2, 10)
    poll = subprocess.run(
        ['curl', '-s', '-H', 'Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN',
         '$HOST/api/2.0/sql/statements/' + statement_id],
        capture_output=True, text=True
    )
    r = json.loads(poll.stdout)
    status = r.get('status', {}).get('state', 'UNKNOWN')

if status == 'SUCCEEDED':
    cols = [c['name'] for c in r.get('manifest', {}).get('schema', {}).get('columns', [])]
    rows = r.get('result', {}).get('data_array', [])
    # Output as JSON for easy parsing
    print(json.dumps({'columns': cols, 'rows': rows, 'row_count': len(rows)}, indent=2))
elif status == 'FAILED':
    err = r.get('status', {}).get('error', {})
    print(json.dumps({'error': err.get('message', 'Unknown error'), 'error_code': err.get('error_code', '')}, indent=2))
    sys.exit(1)
else:
    print(json.dumps({'status': status, 'statement_id': statement_id, 'message': 'Query still running after ${MAX_WAIT}s'}))
    sys.exit(1)
" <<< "$RESPONSE"

File: skills/unity-databricks/scripts/setup-check.sh
================
#!/bin/bash
# Verify Databricks CLI installation and authentication
# Usage: ./setup-check.sh [profile]

set -euo pipefail

PROFILE="${1:-}"
HOST="https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com"
MIN_VERSION="0.205"

echo "=== Databricks Setup Check ==="

# 1. CLI installed?
if ! command -v databricks &>/dev/null; then
    echo "FAIL: Databricks CLI not found. Install: brew install databricks"
    exit 1
fi
echo "OK: CLI found at $(which databricks)"

# 2. Version check
VERSION=$(databricks --version 2>/dev/null | grep -oE '[0-9]+\.[0-9]+\.[0-9]+' | head -1)
if [ -z "$VERSION" ]; then
    echo "WARN: Could not determine CLI version"
else
    MAJOR=$(echo "$VERSION" | cut -d. -f1)
    MINOR=$(echo "$VERSION" | cut -d. -f2)
    MIN_MAJOR=$(echo "$MIN_VERSION" | cut -d. -f1)
    MIN_MINOR=$(echo "$MIN_VERSION" | cut -d. -f2)
    if [ "$MAJOR" -gt "$MIN_MAJOR" ] || { [ "$MAJOR" -eq "$MIN_MAJOR" ] && [ "$MINOR" -ge "$MIN_MINOR" ]; }; then
        echo "OK: CLI version $VERSION (>= $MIN_VERSION)"
    else
        echo "WARN: CLI version $VERSION (recommended >= $MIN_VERSION). Update: brew upgrade databricks"
    fi
fi

# 3. Config file
if [ -f "$HOME/.databrickscfg" ]; then
    echo "OK: ~/.databrickscfg exists"
    PROFILES=$(grep '^\[' "$HOME/.databrickscfg" | tr -d '[]' || true)
    if [ -n "$PROFILES" ]; then
        echo "    Profiles: $PROFILES"
    fi
else
    echo "INFO: No ~/.databrickscfg — using OAuth token cache"
fi

# 4. Auth check — use profile to avoid duplicate-host ambiguity
EFFECTIVE_PROFILE="${PROFILE:-DSS-UNITY-PROD}"
echo ""
echo "--- Auth Check (profile: $EFFECTIVE_PROFILE) ---"
AUTH_OUT=$(databricks auth token --profile "$EFFECTIVE_PROFILE" 2>&1) || true

if echo "$AUTH_OUT" | grep -qi "error\|expired\|failed"; then
    echo "FAIL: Auth not valid for $EFFECTIVE_PROFILE"
    echo "  Run: databricks auth login --host $HOST"
    exit 1
else
    echo "OK: Auth valid for $EFFECTIVE_PROFILE"
fi

# 5. Quick connectivity test
echo ""
echo "--- Connectivity ---"
WHOAMI=$(databricks current-user me --profile "$EFFECTIVE_PROFILE" --output json 2>&1) || true
if echo "$WHOAMI" | grep -q "userName"; then
    USER=$(echo "$WHOAMI" | python3 -c "import json,sys; print(json.load(sys.stdin).get('userName','unknown'))" 2>/dev/null)
    echo "OK: Connected as $USER"
else
    echo "FAIL: Could not reach workspace at $HOST"
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "=== All checks passed ==="

File: skills/unity-databricks/SKILL.md

---
name: unity-databricks
description: >-
  Use when the user asks about Databricks pipelines, Unity Catalog tables, or running SQL queries
  against Databricks warehouses. Covers pipeline monitoring (read-only), catalog/schema/table browsing,
  and SQL execution via the SQL Statements API. Also handles auth detection and re-auth guidance.
allowed-tools:
  - Bash
  - Read
  - Write
  - Edit
  - Glob
  - Grep
  - Agent
---

# Unity Databricks Skill

Monitor DLT pipelines, browse Unity Catalog, and run SQL queries against Databricks workspaces.

## Before Any Operation

1. Read `~/.claude/skills/unity-databricks/references/workspace-config.md` for warehouse IDs, catalog names, and pipeline IDs
2. Verify auth is valid: `DATABRICKS_HOST=https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com databricks auth token --host https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com 2>&1`
3. If auth fails, tell the user to run: `databricks auth login --host https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com`

## Auth Detection

The Databricks CLI uses OAuth U2M (browser SSO). Tokens auto-refresh for ~1 hour, then expire.

**Check token validity:**
```bash
databricks auth token --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD 2>&1
```

If the output contains `Error` or `expired`, tell the user:
> Your Databricks token has expired. Run this in your terminal:
> `databricks auth login --host https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com`

**Profile-based auth** (if `~/.databrickscfg` exists):
```bash
databricks auth token --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD 2>&1
```

## 1. Pipeline Monitoring (Read-Only)

**List all pipelines:**
```bash
databricks pipelines list-pipelines --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json
```

**Get pipeline details:**
```bash
databricks pipelines get <pipeline_id> --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json
```

**List recent updates (runs):**
```bash
databricks pipelines list-updates <pipeline_id> --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json
```

**Get specific update details:**
```bash
databricks pipelines get-update <pipeline_id> --update-id <update_id> --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json
```

**Pipeline status interpretation:**
- `IDLE` — pipeline is not running, last run completed
- `RUNNING` — pipeline is actively processing
- `FAILED` — last run failed, check update events for details
- `STARTING` — pipeline is initializing

When reporting pipeline status, always include: name, state, last update time, and any error messages from the most recent update.

## 2. Unity Catalog Browsing

**List catalogs:**
```bash
databricks unity-catalog catalogs list --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json
```

**List schemas in a catalog:**
```bash
databricks unity-catalog schemas list --catalog-name <catalog> --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json
```

**List tables in a schema:**
```bash
databricks unity-catalog tables list --catalog-name <catalog> --schema-name <schema> --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json
```

**Get table details (columns, types, properties):**
```bash
databricks unity-catalog tables get <catalog>.<schema>.<table> --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json
```

**Search tables by name pattern:**
```bash
databricks unity-catalog tables list --catalog-name <catalog> --schema-name <schema> --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json | python3 -c "
import json, sys
tables = json.load(sys.stdin)
for t in (tables if isinstance(tables, list) else tables.get('tables', [])):
    if '<pattern>' in t.get('name', '').lower():
        print(f\"{t['catalog_name']}.{t['schema_name']}.{t['name']}  ({t.get('table_type', 'N/A')})\")"
```

## 3. SQL Queries via SQL Statements API

Use the `run-query.sh` helper script for SQL execution:

```bash
~/.claude/skills/unity-databricks/scripts/run-query.sh "<SQL_QUERY>" [warehouse_id]
```

- Default warehouse: `b682b4d44313d3a4` (Default Unity SQL Endpoint — RUNNING)
- The script handles: submit → poll for completion → format results
- Results are returned as JSON with column names and rows

**Direct API approach** (when the script is unavailable):

```bash
# Get a token
TOKEN=$(databricks auth token --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD 2>&1 | grep -o 'eyJ[^"]*')

HOST="https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com"
WAREHOUSE_ID="b682b4d44313d3a4"

# Submit query
RESPONSE=$(curl -s -X POST "$HOST/api/2.0/sql/statements/" \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d "{
    \"warehouse_id\": \"$WAREHOUSE_ID\",
    \"statement\": \"SELECT 1 AS test\",
    \"wait_timeout\": \"30s\"
  }")

echo "$RESPONSE" | python3 -c "
import json, sys
r = json.load(sys.stdin)
status = r.get('status', {}).get('state', 'UNKNOWN')
if status == 'SUCCEEDED':
    cols = [c['name'] for c in r.get('manifest', {}).get('schema', {}).get('columns', [])]
    print('\t'.join(cols))
    for row in r.get('result', {}).get('data_array', []):
        print('\t'.join(str(v) for v in row))
elif status == 'FAILED':
    print(f\"ERROR: {r.get('status', {}).get('error', {}).get('message', 'Unknown error')}\")
else:
    print(f\"Status: {status} — statement_id: {r.get('statement_id', 'N/A')}\")"
```

## Examples

### Check pipeline status
**User**: "How are my Databricks pipelines doing?"
**Action**: Read workspace-config.md for pipeline IDs, verify auth, run `pipelines get` for each pipeline, report status including last update time and any errors.

### Browse catalog tables
**User**: "What tables are in the audience_de_prod catalog?"
**Action**: Verify auth, run `schemas list` for audience_de_prod, then `tables list` for each schema (or a user-specified schema). Present as a tree: catalog → schema → tables.

### Run a SQL query
**User**: "Query the top 10 rows from audience_de_prod.default.some_table"
**Action**: Verify auth, use run-query.sh with `SELECT * FROM audience_de_prod.default.some_table LIMIT 10`, format results as a table.

### Auth expired
**User**: "Check my pipeline status" (but token is expired)
**Action**: Detect auth failure, tell user to run `databricks auth login --host https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com`, wait for confirmation, then proceed.

## Guidelines

- **Read-only pipelines**: Never start, stop, or modify pipelines. Only monitor status and view update history.
- **Auth cannot be automated**: OAuth U2M requires browser SSO. When auth expires, tell the user the exact command to run — do not attempt to automate re-authentication.
- **Default to prod**: Unless the user specifies nonprod, always use the prod workspace.
- **Confirm before large queries**: If a query lacks LIMIT or targets a known large table, suggest adding `LIMIT 100` before executing.
- **Use the running warehouse**: Default to `b682b4d44313d3a4` (Default Unity SQL Endpoint) which is typically RUNNING. Other warehouses may be STOPPED and require startup time.
- **Never expose tokens**: Do not print or log Bearer tokens in output. Use them inline in commands only.
- **Progressive catalog browsing**: Start with catalogs → schemas → tables. Don't dump all tables across all schemas at once.

================
File: memory/tools/databricks.md
================
# Databricks

CLI patterns, auth workflow, and reference commands.

---

## Auth

- **2026-03-17** [claude-code]: OAuth U2M via `databricks auth login --host <url>`. Token cache at `~/.databricks/token-cache.json`. Tokens auto-refresh for ~1 hour, then expire. No `~/.databrickscfg` required for basic auth — profiles optional.
- **2026-03-17** [claude-code]: Check token: `databricks auth token --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD`. Check identity: `databricks current-user me --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD`. Always use `--profile` (not `--host`) because multiple profiles share the same host URL, causing ambiguity errors.

## CLI Patterns

- **2026-03-17** [claude-code]: Pipeline commands use `list-pipelines` (not `list`). Always use `--output json` for parseable output.
- **2026-03-17** [claude-code]: Unity Catalog hierarchy: `databricks catalogs list` → `databricks schemas list CATALOG` → `databricks tables list CATALOG SCHEMA --omit-columns --omit-properties` → `databricks tables get CATALOG.SCHEMA.TABLE`. Use positional args (not `--catalog-name`/`--schema-name` flags). Always add `--omit-columns --omit-properties` when listing tables to avoid timeouts on large schemas.
- **2026-03-17** [claude-code]: SQL Statements API: POST to `/api/2.0/sql/statements/` with warehouse_id and statement. Poll via GET on `/api/2.0/sql/statements/{statement_id}`. Helper script at `~/.claude/skills/unity-databricks/scripts/run-query.sh`.

## Workspace Reference

- **2026-03-17** [claude-code]: Workspace-specific data (warehouse IDs, catalogs, pipelines, user groups) lives in `~/.claude/skills/unity-databricks/references/workspace-config.md`. Behavioral rules in `rules/databricks.md`.

================
File: rules/databricks.md
================
# Databricks Workflow

## Auth Check First

Before any Databricks operation, verify auth is valid:
```bash
databricks auth token --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD 2>&1
```
If expired, tell the user the exact re-auth command. Do not attempt to automate OAuth browser SSO.

## Default Workspace

Always default to **prod** (`https://dss-unity-prod-us-east-1.cloud.databricks.com`) unless the user explicitly says nonprod.

## Read-Only Pipelines

Never start, stop, reset, or modify DLT pipelines. Only monitor: get status, list updates, view events.

## Token Safety

Never print, log, or expose Bearer tokens in output. Use them inline in curl/CLI commands only.

## Schema Browsing vs Data Queries

- **Listing tables/schemas**: Use the Databricks CLI (`databricks tables list CATALOG SCHEMA --profile DSS-UNITY-PROD --output json --omit-columns --omit-properties`). The SQL Statements API (`SHOW TABLES`, `information_schema`) hangs on large schemas.
- **Querying data**: Use the SQL Statements API (`POST /api/2.0/sql/statements/`). It works well for SELECT queries.

## Before Any Databricks Operation

Read `~/.claude/skills/unity-databricks/references/workspace-config.md` for warehouse IDs, catalog names, and pipeline IDs.

================
File: rules/memory-system.md
================
# Memory System

## Write Rules

1. When you learn something worth remembering, write it to the right file immediately.
2. Keep `memory.md` as a current index with one-line descriptions.
3. Entries: date, what, why — nothing more.
4. **Source tag every entry** with `[claude-code]` or `[cortex-code]` to indicate which system created it. Detect via `CORTEX_SESSION_ID` env var (present = cortex-code, absent = claude-code). Format:
   - Bullet entries: `- **2026-03-12** [claude-code]: description`
   - Failure pattern headers: `### Title (2026-03-12) [severity] [deterministic|infrastructure] [claude-code]`
   - Failure pattern triggers: Include cross-reference IDs in parentheses after the quote.
     - Claude Code: `Trigger: quote (tr-{trace_id})` — use the MLflow trace request_id
     - Cortex Code: `Trigger: quote (session-{session_id}, msg-{msg_id})` — use the conversation session_id and message `id` field from the conversation JSON at `~/.snowflake/cortex/conversations/`
   - Known issue entries: `Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-12`
   - Table rows: add a `Source` column
   - Changelog bullets: `- **2026-03-12** [claude-code]: description`
5. Read `.claude/memory/memory.md` at the start of every session. Load other memory files only when relevant.
6. If a file doesn't exist yet, create it.
7. Don't wait to be asked. Don't wait for session end.

## Recall Rules

When asked "do you remember?" or about a URL/artifact/file you created:
1. First search memory files (`grep` across `~/.claude/memory/`)
2. If not found, search session transcripts (environment-aware):
   - If `CORTEX_SESSION_ID` present: `grep -r "<keyword>" ~/.snowflake/cortex/conversations/ --include="*.json"`
   - If `CORTEX_SESSION_ID` absent: `grep -r "<keyword>" ~/.claude/projects/ --include="*.jsonl"`  
   - For comprehensive search: check both locations regardless of environment
3. If not found, search MLflow traces (`sqlite3 ~/mlflow.db "SELECT request_id, key, value FROM trace_request_metadata WHERE value LIKE '%<keyword>%'"`)
4. Only say "I don't remember" after ALL THREE come up empty
Memory files are incomplete — transcripts and traces are the full record.

## Placement Test

When learning a user preference or insight, apply this test:
- "Would I need this to behave correctly even if I never look it up?" → `rules/`
- "Is this reference data I look up for a specific task?" → `memory/`
- "Is this contextual reasoning that helps me make better decisions?" → `lessons/`

**Admission test for lessons**: Must (1) generalize beyond one incident, AND (2) add reasoning value beyond a bare imperative. If it's just "always do X" → rule. If it's just "I did X wrong" → failure pattern.

## Graduation Chain

```
Failure Pattern  →  Lesson  →  Rule
  (incident)        (insight)    (imperative)
```

- **FP → Lesson**: When the insight generalizes beyond one incident. Test: "Does this apply to a *class* of problems?" The FP stays (marked `[graduated]`), the lesson captures the reasoning.
- **Lesson → Rule**: When "The Lesson" can be stated as a bare imperative without needing context. Test: "Can I follow this correctly without knowing *why*?" Extract the imperative into `rules/`. The lesson stays as the "why" behind the rule.
- **Not everything graduates.** Some lessons stay lessons forever.

## Lessons File Structure

Top-level `lessons/` directory (not inside `memory/`). One file per domain, multiple lessons per file separated by `---`. Template:

```markdown
# [Short title]

**domain:** evals | merlin | claude-code | prompting | general
**status:** active | deprecated
**discovered:** YYYY-MM-DD
**origin:** failure-pattern | exploration | external | user-directive
**related:** [optional: failure pattern title, rule filename, or memory file]

## Context / ## Approach / ## The Lesson / ## Boundaries
```

Load on-demand when working in the relevant domain. Never auto-load.

## File Structure

- `memory.md` — index of all memory files
- `general.md` — cross-project facts, preferences, environment setup
- `domain/{topic}.md` — domain-specific knowledge (one file per topic)
- `tools/{tool}.md` — tool configs, CLI patterns, workarounds

## Git Sync

After any memory or settings file changes:
1. **Prefix commit messages** with `[claude-code]` or `[cortex-code]` to track which system made changes
2. **Commit and push**: `cd ~/.claude && git add -A && git commit -m "[system-prefix] describe change" && git push`
3. **Examples**: 
   - `[cortex-code] Reorganize memory: fix failure pattern counts`
   - `[claude-code] Add new Jira skill with MCP integration`

## Error Classification

Every failure pattern header includes a `[type]` tag after severity:

| Type | Meaning | Action |
|------|---------|--------|
| `[deterministic]` | Wrong schema, wrong tool, missed instruction, format violation | Conclude immediately — the fix is known. Write a specific prevention rule. |
| `[infrastructure]` | Timeout, rate limit, network error, MCP flakiness | Log it. Do NOT draw conclusions from a single occurrence. Only write a prevention rule after a pattern emerges across multiple sessions. |

Format: `### Title (date) [severity] [type] [system-source]`

When tagging a new failure, classify it before writing. Ask: "Would a retry fix this?" Yes → infrastructure. No → deterministic.

## Failure Pattern Graduation

When a failure pattern's prevention rule has been copied into a `rules/` file (making it auto-enforced), mark the pattern header with `[graduated]`:

`### Title (date) [severity] [type] [graduated] [system-source]`

Graduated patterns stay in `failure-patterns.md` — they are NOT archived or removed. Graduation means the rule is now enforced structurally, but the pattern remains as audit trail and eval reference. The user is actively doing evals on failure patterns and needs the full history.

To check graduation status: compare each pattern's prevention rule against `rules/*.md` content. If the rule text appears in a rules file, the pattern qualifies for graduation.

## Reorganize Memory

When the user says "reorganize memory": read all files, remove duplicates/outdated entries, merge related entries, split oversized files, re-sort by date, scan transcripts for unsaved knowledge, update index, show summary.
