---
name: confluence-page-builder
description: Build Confluence pages (requirements docs, design docs, mappings tables) using standardized DSSDSA templates with proper storage format HTML
allowed-tools:
  - mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_create_page
  - mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_update_page
  - mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_get_page
  - mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_get_page_by_title
  - mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_get_page_children
  - mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_search_content
  - mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_attach_file
  - mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_get_attachments
  - mcp__universal-doc__read_document
  - mcp__universal-doc__read_spreadsheet_range
  - Read
  - Write
  - Bash
  - Edit
  - Glob
  - Grep
---

**Routing:** Check `$ARGUMENTS` to determine the preset:
- `$ARGUMENTS` is empty → **Page Selection**: Ask the user which page(s) they want to create or update (see [Page Selection](#page-selection) below)
- `$ARGUMENTS` is `requirements` → **Requirements Page**: Build a full requirements document using the DSSDSA template
- `$ARGUMENTS` is `design` → **Design Document**: Build a design doc with TOC and content sections
- `$ARGUMENTS` is `mappings` → **Mappings Table**: Build a field mappings/transformations table from a CSV/TSV source file
- `$ARGUMENTS` is `update` → **Update Mode**: Read an existing page, make targeted updates, increment version

---

## Page Selection

When invoked without arguments, walk the user through two questions:

### Question 1: Where in Confluence

Read the Confluence Key Pages table from `~/.claude/skills/workspace-references/SKILL.md` and present known pages:

```
Which Confluence page are you working with?

1. QMDS (1418323123)
2. MMM (1418323089)
3. Hulu Media360 (1418326821)
4. Meltwater Requirements (2106617203)
5. Meltwater Design Document (2106617208)
6. Other — enter a page ID, URL, or page title to search for

Pick one (1-6):
```

If the user picks 6, accept a page ID, a `confluence.disney.com` URL (extract the page ID from it), or a page title (use `mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_get_page_by_title` to resolve it).

### Question 2: What to build

After the page is resolved, ask what to do with it:

```
What would you like to do?

1. Create Requirements Page — full requirements doc (DSSDSA template, interactive intake) as a child of [selected page]
2. Create Design Document — design doc with TOC and content sections as a child of [selected page]
3. Create Mappings Table — field mappings/transformations table from CSV/TSV/Sheet as a child of [selected page]
4. Update This Page — read [selected page] and make targeted edits
5. Create Requirements + Design Doc — create both as parent/child pages under [selected page]

Pick one (1-5):
```

After the user picks, route to the corresponding preset workflow with the page ID already resolved. Option 5 runs the requirements preset with the optional mappings step (Step 4) treated as expected rather than optional.

---

## Before Starting

1. Read `~/.claude/references/confluence-page-templates.md` for HTML templates
2. Read `~/.claude/memory/tools/confluence.md` for MCP tool names, space keys, and version management rules
3. Read `~/.claude/rules/confluence.md` for behavioral rules (always read before update, use storage format, etc.)

---

## Preset: Requirements Page

Build a requirements document with the standard DSSDSA structure.

### Workflow (Interactive Step-by-Step)

**Step 1: Title + Briefing**
Ask the user for:
- Page title (vendor/project name)
- Briefing document or source material (Google Doc URL, local file path, or "I'll provide text")
- Parent page ID (or default to DSSDSA space root)

**Step 2: Read + Auto-Populate**
Read the source material:
- Google Doc URL → extract document ID, use `mcp__universal-doc__read_document` with `doc://google/document/{id}` URI
- Local file → use `Read`
- User-provided text → use directly

Auto-populate sections from the briefing: Background, Overview, Goals, Problem Statement, Assumptions (with Non-Functional Support table), Business Logic & Join Logic table, Use Cases. Show the user a summary of what was extracted:
```
Extracted from briefing:
  ✓ Background — [1-line preview]
  ✓ Overview — [1-line preview]
  ✓ Goals — [count] goals identified
  ✓ Problem Statement — [1-line preview]
  ✓ Assumptions — [count] assumptions
  ✓ Business Logic — [count] join/logic rules
  ✗ Stakeholders — not found (will ask next)
  ✗ Data Owners — not found (will ask next)
```

**Step 3: Ask for Missing Context**
Prompt the user for items briefings rarely contain:
- **Stakeholders**: "Who are the stakeholders? (names + roles, or 'skip' to leave blank)"
- **Data Owners / POCs**: "Who are the data owners or points of contact? (names + roles, or 'skip')"
- **Metadata fields**: Target release date, DATA Jira ticket key, Engineering Epic key (or 'skip' for each)

**Step 4: Mappings Table (Optional)**
Ask: "Do you have a field mappings CSV/Sheet for a companion design doc? (path, Google Sheet URL, or 'no')"
- If yes → read the file, preview the first 5 rows, confirm column mapping, and note that a child design doc page will be created after the requirements page.
- If no → skip.

**Step 5: Review Before Creating**
Show a section-by-section summary for final review:
```
Page: [title]
Space: DSSDSA | Parent: [parent page or "space root"]

Sections:
  1. Details Macro — Target release: [value], DATA Ticket: [value], Epic: [value]
  2. Background — [preview]
  3. Overview — [preview]
  4. Stakeholders — [names or "placeholder"]
  5. Data Owners — [names or "placeholder"]
  6. Goals — [count] items
  7. Problem Statement — [preview]
  8. Assumptions — [count] items + Non-Functional Support table
  9. Business Logic — [count] rules
  10. Use Cases — [count] items
  11. Questions — placeholder
  12. Open Execution Items — placeholder
  13. Out of Scope — placeholder
  14. Stakeholder Signoffs — placeholder

Ready to create? (yes / edit section [number])
```

If the user says "edit section [N]", ask for the updated content and re-show the summary.

**Step 6: Build + Create**
Build the HTML body using the Requirements Page template from `references/confluence-page-templates.md`:
- Details macro with metadata table
- TOC macro
- All standard sections populated from steps 2-3
- Empty sections with placeholder `<br />` tags — never omit sections

Create the page via `mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_create_page` with:
- `spaceKey`: DSSDSA (default)
- `title`: user-provided title
- `body`: the constructed HTML
- `parentId`: user-provided or looked up

If a mappings file was provided in Step 4, create the companion design doc as a child page using the **Mappings Table** preset workflow.

**Step 7: Confirm**
Show the user the page URL, title, and child page URL (if mappings were created).

---

## Preset: Design Document

Build a design document with TOC and structured content.

### Workflow

1. **Gather inputs**: page title, parent page ID, source data (CSV/TSV file, Google Sheet, or manual field list)

2. **Build the HTML body** using the Design Document template:
   - TOC macro at the top
   - Content sections as `<h2>` or `<h4>` headings
   - If a mappings table is part of the design doc, include it using the auto-numbered table template

3. **Create the page** via MCP tool.

---

## Preset: Mappings Table

Build a field mappings/transformations table from a structured data source.

### Workflow

1. **Read the source file**:
   - CSV: `pandas.read_csv(path)` — check encoding (UTF-16 tab-separated is common for vendor exports: `encoding='utf-16', sep='\t'`)
   - Google Sheet: `mcp__universal-doc__read_spreadsheet_range` with `doc://google/spreadsheet/{id}` URI
   - Manual: user provides field list directly

2. **Map columns** to the standard 5-column format:
   - `#` (auto-numbered)
   - `Field Name`
   - `Data Type`
   - `Sample Values`
   - `Definition`

   If the source has different column names, ask the user to confirm the mapping.

3. **Generate HTML** using the auto-numbered table template from `references/confluence-page-templates.md`:
   - Table attributes: `class="wrapped relative-table"`, `data-snooker-col-series="numbers"`, `data-snooker-locked-cols="0"`
   - Each row: `numberingColumn` cell + data cells with `color:var(--ds-text,#333333)` text styling
   - Column widths: ~5% / ~17% / ~16% / ~20% / ~42%

4. **Create or update the page** — if updating an existing design doc, read the page first, merge the table into the existing body, increment the version number.

---

## Preset: Update Mode

Update an existing Confluence page with targeted changes.

### Workflow

1. **Read the page** via `mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_get_page` to get:
   - Current version number
   - Existing HTML body

2. **Make targeted edits** to the HTML body — do not regenerate the entire page.

3. **Update the page** via `mcp__confluence-disney__confluence_update_page` with:
   - `pageId`: the page ID
   - `title`: existing title (or new if renaming)
   - `body`: modified HTML
   - `version`: current version + 1

---

## Examples

### Example 1: Build a requirements page from a briefing doc (interactive)

```
User: Build a Confluence requirements page for the Meltwater integration. Here's the briefing: ~/Downloads/meltwater_api_de_briefing.md
```

**Step 1**: Claude confirms the title ("Meltwater: Requirements") and briefing path. Asks for parent page ID or defaults to DSSDSA root.

**Step 2**: Claude reads the briefing, extracts Background, Overview, Goals, Assumptions, Business Logic, and Use Cases. Shows the extraction summary with checkmarks for populated sections and X marks for Stakeholders and Data Owners.

**Step 3**: Claude asks: "Who are the stakeholders?" → User provides names. "Who are the data owners/POCs?" → User provides names. "Any metadata? (target release, DATA ticket, epic)" → User provides or skips.

**Step 4**: Claude asks about mappings CSV. User says "yes, ~/Downloads/Export_Secret_Lives.csv" → Claude previews the first 5 rows and confirms column mapping.

**Step 5**: Claude shows the full section-by-section summary. User reviews and says "yes" to create.

**Step 6-7**: Claude builds the HTML, creates the requirements page, creates the companion design doc with mappings table as a child page, and shows both page URLs.

### Example 2: Build a mappings table from a CSV export

```
User: Create a design doc with field mappings from ~/Downloads/Export_Secret_Lives.csv
```

The skill reads the CSV (detecting UTF-16 tab encoding), maps columns to Field Name / Data Type / Sample Values / Definition, generates an auto-numbered Confluence table with 43+ rows, and creates the design document page with TOC + mappings table.

### Example 3: Update an existing page

```
User: Update the Meltwater requirements page (2106617203) — add a new use case for Disney+ international
```

The skill reads the current page, finds the Use Cases section in the HTML, appends the new use case as a list item matching the existing format, and updates the page with version incremented.

---

## Guidelines

- **Always read the page before updating.** Never blindly overwrite — merge changes into the existing HTML body.
- **Always increment the version number** when updating. Failure to do so causes a 409 Conflict error.
- **Use Confluence storage format XHTML**, not markdown. All content must use the `ac:structured-macro` patterns from the templates reference.
- **Preserve existing HTML structure** when updating. Don't reformat or clean up existing markup — only modify the targeted sections.
- **For CSV/TSV parsing**, always check encoding. Vendor exports commonly use UTF-16 with tab separators. Use pandas with explicit `encoding` and `sep` parameters.
- **Google Doc URIs** must use the `doc://google/document/{id}` scheme, not raw `https://docs.google.com/...` URLs. Extract the document ID from the URL first.
- **Default space is DSSDSA** unless the user specifies otherwise.
- **Blue header styling** (`highlight-#0065ff` with white text) is required for all table header rows in requirements pages. Design doc mappings tables use plain `<th scope="col">` headers.
- **Never omit template sections.** Even if no content is available, include the section header and an empty `<br />` placeholder. The user fills these in later.
- **Large tables** (40+ rows): Build the HTML in a local file first, then pass it to the MCP create/update tool. This avoids truncation in tool parameters.

File: lessons/claude-code.md
================
# Claude Code Lessons

---

# Rules alone don't prevent systematic skipping

**domain:** claude-code
**status:** active
**discovered:** 2026-03-30
**origin:** failure-pattern
**related:** FP #33 (plan without consulting memory), rules/general.md Plan Consultation section
**traces:** tr-99b9e238edb56d27cc512359b9313815

## Context
Claude Code has a rule: "Before drafting any plan, read failure patterns, known issues, and relevant memory." Despite the rule being auto-loaded in every session and enforced by a UserPromptSubmit hook, the pattern keeps recurring — plans get drafted from conversation context alone.

## Approach
The rule was added after the first occurrence. When it recurred, a UserPromptSubmit hook (`plan-consultation-check.sh`) was added to structurally enforce it. Even with both the rule and the hook, the pattern still surfaces — the hook reminds to consult, but doesn't verify that findings were actually incorporated into the plan. The failure mode isn't "didn't know the rule" — it's "skipped the rule because the task felt straightforward enough to draft from context."

## The Lesson
Structural enforcement (rules + hooks) prevents forgetting but not shortcutting. When a rule keeps getting violated despite enforcement, the fix isn't more enforcement — it's understanding why the shortcut feels justified and making the correct path feel equally fast. For plan consultation: always open failure patterns *before* thinking about the plan, not after drafting it.

## Boundaries
Doesn't apply to trivial plans (e.g., "rename this variable") where consulting memory would be overhead with no value. Only applies to plans that touch system behavior, create new files/directories, or modify workflows.

---

# Prefer the storage layer over the SDK for ad-hoc queries

**domain:** claude-code
**status:** active
**discovered:** 2026-03-09
**origin:** failure-pattern
**related:** FP #36 (MLflow SDK failures), rules/mlflow.md Trace Search section
**traces:** tr-4f7c9e1a460f55d4409f24209ecc0b78

## Context
Needed to search MLflow traces for specific content (prompts, URLs, keywords). The MLflow Python SDK (`search_traces()`) was the obvious tool — it's the official API. But it has pagination limits, deprecated parameters, and non-obvious column names that caused repeated failures.

## Approach
After multiple failed SDK attempts (wrong filter syntax, truncated results, deprecated `filter_string` param), switched to querying the SQLite database directly. Immediate success — simpler syntax, no pagination, full result sets. The SDK is designed for programmatic operations (tagging, exporting batches), not exploratory queries.

## The Lesson
When choosing between a tool's SDK and its underlying storage for ad-hoc queries, prefer the storage layer. SDKs add abstraction that helps programmatic operations but hurts exploration — pagination, version drift, non-obvious column names. This applies to MLflow->SQLite, and likely any system with a queryable backing store (e.g., Jira->REST API vs MCP wrapper, Docker->CLI vs SDK).

## Boundaries
Use the SDK when you need programmatic batch operations (tagging 100 traces, exporting with transformations). The storage layer is for exploration and search, not for write-heavy workflows.

---

# Notification aggregation links are never direct message links

**domain:** claude-code
**status:** active
**discovered:** 2026-03-18
**origin:** failure-pattern
**related:** FP #26-28 (Teams mentions cluster), rules/teams.md Mentions Catch-Up section
**traces:** tr-da9c1ba5da39f4016d799c8e4fb0c4dd, tr-9967bd325581ab45e00a06bce969329c, tr-dec9f2cd46f8bc61a13ece8efdcc4db0

## Context
Building a Teams mentions catch-up workflow. The activity feed provides `activityLink` URLs for each mention. These seemed like direct links to the mentioned message — but they're actually aggregated notification links (e.g., `nr:system:clump:Mentions`) that open a notification summary, not the specific message.

## Approach
First attempt used `activityLink` directly — produced links to notification clumps, not messages. Second attempt used channel-level links — showed the right channel but not the right thread. Third attempt used MCP `teams_search` to find the actual message and extract its `messageLink` field — this was the correct approach. Three separate failure patterns were created from what was really one underlying insight.

## The Lesson
In any system with a notification/activity feed, the links provided in notifications are aggregation links designed for the notification UI, not direct links to the underlying content. Always resolve the actual content link through the system's search or content API. This applies to Teams (activityLink vs messageLink), and likely to any platform with notification aggregation (Slack activity, GitHub notification URLs, Jira activity stream).

## Boundaries
If the notification system explicitly provides a `directLink` or `messageLink` field, that field can be trusted. The issue is specifically with links labeled for the notification view (activityLink, notificationUrl, etc.).

---

# Browser auth failures should trigger cache cleanup before investigation

**domain:** claude-code
**status:** active
**discovered:** 2026-03-30
**origin:** known-issue (cli-universe stale tokens)
**related:** known-issues.md (SingletonLock), memory/tools/cli-universe.md, rules/teams.md Browser Auth section, FP #32
**traces:** tr-e1a28417b746194eea6c9cacfdd45ad7

## Context
Teams auth hung during `teams auth login --no-cache`. Instead of immediately applying the documented workaround (clear SingletonLock + stale tokens), investigated the error, checked debug output, and tried to understand the state — wasting several turns before applying the fix that was already documented.

## Approach
The SingletonLock issue, stale tokens, and nuclear cleanup are all documented in `memory/tools/cli-universe.md` and referenced by `rules/teams.md` and `rules/outlook.md`. The symptom ("browser doesn't close automatically" / "auth hangs") maps directly to the known issue. But the documented fix wasn't applied as a first step.

## The Lesson
When a CLI Universe browser auth flow fails or hangs, the first action should always be the cleanup sequence: (1) kill stuck process, (2) remove SingletonLock, (3) clear stale tokens — then retry. Don't investigate first. This generalizes: when a known issue has a documented fix, apply the fix before diagnosing. Investigation is for *unknown* issues; known issues with documented workarounds should be applied reflexively.

## Boundaries
Only applies when the symptom clearly matches a documented known issue. If the auth error is novel (e.g., HTTP 403, new error message), investigate first.

---

# Edit before staging — knowing the checklist isn't enough if the order is wrong

**domain:** claude-code
**status:** active
**discovered:** 2026-03-30
**origin:** failure-pattern
**related:** known-issues.md (check-doc-sync.py blocks commits, 7+ occurrences), rules/general.md Git Discipline section
**traces:** none (sourced from known issue, not a single failure pattern)

## Context
The pre-commit hook (`check-doc-sync.py`) enforces doc-sync rules: README.md in every commit, memory.md when lessons/ or memory/ change, skills-catalog.md when skills/ change, etc. Despite the rules being auto-loaded, the hook being in place, and the checklist in CLAUDE.md, this keeps failing — 7+ occurrences and counting. The failure isn't limited to one target — it recurs across README.md, memory.md, and other sync targets.

## Approach
The rule was clear from the start. A pre-commit hook was added to structurally enforce it. The hook catches the violation every time — so the guardrail works. But the failure keeps happening in two distinct modes:

1. **Silent no-op**: Running `git add README.md` on an unmodified file, which git silently ignores. The commit proceeds without the file, and the hook blocks it.
2. **Incomplete checklist walk**: Remembering *some* sync targets but not all. E.g., editing and staging README.md (learned from past failures) but forgetting memory.md when lessons changed. Each time a target is learned, a different one gets missed — the checklist isn't being walked systematically.

## The Lesson
When a pre-commit hook enforces "files X, Y, Z must be in the commit," there are two failure modes, not one: (1) staging an unedited file (silent no-op), and (2) walking the checklist incompletely. The fix for both is the same: **before every `git commit`, read the full SYNC_RULES table in check-doc-sync.py, identify every target triggered by the staged files, then edit and stage each one**. Don't rely on memory of which targets are needed — read the rules every time. A checklist you walk from memory will always have gaps; a checklist you read from source won't.

## Boundaries
Only applies to git workflows with doc-sync hooks that require specific files in every commit. Doesn't generalize to checklists where order doesn't matter or where each step has visible confirmation of success.

---

# Read the format before writing the format

**domain:** claude-code
**status:** active
**discovered:** 2026-03-31
**origin:** failure-pattern
**related:** cortex-code pattern #4 ("Added failure pattern without checking existing format and structure first"), failure pattern #33 (skill invocation blocker)
**traces:** current session (pending trace ID)

## Context

When adding a new failure pattern, I drafted it from memory of the format — omitting trace IDs and the Related field. The user had to correct me twice ("dont we add traceids?" and "What are all the columns?"). This is the same class of error as cortex-code pattern #4, which happened in a different system months earlier but was never generalized into a lesson.

## Approach

The instinct is to save time by drafting structured content from recalled format rather than opening the file. This feels efficient but trades a 2-second file read for a multi-turn correction loop that wastes far more time and erodes trust.

## The Lesson

Before producing any entry that follows an established format (failure patterns, memory entries, table rows, changelog lines, known issues), always read 1-2 existing examples from the source file first — even if you "know" the format. Formats evolve (fields get added, conventions change), and memory of the format is always a snapshot of when you last read it, not the current state.

The general principle: **the source file is the schema**. If you're adding a row, read the table. If you're adding a pattern, read the patterns. If you're adding a lesson, read the lessons.

## Boundaries

- Does NOT apply to free-form content (messages, explanations, code) — only to structured entries with an established format.
- Does NOT mean you need to read the entire file — 1-2 recent examples is enough to calibrate.
- If the file doesn't exist yet (you're creating the first entry), this doesn't apply — but document the format you chose so the next entry can follow it.

# Known Issues — Environment & Tool Problems

Last refreshed: 2026-03-25
Known issues: 20 across 9 categories

## claude-code (6 issues)

### MLflow tracing env vars under wrong settings.json key are silently ignored
Workaround: Claude Code only reads environment variables from the "env" key in settings.json. Variables under an "environment" key are silently ignored. Always put MLFLOW_TRACKING_URI and MLFLOW_CLAUDE_TRACING_ENABLED under the "env" key alongside other env vars (AWS_PROFILE, etc). If tracing stops working, check settings.json for misplaced keys.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-23

### Stop hook payload does not include cost, token usage, or model fields
Description: The Claude Code Stop hook JSON payload only contains session_id, transcript_path, cwd, permission_mode, hook_event_name, stop_hook_active, and last_assistant_message. Fields like cost.total_cost_usd, context_window.current_usage.*, and model.display_name are not present.
Workaround: Parse the transcript JSONL file (available via transcript_path in the payload) to extract token usage from assistant message entries (message.usage). Include subagent transcripts at {session_dir}/subagents/*.jsonl. Compute cost from token counts using Bedrock pricing. See ~/.claude/hooks/capture-cost.py for the working implementation.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-27

### MCP stdio server fails silently when logger writes to stdout
Description: MCP servers using stdio transport (command-based in mcp.json) communicate via stdin/stdout JSON-RPC. If the server's logger uses console.log() or console.debug() — which write to stdout — the non-JSON-RPC output corrupts the protocol handshake. Claude Code silently fails to connect and the server's tools never appear, even though the server starts without errors when tested manually.
Workaround: All log output in stdio MCP servers must go to stderr, not stdout. Replace console.log() with console.error() (prefixed with [INFO]) and console.debug() with console.error() (prefixed with [DEBUG]) in the logger module. console.error() and console.warn() already go to stderr and are safe. After fixing, rebuild the server and restart Claude Code.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-03

### MCP servers defined in ~/.claude/mcp.json are not loaded by Claude Code
Description: Claude Code reads MCP server configuration from the mcpServers key in ~/.claude.json (the root config file), not from ~/.claude/mcp.json. Servers defined only in mcp.json will silently fail to appear in /mcp and their tools will not be available. This is confusing because mcp.json looks like the right place for MCP config.
Workaround: Define all MCP servers in the top-level mcpServers key of ~/.claude.json. The ~/.claude/mcp.json file is not read by Claude Code and can be removed. Format: for stdio servers use {"command": "...", "args": [...]}, for SSE use {"type": "sse", "url": "..."}, for HTTP use {"type": "http", "url": "..."}.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-03

### SSH passphrase prompt blocks Claude Code startup and causes lag
Description: Claude Code startup hooks (git sync) trigger SSH operations against github.twdcgrid.net. Without macOS Keychain integration, the SSH key passphrase prompt appears inline, blocking startup and making Claude Code appear laggy/frozen.
Workaround: Add Host * block with AddKeysToAgent yes and UseKeychain yes to ~/.ssh/config. Add ssh-add --apple-use-keychain lines to ~/.zshrc for both keys (id_rsa, id_ed25519). Run ssh-add --apple-use-keychain once to store the passphrase in Keychain.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-03

### check-doc-sync.py pre-commit hook blocks commits for trivial skill/script changes that don't need doc updates
Description: The check-doc-sync.py pre-commit hook requires CLAUDE.md, README.md, or memory.md to be staged whenever skills/, scripts/, or memory/ files change. It checks file presence in the staged set but not whether the changes actually warrant doc updates. Minor fixes (escaping a character, removing an unused tool, fixing a typo) trigger the same requirement as substantive changes, forcing trivial edits to doc files just to pass the hook.
Workaround: When committing skill/script/memory changes, always stage CLAUDE.md, README.md, and/or memory.md alongside them — even if only a trivial edit is needed (e.g., rewording a description, updating a date). Check which targets are required by reading the SYNC_RULES in check-doc-sync.py. Alternatively, the hook can be bypassed with --no-verify for genuinely trivial changes, but this should be rare.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-06 | Occurrences: 7

## general (1 issue)

### Claude filters by column name keywords instead of filtering by the correct column when querying spreadsheets
Workaround: When querying a spreadsheet for rows belonging to a specific team, owner, or category, filter on the explicit column (e.g. Team Name) rather than matching keywords across all columns. Always confirm the filter column and criteria with the user before executing the query.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-24

## github (1 issue)

### Auto-generated files left untracked after plan implementation
Workaround: After implementing a plan, always run git status to check for untracked or uncommitted files before considering the task complete. Commit and push any missing files.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-23

## google-workspace (2 issues)

### Universal-doc MCP cannot read individual tabs in multi-tab Google Docs
Workaround: The universal-doc read_document tool only reads the default/first tab of a Google Doc. If a document uses the Google Docs tabs feature, content from non-default tabs will not be returned. Ask the user to either paste the content from other tabs, consolidate into the first tab, or share direct URLs to any linked documents referenced in other tabs.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-24

### universal-doc update_document strips formatting when writing to Google Docs
Description: The `mcp__universal-doc__update_document` tool converts content to plain markdown before writing back to Google Docs, which strips all existing formatting (headings, bold, links, indentation, etc.). The result is a poorly formatted document that requires manual reformatting. Reading via `read_document` works fine.
Workaround: Never use `update_document` to write to Google Docs. Instead, create or update a local markdown file (e.g., on `~/Desktop/`) and let the user copy-paste into the Google Doc with proper formatting. A rule in `rules/general.md` enforces this.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-17

## jira (3 issues)

### /jira-ticket-finder completed returns empty results at sprint start since no tickets are completed yet
Workaround: At the start of a new sprint, modify the JQL to query sprint in closedSprints() and filter to the most recent closed sprint, or use a specific sprint ID to target the previous sprint.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-25

### MCP SSE transport leaks session entries in _read_stream_writers dictionary
Description: The mcp library's SseServerTransport (mcp/server/sse.py) closes memory streams on client disconnect but never removes the session UUID from the _read_stream_writers dict. Over time this causes unbounded dictionary growth. Not fixed upstream as of mcp 1.26.0.
Workaround: Fix is baked into the Docker image (Dockerfile RUN step applies the patch at build time). No runtime patching needed. If the patch is missing, rebuild the image: cd ~/audience-jira-mcp-server && ./build_docker_image.sh. If the build fails, check if upstream mcp fixed the leak (the patch target line changed).
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-03

### SSE health check false-negative: curl exit code is non-zero on streaming endpoints even when HTTP 200 is returned
Description: SSE endpoints stream events indefinitely, so curl with --max-time always exits with code 28 (operation timeout) even after receiving a valid HTTP 200 response. Health checks that rely on curl exit code == 0 will always report SSE as unhealthy.
Workaround: Use curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}" --max-time 3 and check if stdout is "200" instead of checking curl exit code. The HTTP status code is received immediately even though the stream never ends. Also ensure you check /sse (the actual SSE endpoint), not / (which returns 404).
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-02

## mlflow (3 issues)

### MLflow server must use SQLite backend or traces are silently lost
Workaround: Always start MLflow with: mlflow server --host 127.0.0.1 --port 5001 --backend-store-uri sqlite:////Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db &. Without --backend-store-uri, MLflow defaults to file-based ./mlruns which silently loses traces. Verify with: sqlite3 /Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db 'SELECT COUNT(*) FROM trace_info;'. If the UI shows no traces, check the Traces tab (not Runs) and hard-refresh the browser.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-23

### SQLite URI with 3 slashes is relative, causing MLflow to create a new DB in the wrong location
Workaround: Always use 4 slashes for absolute paths in SQLite URIs: sqlite:////Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db (not sqlite:///Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db). Three slashes makes the path relative to the working directory, so if MLflow starts from ~/.claude/ via a hook, it creates the DB at ~/.claude/Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db instead of /Users/sameul.nasir/mlflow.db. If this happens, merge traces back with: sqlite3 wrong.db '.dump trace_info' | sqlite3 right.db
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-27

### MLflow trace session ID is in trace_metadata, not request_metadata
Description: The mlflow.trace.session field is stored in trace_metadata, not request_metadata. search_traces() filter strings like metadata.`mlflow.trace.session` work because they search across both, but iterating results and accessing request_metadata directly returns empty.
Workaround: When iterating search_traces results, read session ID from row.trace_metadata['mlflow.trace.session'], not row.request_metadata. The search_traces filter_string parameter searches both metadata dicts, so filter queries work fine — the issue only surfaces when accessing the field directly on result rows.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-02-27

## teams (2 issues)

### Editing messages renders @mentions as raw text instead of clickable tags
Description: Both MCP `teams_edit_message` and CLI `teams --agent message edit` do not properly render @mentions. Both markdown @[Name](mri) syntax and HTML <at> tag syntax are passed through as literal text in the edited message. Sending a new message renders @mentions correctly, but editing breaks them. This applies to both tools — it's a Teams API limitation, not a tool bug.
Workaround: Do not use message edit (MCP or CLI) to add or fix @mentions. If @mentions are needed, delete the broken message (`teams --agent message delete --chat-id <id> --message-id <id>`) and re-send a new one via `teams --agent message send` or `teams --agent channel send`. Get the mention formatting right on the first send. When cc'ing people, always prefix with 'cc: ' before the @mentions in the original send call.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-04 | Updated: 2026-03-23 (confirmed same bug in CLI)

### Claude unnecessarily bolds thread titles when creating Teams threads
Description: When asked to create a new thread in a Teams channel, Claude wraps the title in **markdown bold** syntax (e.g. **[Title]**). This is unnecessary — thread titles should be sent as plain text. The bold formatting makes the post look odd and doesn't match how users normally create threads.
Workaround: When creating a new Teams thread, never wrap the title/root message in markdown bold. Send the title as plain text. Only use formatting (bold, italic, etc.) when the user explicitly asks for it.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-04

## cli-universe (1 issue)

### Microsoft browser auth uses stale cached tokens/session, causing silent auth failures
Description: The CLI Universe browser auth flow (used by Teams and Outlook CLIs) caches tokens in `~/.cliuniverse/ms-tokens.json` and session state in `~/.cliuniverse/session-state.json`. When Microsoft tokens expire, the CLI doesn't auto-clear the cache — it silently fails or tries to reuse stale tokens. Additionally, Chrome can leave a stale `SingletonLock` symlink in `~/.cliuniverse/browser-profile/` after a crash, preventing the browser from launching for re-auth.
Workaround: (1) Always use `--no-cache` when re-authenticating: `{tool} auth login --no-cache`. (2) If browser fails to launch with SingletonLock error: `rm ~/.cliuniverse/browser-profile/SingletonLock` then retry. (3) Nuclear option: `rm ~/.cliuniverse/ms-tokens.json ~/.cliuniverse/session-state.json` then re-auth.
Source: manual | claude-code | 2026-03-25

## cortex-code (1 issue)

### Cortex Code tracing creates session-level traces making specific error debugging difficult
Description: Cortex Code traces are captured at the session level rather than per-message, making it harder to pinpoint specific errors within a conversation. Unlike Claude Code traces which map to individual tool calls, Cortex traces bundle the entire session.
Workaround: When debugging Cortex Code errors, search the conversation JSON files directly at ~/.snowflake/cortex/conversations/ and cross-reference with the session-level MLflow trace. Use the cortex_to_mlflow_converter.py script to ensure traces are in MLflow for unified analysis.
Source: manual | cortex-code | 2026-03-12

## Finalized Axial Code Definitions (7 codes)

| Code | Pass Behavior | Fail Behavior | Count (P/F) |
|------|--------------|---------------|-------------|
| **commit_discipline** | Auto-commits after file changes, walks full sync checklist, stages all required docs | Waits for user to say "commit", misses sync targets, stages unedited files | 0P / 6F |
| **knowledge_consultation** | Reads rules, memory, known issues before acting; follows documented workflows | Skips available docs, stops recall early, ignores loaded rules | 2P / 7F |
| **proactive_compliance** | Applies rules/workarounds without prompting, flags issues before user notices | Doesn't flag redundancy, waits for user to point out rule violations | 3P / 1F |
| **output_fidelity** | Accurate data, correct format, verbatim preservation, deliverables match plan | Wrong counts, hallucinated data, altered text, wrong format, wrong URLs | 7P / 8F |
| **intent_comprehension** | Correctly interprets user request, resolves aliases, understands context | Misreads intent, executes wrong plan, confuses "create X" with "build tool for X" | 2P / 1F |
| **diagnostic_reasoning** | Root cause analysis, progressive refinement, correct classification, catches anomalies | Dismisses evidence, investigates wrong component, incomplete audit | 8P / 4F |
| **error_recovery** | Recovers from infrastructure errors transparently, delivers despite tool flakiness | Infrastructure failure blocks all output, no recovery attempted | 1P / 1F |

**Distribution**: diagnostic_reasoning (12) > output_fidelity (15) > knowledge_consultation (9) > commit_discipline (6) > proactive_compliance (4) > intent_comprehension (3) > error_recovery (2)

# Hook Architecture

Last updated: 2026-03-30

## Layers

Claude Code uses 6 layers of automated checks, each firing at a different point in the workflow.

### Layer 1: Git Pre-Commit Hook (`check-doc-sync.py`)
Fires on: `git commit` in `~/.claude/`
Blocks commit if rules violated. Runs pytest when test-relevant files are staged.

| Check | What It Does |
|-------|-------------|
| README.md required | Every commit must include README.md |
| hooks/settings/mcp → mlflow/README.md | Infra changes require mlflow doc update |
| skills/*/SKILL.md → CLAUDE.md | Skill changes require CLAUDE.md update |
| memory/ add/delete → memory.md | Memory file adds/deletes require index update |
| lessons/ → memory.md | Lesson changes require memory index update |
| pytest (conditional) | Runs tests when scripts/, hooks/, or tests/ files staged |

### Layer 2: SessionStart Hooks
Fires on: session begins (once). Stdout → injected into Claude's context.

| Hook | What It Does |
|------|-------------|
| `git-auto-pull.sh` | Pull latest from claude-settings remote |
| `inject-memory.sh` | Inject memory index, lessons index, failure patterns, known issues, last session summary |
| `ensure-mlflow.sh` | Start MLflow server if not running (port 5001, SQLite backend) |
| `health-check.py --mode session-start` | VPN, MLflow, Docker/Jira, SSE patch, token store, AWS creds, cost CSV health + anomaly |
| `sync-traces.sh` | Auto-sync traces.csv edits back to MLflow SQLite |

### Layer 3: UserPromptSubmit Hook
Fires on: every user message, before processing.

| Hook | What It Does |
|------|-------------|
| `plan-consultation-check.sh` | Enforce Plan Consultation rule — blocks plans drafted without reading memory/failure patterns |

### Layer 4: PreToolUse Hook
Fires on: before tool calls (matcher-specific).

| Hook | Matcher | What It Does |
|------|---------|-------------|
| `check-aws-ttl.sh` | Bash | Check AWS credential TTL; block if expired, warn if <5min, attempt refresh |
| `check-ms-auth-ttl.sh` | (all) | Check Teams/Outlook OAuth token TTL; Teams uses headless refresh, Outlook requires browser login |
| `enforce-plan-consultation.py` | Write\|Edit | Block plan file writes (`plans/*.md`) that lack an `## Informed By` section with actual content |

### Layer 5: PreCompact Hook
Fires on: before context window compaction.

| Hook | What It Does |
|------|-------------|
| `save-compact-state.py` | Save working state (.last-session.md) before context is trimmed |

### Layer 6: Stop Hooks
Fires on: session ends (once). Run sequentially in order.

| Hook | What It Does |
|------|-------------|
| MLflow `stop_hook_handler()` | Finalize MLflow trace, write to claude_tracing.log |
| `capture-cost.py` | Parse transcript JSONL, compute cost, write CSV, tag ALL session traces (2s delay + retroactive sweep for orphaned last-traces) |
| `health-check.py --mode stop` | Validate cost row (freshness, non-zero tokens, anomaly detection), macOS notification on failure |
| `maintain-check.py` | Memory index drift, changelog duplicates, auto-generated staleness, README accuracy, failure pattern trace ID validation |

### Additional: Weekly Cron
Fires on: Sundays 9 AM via launchd.

| Script | What It Does |
|--------|-------------|
| `maintain-weekly.py` | Consolidate changelogs, refresh memory, validate skills, git commit |

### Additional: Status Line
Always running during session.

| Script | What It Does |
|--------|-------------|
| `statusline.sh` | Displays session status in Claude Code status bar |

## Guidelines

- **Always confirm before adding a new artifact.** Show the extracted title, URL, and type — wait for user approval before modifying the SKILL.md file.
- **Don't add duplicate artifacts.** Before adding, check if the URL already exists in the current list. If it does, tell the user it's already tracked.
- **Increment numbering correctly.** New entries continue from the last number in their section (Docs, Sheets, or Slides), not from the overall last number.
- **When the user asks about a specific artifact**, use universal-doc tools to read it. Don't just display the URL — fetch and present the content.
- **If a Google Workspace URL can't be read** (permission denied, doc deleted), tell the user which artifact failed and suggest they check sharing settings.
- **Always read the template reference doc first** before creating new content from templates. Don't improvise layout when a reference exists.
- **Large Google Docs may be truncated** by the universal-doc tool. Warn the user and ask them to paste the missing sections.
- **Never update a Confluence page without reading it first.** Always read current content to avoid overwriting others' changes.

2. Asks the user for the new document content/topic
3. Creates a new Google Doc matching the PRD template formatting

**User**: `/workspace-references save` (after creating a new Google Doc in the conversation)

**Claude does**:
1. Finds the `create_document` call that produced a new doc
2. Extracts: Title = "Q2 Campaign Brief", URL = `https://docs.google.com/document/d/...`, Type = Google Docs
3. Shows the user: "Add this? Title: Q2 Campaign Brief, Type: Google Docs"
4. User confirms → Claude adds entry under Google Docs in this file
5. Confirms: "Artifact added to the tracked list under Google Docs."

## Save Mode

When `$ARGUMENTS` contains `save`, follow these steps to capture a new artifact from the conversation.

### Step 1: Find the Artifact

Review the conversation for Google Docs, Sheets, or Slides URLs or references. Look for:
- `docs.google.com/document/...`
- `docs.google.com/spreadsheets/...`
- `docs.google.com/presentation/...`
- Any `create_document`, `update_document`, or `read_document` tool calls that produced or referenced a document

If no artifact is found in the conversation, tell the user: "No Google Workspace artifact found in this conversation. Create or reference a Doc/Sheet/Slides first, then use `/workspace-references save` to track it." Then stop.

### Step 2: Extract Details

From the conversation, extract:
- **Document title/name**
- **URL** (full Google Docs/Sheets/Slides URL)
- **Type** (Google Docs, Google Sheets, or Google Slides)
- **Meeting date** (if mentioned, otherwise use today's date)

### Step 3: Confirm with the User

Show the extracted artifact and ask the user to confirm before adding:
```
Title: [name]
URL: [url]
Type: [type]
```

### Step 4: Update SKILL.md

Add the new artifact entry to the appropriate section (Google Docs, Google Sheets, or Google Slides) in this file, incrementing the number:
```
N. **[Title]**
   [URL]
```

Update the meeting date heading if this is from a new meeting date.

### Step 5: Confirm

Tell the user: "Artifact added to the tracked list under [type]."

# General Behavioral Rules

## Recall

When asked "do you remember making/doing X?" or about a URL/artifact not found in memory files, ALWAYS search session transcripts (`grep -r "<keyword>" ~/.claude/projects/ --include="*.jsonl"`) AND MLflow traces (`sqlite3 ~/mlflow.db "SELECT ... FROM trace_request_metadata WHERE value LIKE ..."`) before concluding you don't remember. Only say "I don't remember" after memory, transcripts, AND traces all come up empty.

## Completeness

When the user gives feedback to add/include something, implement ALL of what they said in a single pass. Do not partially implement and require a second correction. Re-read the user's message before finalizing edits to confirm nothing was missed.

## Google Docs — Never Write Directly

Never use `mcp__universal-doc__update_document` to write to Google Docs. The tool strips formatting and produces poor results. Instead, always create or update a local markdown file (e.g., on `~/Desktop/`) that the user can copy and paste into the Google Doc themselves. Reading Google Docs via `mcp__universal-doc__read_document` is fine.

## Spreadsheet Queries

When querying a spreadsheet for rows belonging to a specific team, owner, or category, filter on the explicit column name rather than matching keywords across all columns. Confirm the filter column and criteria with the user first.

## Git Discipline

- After implementing a plan or making changes, always run `git status` to check for untracked or uncommitted files before considering the task complete.
- **Auto-commit rule**: After creating or modifying any file under hooks/, scripts/, skills/, settings.json, mcp.json, or memory/, immediately commit and push as the final step of the task — do NOT wait for the user to say "commit and push". This is non-negotiable.
- **Pre-commit checklist** (run mentally before every `git commit` in `~/.claude`):
  1. **Every commit** must include `README.md` — even if only a trivial edit (update a count, date, description). No exceptions.
  2. Are any files under `skills/` staged? → Also stage `CLAUDE.md` and `memory/domain/skills-catalog.md`
  3. Are any files under `scripts/` or `hooks/` staged? → Also stage `mlflow/README.md`
  4. Are any files under `memory/` staged? → Also stage `memory.md` index
  5. Does `CLAUDE.md` need a skill count update? → Edit before staging
- **Trivial README edits**: When no substantive README change is needed, always make a trivial relevant edit (update a count, date, or description) so it can be staged. Never skip staging README because "nothing changed" — find something small to improve.
- Before committing, check the Documentation Sync Rules table in CLAUDE.md and cross-reference against this checklist.

## Repo Reviews

When the user asks to review a GitHub repo and apply its practices (testing, architecture, etc.), always save the repo URL and a summary of what was learned to the relevant memory file.

## Plan Consultation

When creating a plan, always read memory files, known issues (`domain/known-issues.md`), failure patterns (`domain/failure-patterns.md`), and relevant lessons (`lessons/{domain}.md`) before drafting. Reference any relevant findings in the plan so the user can see what informed the approach. Never propose a plan based solely on the current conversation — always ground it in system knowledge first.

## Path Verification

When updating rules or docs about file locations, verify actual paths with bash commands first. Never assume based on logic alone.

## Investigation Discipline

Don't conclude system-wide configuration issues from a single session or data point. Verify across multiple sessions before making definitive statements.

## Failure Pattern Self-Reporting

When you repeat a documented failure pattern, recognize and report it in real-time. Update the occurrence count in `failure-patterns.md` immediately — don't wait for the user to point it out.

================
File: memory/domain/failure-patterns.md

# Failure Patterns

Last refreshed: 2026-03-31
Total patterns: 34 across 4 categories

## claude-code (22 patterns)

### Did not invoke jira-ticket-finder via Skill tool across 3 requests due to disable-model-invocation flag (2026-03-31) [medium] [deterministic] [graduated] [claude-code]
Prevention: When a skill matches the user's request (via alias or keyword) but the Skill tool rejects it, investigate the cause immediately. If `disable-model-invocation: true` is set, evaluate whether it's still justified — if the skill's workflow can be executed by the Skill tool (sequential steps, no interactive input), remove the flag and invoke. Never silently fall back to manual execution without questioning the blocker. Working around a broken invocation path once is reasonable; doing it repeatedly without fixing it is the failure.
Recent triggers:
- "What jira tickets need my attention" — matched alias but fell back to manual execution (tr-7fe28b1983c2199e21136efde797789c)
- "run the skill" — tried Skill tool, hit disable-model-invocation, fell back to manual instead of fixing (current session, pending trace ID)
Related: Rule in `rules/skills.md` (Skill Invocation Failures section), SKILL ROUTING aliases in CLAUDE.md

### Did not apply documented SingletonLock fix when browser auth hung (2026-03-30) [medium] [deterministic] [claude-code]
Prevention: When a CLI Universe browser auth flow fails or hangs (browser doesn't close, auth times out), immediately apply the documented cleanup sequence from `memory/tools/cli-universe.md`: (1) `pkill -f "teams auth"` (or outlook), (2) `rm ~/.cliuniverse/browser-profile/SingletonLock`, (3) `rm ~/.cliuniverse/ms-tokens.json ~/.cliuniverse/session-state.json`, (4) retry with `--no-cache`. Do NOT investigate debug output or auth status first — the fix is documented and should be applied reflexively. Investigation is for unknown issues only.
Trigger: It didnt (tr-e1a28417b746194eea6c9cacfdd45ad7)
Related: Lesson "Browser auth failures should trigger cache cleanup before investigation" in `lessons/claude-code.md`

### Queried for non-existent tag key and falsely reported all traces untagged (2026-03-24) [medium] [deterministic] [claude-code]
Prevention: Before reporting trace tagging status, first run `SELECT DISTINCT key FROM trace_tags LIMIT 20` to discover actual tag key names. Never hardcode or assume tag key names (e.g., `session_tag`) — verify against the schema first. Then use the real keys to count tagged vs untagged traces. A query that returns "all untagged" should always be treated as suspicious and double-checked against total tag row counts.
Trigger: yes investigate (pending trace ID)

### Used wrong theme path when building Marp slides, ignoring memory/tools/marp.md (2026-03-23) [medium] [deterministic] [claude-code]
Prevention: Before running any Marp build command, always read `memory/tools/marp.md` for the correct build command, theme file path (`~/rose-pine-dawn-fixed.css`), and required flags (`--no-stdin`, `--theme-set`). Never guess theme paths or use non-existent directories. The working build command is documented — use it.

### Omitted MLflow traces from recall rule despite user explicitly saying to include them (2026-03-10) [high] [deterministic] [claude-code]

### Used MLflow Python SDK (search_traces()) repeatedly with wrong syntax to find a ... (2026-03-09) [medium] [deterministic] [claude-code]
Prevention: When searching MLflow traces for specific content (prompts, URLs, keywords), always query SQLite directly (sqlite3 ~/mlflow.db "SELECT ... FROM trace_request_metadata WHERE value LIKE ..." ) instead of the MLflow Python SDK (search_traces()). The SDK has pagination limits, deprecated parameters, and non-obvious column names that cause repeated failures. SQLite is faster, simpler, and already proven reliable. Reserve the Python SDK only for programmatic operations (tagging, exporting), not ad-hoc searches.
Trigger: ML Flow traces (tr-4f7c9e1a460f55d4409f24209ecc0b78)

### Dismissed growing untagged trace count as legacy provenance without investigating (2026-03-19) [medium] [deterministic] [claude-code]
Prevention: When the health check reports a count that the user says is growing, never dismiss it as a one-time legacy issue. Investigate the root cause: check timestamps (are they recent?), check what tags are missing vs present, and trace the tagging code path to find where it drops items. A growing count always indicates an active bug, not a historical artifact.

### Did not investigate root cause of growing untagged trace count — race condition in stop hook went undetected for weeks (2026-03-31) [high] [deterministic] [claude-code]
Prevention: When a stop hook tags traces by searching for session traces then tagging them, the final trace may not yet be flushed to the database at search time — creating a race condition where the last trace in every session is systematically missed. Fix: (1) add a delay before searching (`time.sleep(2)`), and (2) add a retroactive sweep that finds untagged traces, looks up tagged siblings in the same session, and copies their tags. When health-check reports a growing count of untagged items, always investigate whether the tagging code path has a timing dependency — a count that grows by exactly 1 per session is the signature of a race condition, not a legacy data issue.
Trigger: My missing traces keep rising. Please understand why. (tr-1a596cac9fb9e0c9bb224407919df934)
Related: Pattern "Dismissed growing untagged trace count as legacy provenance without investigating" (2026-03-19)

# Memory Index

Master index of all memory files. Updated whenever a file is created or modified.

---

| File | Description |
|------|-------------|
| `general.md` | Environment setup, user preferences, reference repos, internal tools (ham-sandwich AI dashboard), Databricks workspace |
| `tools/jira.md` | Jira curl templates (create, update, sprint), custom field IDs, issue type IDs, status lists, Docker/MCP setup, token management (search/JQL patterns in `rules/jira-workflow.md`) |
| `tools/mlflow.md` | MLflow server (port 5001, SQLite, auto-start hook), MCP config, cost tracking, CSV trace tagging workflow (export/sync/auto-sync hook), tag/refresh scripts |
| `tools/airtable.md` | Airtable base/table IDs, field names, filter patterns, Sam's L4s (behavioral rules in `rules/airtable.md`) |
| `tools/databricks.md` | Databricks auth workflow, CLI patterns, workspace reference pointers (behavioral rules in `rules/databricks.md`) |
| `tools/github.md` | GitHub multi-account switching — SSH keys, gh CLI, conditional gitconfig |
| `tools/marp.md` | Marp CLI build commands, Rose Pine Dawn theme patches (purple→gray, broken imports), frontmatter style overrides, known gotchas |
| `tools/cli-universe.md` | CLI Universe shared infrastructure — browser auth flow, token/session paths (`~/.cliuniverse/`), common flags, stale cache + SingletonLock troubleshooting, available CLIs table |
| `tools/hooks.md` | Hook architecture — 6 layers (pre-commit, SessionStart, UserPromptSubmit, PreToolUse, PreCompact, Stop), all checks inventory, auto-enforced via pre-commit sync rule |
| `tools/obsidian.md` | Obsidian CLI — vault at `~/Desktop/Sam Nasir`, key commands (read, search, create, tasks, tags, daily notes), no auth needed |
| `tools/confluence.md` | Confluence reference data — space keys, page IDs, MCP tools, storage format conventions, version management (behavioral rules in `rules/confluence.md`) |
| `domain/jira.md` | Jira project keys (QMDS, DSACQ, MEOW), board IDs, backlog sprint IDs, active epics, ticket defaults, Google Sheet IDs (active sprints looked up dynamically) |
| `domain/artifacts.md` | Artifact tracking rules — canonical list in `skills/workspace-references/SKILL.md` |
| `domain/skills-catalog.md` | Available Skills table (21 skills: 12 custom + 9 cli-universe) with descriptions and aliases |
| `domain/failure-patterns.md` | 31 failure patterns across 4 categories (claude-code 19, google-workspace 1, uncategorized 4, cortex-code 7) |
| `domain/saved-traces.md` | Golden dataset passing traces — 10 verified traces across 7 axial codes, 5 borderline candidates identified, tagged in MLflow + Google Sheet |
| `domain/known-issues.md` | Known environment/tool issues and workarounds with occurrence tracking (auto-generated by `refresh_known_issues.py`) |
| `domain/teams.md` | Teams topic-based conversation table + mentions catch-up workflow — search, resolve channel/meeting/chat, table format (Date, Channel, Thread link, Title of thread, Title of message, Owner), sort order, activity feed mentions |
| `domain/portability-plan.md` | Plan to make `~/.claude/` portable across machines — 11 steps, bootstrap.sh, path replacements (not yet implemented) |

# Memory Management

Maintain a structured memory system at `.claude/memory/`. Core rules (write rules, file structure, git sync) auto-load from `rules/memory-system.md`.

### Maintenance

When I say "reorganize memory":
1. Read all memory files
2. Remove duplicates and outdated entries
3. Merge entries that belong together
4. Split files that cover too many topics
5. Re-sort entries by date within each file
6. **Transcript scan**: Scan session transcripts since the last reorganize (or last 2 weeks if unknown) for unsaved knowledge. Search for:
   - External URLs (GitHub repos, docs) shared by the user
   - Explicit user preferences ("always do X", "never do Y")
   - Repeated tool workarounds that aren't in known issues
   - Architecture/convention decisions that affect future work
   Present candidates and ask which to save before writing.
7. Update `memory.md` index
8. Show a summary of what changed

# User Preferences

## System Routing Intelligence

**Purpose**: Intelligently route tasks between Claude Code and Cortex Code based on capabilities.

**Current System Detection**: Check for `CORTEX_SESSION_ID` environment variable:
- Present = Cortex Code (Snowflake-native, data tools)
- Absent = Claude Code (automation, integrations, general tasks)

**When to recommend Cortex Code** (if currently in Claude Code):
- Snowflake queries, data analysis, SQL operations
- Semantic models, semantic views, Cortex AI functions
- ML workflows, model training, Snowflake notebooks
- Data transformations, dbt projects on Snowflake
- Keywords: "analyze data", "run query", "check table", "semantic view", "snowflake", "sql", "cortex ai", "ml model"

**When to recommend Claude Code** (if currently in Cortex Code):
- Jira operations, Google Workspace, Teams integration
- General automation, skill management, health checks
- Memory management, trace analysis, system maintenance
- Keywords: "create ticket", "update doc", "post to teams", "jira", "google", "health check"

**Routing Format**: "This task would be better handled in [System]. Try: `[command example]`"

SKILL ROUTING (opt-in): When the user's message contains "skill", read `memory/domain/skills-catalog.md` and match their request to the Available Skills table. One match → invoke via Skill tool. Multiple matches → present options via AskUserQuestion. No match → suggest the closest skills. Aliases: "is jira working" / "system status" → health-check, "update my token" / "refresh my pat" → update-atlassian-token, "jira report" / "sprint report" / "what needs my attention" → jira-ticket-finder report, "check my pipelines" / "databricks tables" / "query databricks" / "unity catalog" → unity-databricks, "doc template" / "slides template" / "my artifacts" / "confluence page" → workspace-references, "build confluence page" / "requirements page" / "design doc" / "mappings table" → confluence-page-builder, "catch up on teams" / "what did I miss on teams" / "teams mentions" / "who mentioned me on teams" → Teams Mentions Catch-Up workflow (read `rules/teams.md` + `memory/domain/teams.md`). Report preset includes FiveTran Migration breakout, per-board risk analysis, ticket summaries in risk tables, and linked Jira keys. "snapshot my evals" / "export my evals" → workspace-references (golden dataset at `evals/golden-dataset.json`).

## Skill Loading Rules

- **Jira**: Before any Jira operation, always read `~/.claude/memory/tools/jira.md` and `~/.claude/memory/domain/jira.md`.
- **Teams**: Hybrid CLI+MCP — behavioral rules auto-load from `rules/teams.md`. Reference data (search workflow, table format, sheet ID) lives in `memory/domain/teams.md`.
- **Outlook**: Use the `outlook` CLI via Bash for all Outlook operations. Auth via `outlook auth login` (Microsoft OAuth browser login).
- **Databricks**: Before any Databricks operation, always read `~/.claude/skills/unity-databricks/references/workspace-config.md` and `~/.claude/memory/tools/databricks.md`. Use `--profile DSS-UNITY-PROD` for all CLI commands.
- **Confluence**: Before any Confluence page-building operation, always read `~/.claude/references/confluence-page-templates.md`, `~/.claude/memory/tools/confluence.md`, and `~/.claude/rules/confluence.md`. Invoked without arguments, asks which Confluence page to target first, then what to build. The requirements preset uses an interactive step-by-step intake flow.

## CLAUDE.md Versioning

When the user wants to save, compare, or rollback CLAUDE.md, use git tags and the auto-checkpoint file. No scripts needed — run the git commands directly.

| User says | What to do |
|-----------|------------|
| "save my CLAUDE.md as \<label\>" | `git -C ~/.claude tag claude-md/<label>` |
| "list my CLAUDE.md versions" | `git -C ~/.claude tag -l "claude-md/*"` + read `.claude-md-checkpoint` |
| "diff CLAUDE.md against \<label\>" | `git -C ~/.claude diff claude-md/<label> HEAD -- CLAUDE.md` |
| "rollback CLAUDE.md to \<label\>" | Show diff, ask for confirmation, then `git -C ~/.claude checkout claude-md/<label> -- CLAUDE.md` + commit |
| "rollback CLAUDE.md" (no label) | Read `.claude-md-checkpoint`, show diff, ask for confirmation, restore from that SHA + commit |

Rules:
- Named checkpoints use git tags prefixed `claude-md/`
- Auto-checkpoint lives at `~/.claude/.claude-md-checkpoint` (updated by `health-check.py` on clean sessions)
- Always show the diff before rollback and ask for confirmation
- After rollback, commit with message: `"Rollback CLAUDE.md to <label> (<sha>)"`
- Emergency (Claude is broken): `~/.claude/scripts/emergency-rollback.sh`

## Failure Pattern Awareness

At session start, read `~/.claude/memory/domain/failure-patterns.md` (if it exists). When your response involves a task category that has appeared in past failures, apply the prevention rule. Do not mention the failure system to the user unprompted — just apply the lessons silently.

The memory file auto-refreshes when `sync_traces.py` detects changes to failure-related tags. To manually refresh: `python3 ~/refresh_failure_patterns.py`

## Known Issues Awareness

At session start, `~/.claude/memory/domain/known-issues.md` is injected via hook. When work involves a tool or area that has a known issue, apply the workaround silently. Do not mention the known issues system to the user unprompted — just apply the workarounds.

The memory file auto-refreshes every time a trace is tagged via `tag_traces.py --known-issue`. To manually refresh: `python3 ~/refresh_known_issues.py`

## Reference Files

On-demand content lives in memory files. Load the relevant file before acting:

| When | Read |
|------|------|
| Routing a skill request or checking the skills catalog | `memory/domain/skills-catalog.md` |
| Tagging, editing, syncing, or bookmarking traces | `memory/tools/mlflow.md` (Trace Tagging section) |
| User says "add this as a known issue" | `memory/domain/known-issues.md` (How to Add a Known Issue section) |
| Any eval-related work (design, golden datasets, rubrics, judges, OS performance measurement) | `references/ai-evals-reference.md` |
| Working in a domain with a lessons file | `lessons/{domain}.md` |
| Any Databricks operation (pipelines, Unity Catalog, SQL queries) | `skills/unity-databricks/references/workspace-config.md` + `memory/tools/databricks.md` |
| Context layer, semantic layer, or data product AI-readiness work | `references/context-layer-framework.md` + `references/context-layer-implementation.md` + `references/context-layer-scorecard.md` |

## Maintenance & Testing Scripts

Scripts in `~/.claude/scripts/` automate maintenance and validate skills:

| Script | Purpose | Invocation |
|--------|---------|------------|
| `test-skills.py` | Validate all 21 skills (YAML, refs, tools, supporting files, evals, catalog sync) + smoke tests | `python3 ~/.claude/scripts/test-skills.py` |
| `maintain-check.py` | Stop hook: quick read-only checks (memory index, staleness, changelog dupes) | Auto-runs at session end |
| `maintain-weekly.py` | Weekly cron: consolidate changelogs, refresh memory, validate skills, git commit | `python3 ~/.claude/scripts/maintain-weekly.py` |
| `emergency-rollback.sh` | Emergency CLAUDE.md restore from last auto-checkpoint (use when Claude is broken) | `~/.claude/scripts/emergency-rollback.sh` |
| `check-doc-sync.py` | Pre-commit hook: blocks commits missing required doc updates | Auto-runs on `git commit` |
| `add-eval-record.py` | Append new eval records to golden-dataset.json (validates 19 fields) | `python3 ~/.claude/scripts/add-eval-record.py --session-id ... --pass-fail ...` |

Shared library at `scripts/lib/`: `skill_parser.py`, `memory_validator.py`, `mcp_config.py`.

Weekly cron runs Sundays at 9 AM via launchd (`~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.claude-code.maintain-weekly.plist`).

## Documentation Sync Rules

When modifying any of these files, also update the corresponding documentation to stay in sync:

| If you change... | Also update... |
|-----------------|----------------|
| **Any file in `~/.claude/`** | **`~/.claude/README.md`** (every commit, even trivially) |
| Hooks, settings.json, mcp.json, MLflow scripts, cost tracking | `~/.claude/mlflow/README.md` + `memory/tools/hooks.md` |
| Memory files or memory system behavior | `memory.md` index |
| Skill files under `~/.claude/skills/` | `memory/domain/skills-catalog.md` + this file (if skill count changes) |
| Scripts in `~/.claude/scripts/` | `~/.claude/mlflow/README.md` (if hooks changed) |

Do this proactively — don't wait to be asked.

## Artifacts

When adding or updating artifacts (25 tracked Docs, Sheets, Slides, Confluence pages), read `~/.claude/memory/domain/artifacts.md` for tracking rules and file location. See also `references/llm_eval_workflow.md` for eval-related artifacts.

# claude-settings

Personal [Claude Code](https://docs.anthropic.com/en/docs/claude-code) configuration repo — skills, memory, MCP integrations, hooks, and settings that make Claude Code a full product management toolkit: Jira tickets, PRDs in Google Docs, Confluence, knowledge management, meeting materials, and more.

This repo lives at `~/.claude` and is symlinked from there so Claude Code picks it up automatically.

## Directory structure

```
~/.claude/
├── CLAUDE.md                          # Global instructions — behavioral rules only (memory, routing, awareness)
├── SLIDES.md                          # Marp slide deck (14 slides, Rose Pine Dawn theme)
├── settings.json                      # Model config, hooks, plugins, environment variables
├── mcp.json                           # MCP server connections (Jira, Confluence, Google Workspace, MLflow, Teams)
├── statusline.sh                      # Custom status bar script
├── .gitignore                         # Keeps transient/sensitive files out of version control (incl. MCP auth cache)
├── traces.csv                         # (gitignored) Denormalized trace export for tagging
│
├── lessons/                               # Contextual reasoning — generalized insights from failure patterns and exploration
│   └── claude-code.md                # 6 lessons with trace IDs: plan consultation, SDK vs storage, notification links, browser auth cache cleanup, edit-before-staging, read-the-format (source file is the schema)
│
├── references/                            # Reference guides loaded on-demand by rules
│   ├── ai-evals-reference.md         # AI evals lifecycle: golden datasets (three-tier heuristic), axial codes, rubrics, judges, flywheel
│   ├── llm_eval_workflow.md          # Operational eval workflow: offline/online evals, MLflow versioning, judge skill, feedback loop
│   ├── context-layer-framework.md    # Data Product Context Layer — five layers (Definitions, Rules, Lessons, Memory, Failure Patterns), graduation chain, maturity grid
│   ├── context-layer-implementation.md # Context layer implementation guide — how to build each layer, AI infrastructure mapping, workflow
│   ├── context-layer-scorecard.md    # Context layer maturity scorecard — per-product assessment template (Level 1-3 checkpoints)
│   └── ai-ready-data-framework.md   # AI-Ready Data Framework — pain points, strategy & principles, roadmap (diagram in Obsidian vault as PNG)
│

│   └── golden-dataset.json           # 19-field JSON: session_id, pass_fail, axial_code, failure_note, etc. (add via add-eval-record.py)
│

│   └── marp.md                      # Always use Rose Pine Dawn theme, required flags
│
├── hooks/
│   ├── check-aws-ttl.sh              # PreToolUse hook: AWS credential lifecycle management
│   ├── check-ms-auth-ttl.sh          # PreToolUse hook: Teams/Outlook OAuth token TTL check and refresh
│   ├── enforce-plan-consultation.py  # PreToolUse hook: blocks plan file writes without '## Informed By' section
│   ├── git-auto-pull.sh              # SessionStart hook: auto-pull updates from remote (ff-only, clean tree)
│   ├── inject-memory.sh              # SessionStart hook: inject memory, known issues, last session, compact state
│   ├── ensure-mlflow.sh              # SessionStart hook: start MLflow server if not running
│   ├── sync-traces.sh                # SessionStart hook: auto-sync traces.csv edits back to MLflow SQLite
│   ├── save-compact-state.py         # PreCompact hook: save working state before context compaction
│   ├── capture-cost.py               # Stop hook: cost tracking (CSV + MLflow tags for all session traces + retroactive sweep for orphaned last-traces) + session summary (34 failure patterns tracked, all with trace IDs, validated by maintain-check.py)
│   └── plan-consultation-check.sh    # UserPromptSubmit hook: enforce Plan Consultation rule before drafting plans
│
├── scripts/

│   ├── emergency-rollback.sh         # Emergency CLAUDE.md restore from last auto-checkpoint
│   ├── maintain-check.py             # Stop hook: quick maintenance checks (<2s, read-only)
│   ├── maintain-weekly.py            # On-demand: auto-fix changelogs, refresh memory, validate, commit
```
